# DRAGONLANCE: THE KNIGHT'S OATH

## A Choose Your Own Adventure Prelude
### Book I of the Shadow of the Dragon Queen Solo Campaign | Version 19

You are a young squire standing at the gates of the Solamnic Orders. Fighter or Paladin — the choice is yours. Train. Fight. Choose. At the adventure's end one Order will claim your oath — Rose, Sword, or Crown — and you will ride to Vogler as their squire.

**Levels 1-3 | ~35-40 Hours Solo Play | Version 19 | 110+ Scenes | 3 Possible Orders**
**Fighter OR Paladin | 5 Combat Encounters | 8 Romance Arcs**
**Paladin: 4 Divine Quest Scenes | 5 Gods | Chosen or Choosing**

---


# HOW TO PLAY THIS BOOK

## Welcome, Squire

This is a solo Choose Your Own Adventure set in Krynn during the opening days of the War of the Lance. You play a human Solamnic squire. Your first decision — made at Scene 0 before the story begins — is whether you are a Fighter or a Paladin.

Both paths share the same story, companions, romance arcs, Order choices, and combat encounters. Paladins additionally experience four special divine quest scenes woven throughout the adventure, where the old gods — silent for three hundred years — begin to stir.

| Element | How It Works |
|---------|-------------|
| Scenes | Numbered scenes tell the story. Read fully before choosing. |
| Choices | Blue boxes = standard choices with Order point awards. |
| Paladin Scenes | Gold-bordered scenes are Paladin only. Fighters skip to the next scene number. |
| Order Points | Track ROSE, SWORD, and CROWN points on the tally at back. |
| God Signs | Paladins track divine signs separately — one tally per god. Most tallies = your deity. |
| Roll Boxes | Green = required roll. Amber = optional. Roll d20, meet or beat the DC to succeed. |
| Combat | Orange boxes are fights. Use the provided stat blocks. |
| Companions | Green banners = NPC joins. Red banners = NPC departs. |
| Level Ups | Navy boxes mark level gains. Update your character sheet before continuing. |
| No Dice? | Flip a coin for any roll: Heads = success, Tails = failure. |
| Death | 0 HP in combat: turn to that fight's Fallen entry. |
| Conviction Tracks | Some companions challenge your beliefs. Track the consequences on the score sheet. |
| Time | The ~35-40 hour estimate is a suggestion, not a target. Read slowly. Sit with a scene. Re-read a choice. This is your story — take the time it deserves. |

## The Three Orders

### ORDER OF THE ROSE
Justice. Wisdom. Scholars and judges first, warriors second. Earn ROSE by choosing mercy, applying the Measure thoughtfully, protecting the innocent.

### ORDER OF THE SWORD
Courage. Valour. Warriors sworn to the gods of good. Earn SWORD by choosing courage over caution, fighting bravely, refusing to flee.

### ORDER OF THE CROWN
Law. Order. Duty above self. Earn CROWN by following lawful orders, maintaining discipline, fulfilling duty even at personal cost.

## USING YOUR OWN CHARACTER SHEET (CPC)

This prelude works with the Native PC sheet on the next page or your own Created Player Character (CPC). If you are using a CPC: • CPC must be a Level 1 Fighter or Paladin with STR 14+ and CHA 12+. • Wherever native PC stats appear (AC 16, HP 12/10, +5 attack), use your own values. • ADD TO INVENTORY boxes: add the listed item to whichever sheet you are using. • MARK ON YOUR CHARACTER SHEET boxes: permanent change — update your CPC sheet now. • TRACK YOUR HP boxes appear after every combat — update before continuing. • LEVEL UP boxes include both native PC values and CPC-specific instructions. • The native PC stat block is Fighter STR 16, DEX 12, CON 14, INT 10, WIS 12, CHA 14. Paladin: STR 16, DEX 10, CON 13, INT 8, WIS 12, CHA 14.

---


# BEFORE THE STORY BEGINS — CHOOSE YOUR PATH

Before Scene 1, make one choice: are you a Fighter or a Paladin? This shapes how magic, combat, and the divine work in your story. It does not determine your Order — both classes can reach Rose, Sword, or Crown.

## Starting Equipment

| Item | Notes | Carried |
|------|-------|---------|
| Longsword | 1d8+3 slashing, versatile (1d10) | ■ |
| Chain Mail Armour | AC 16, no DEX bonus, disadvantage on Stealth | ■ |
| Shield | +2 AC when equipped (optional — remove if two-handing) | ■ |
| Dagger | 1d4+3, finesse, thrown (20/60 ft.) | ■ |
| Explorer's Pack | Bedroll, tinderbox, 10 torches, 10 days rations, waterskin, 50 ft. rope | ■ |
| Solamnic Tabard | Grants recognition as a Solamnic squire. Social effect. | ■ |
| Mira's Travel Bundle | Yarrow, bandages, salve. (Acquired Scene 21 if Mira joins) | △ |
| Baaz Stone Fragment | Trinket. Earned in first combat. No mechanical effect. | △ |
| Patrol Sketch | Intelligence item. +1 Scene 52 if shown to Caeron. | △ |
| Aldous's Compass | Trinket. Points 12° west of north. Bring to main campaign. | △ |

□ = starting equipment. △ = conditionally acquired during play. CPC users: your starting equipment may differ — use this as a reference guide.

## Gold (Steel Pieces)

> **Starting Gold: 2 stl**
> Dragonlance uses steel pieces (stl) as currency. Track your gold on your character sheet. You earn wages each Act and may find loot on quests. Shops are available at Brightholm and on the road.
>
> | Source | Amount | When |
> |--------|--------|------|
> | Starting funds | 2 stl | Character creation |
> | Squire's stipend | 5 stl | Scene 11 (formation) |
> | Field exercise pay | 10 stl | Scene 26_PREP (departure) |
> | March pay | 5 stl | Scene 62 (road to Vogler) |
> | Combat loot | Variable | After combat (optional, moral choice) |
> | NPC gratitude | Variable | After rescuing NPCs (Persuasion roll) |
> | **Maximum honest total** | **22 stl + gratitude** | |

## FIGHTER

Level 1: HP 12. Fighting Style feat (choose one: Dueling, Great Weapon Fighting, or Protection). Second Wind (bonus action, heal 1d10 + Fighter level HP, 2 uses per long rest, regain 1 use on short rest). Weapon Mastery (3 weapons — choose from your proficient weapons. You can swap masteries after a long rest).

Level 2: Action Surge (one additional Action on your turn, except the Magic action, 1/short or long rest). Tactical Mind (when you fail an ability check, expend a Second Wind use to add 1d10 to the roll; if you still fail, the use is not expended). Fighter Subclass (Champion, Battle Master, or Eldritch Knight).

Level 3: Full subclass features active.
- **Champion:** Improved Critical — your weapon attacks score a critical hit on a natural 19 or 20 (double weapon damage dice). Remarkable Athlete — advantage on Initiative rolls and STR (Athletics) checks. After scoring a critical hit, move up to half your Speed without provoking opportunity attacks.
- **Battle Master:** Superiority Dice (4d8, regain all on short or long rest). Learn 3 manoeuvres: Riposte, Precision Attack, Trip Attack. One manoeuvre per attack.
- **Eldritch Knight:** Spellcasting (2 cantrips, 3 prepared 1st-level spells from any Wizard school, 2 spell slots). War Bond (bond with 1 weapon, cannot be disarmed of it, can summon it as a bonus action).

Stats: STR 16 (+3), DEX 12 (+1), CON 14 (+2), INT 10, WIS 12 (+1), CHA 10. HP 12. AC 16. Prof +2.

Attack: Longsword +5, 1d8+3 (Mastery: Sap). Dagger +5, 1d4+3 (Mastery: Nick).

> **Weapon Mastery Properties (Fighter picks 3):**
> **Cleave** (greataxe, halberd): On hit, deal STR mod damage to a second adjacent creature.
> **Graze** (greatsword, glaive): On miss, deal STR mod damage to the target anyway.
> **Nick** (dagger, scimitar): Make an extra attack with a Light weapon as part of your Attack action (no ability mod to damage).
> **Push** (greatclub, pike): On hit, push Large or smaller creature 10ft away.
> **Sap** (longsword, mace): On hit, target has disadvantage on its next attack roll.
> **Slow** (longbow, whip): On hit, target's Speed reduced by 10ft until start of your next turn.
> **Topple** (battleaxe, lance): On hit, target makes CON save (DC = 8 + Prof + STR mod) or is knocked prone.
> **Vex** (handaxe, shortsword): On hit, gain advantage on your next attack against that target.

Story: Pure martial path. No divine scenes. Your strength is discipline and steel. The gods are absent — and you make do without them.

## PALADIN

Level 1: HP 11. Lay on Hands (bonus action, 5 HP pool per Paladin level / long rest. Touch to heal HP from pool, or expend 5 HP from pool to cure Poisoned condition). Spellcasting (CHA-based, 2 spell slots, prepare Paladin level + CHA mod spells from: Bless, Command, Cure Wounds, Detect Evil and Good, Divine Favour, Divine Smite, Heroism, Protection from Evil and Good, Searing Smite, Shield of Faith, Thunderous Smite, Wrathful Smite). Divine Smite is always prepared and does not count against your prepared spells. Weapon Mastery (2 weapons).

Level 2: Fighting Style feat (choose one: Dueling, Defence, Great Weapon Fighting, or Blessed Warrior — 2 Cleric cantrips). Paladin's Smite (cast Divine Smite once per long rest without expending a spell slot).

Level 3: Sacred Oath (Devotion, Ancients, Vengeance, or Glory). Channel Divinity (2 uses per long rest, regain 1 on short rest). Channel Divinity options include Divine Sense (bonus action, detect Celestials/Fiends/Undead within 60ft for 10 minutes). 1st-level spell slots increase to 3.

> **Divine Smite (1st-level Evocation spell):**
> Cast as a bonus action immediately after hitting a creature with a melee weapon or unarmed strike. Deals 2d8 Radiant damage (+1d8 vs Fiends or Undead). Upcast: +1d8 per slot level above 1st. **Once per turn.** Cannot benefit from critical hits (it is a separate spell, not part of the weapon attack).

Stats: STR 16 (+3), DEX 10, CON 13 (+1), INT 10, WIS 14 (+2), CHA 14 (+2). HP 11. AC 16. Prof +2.

Attack: Longsword +5, 1d8+3 (Mastery: Sap). Divine Smite: bonus action spell after hit, 2d8 radiant (once per turn).

Story: Four additional divine quest scenes (gold bordered). You are drawn toward an old god — or one is drawn toward you. Track God Signs throughout. At the end you choose, or are chosen.

## Paladin: The Five Old Gods of Krynn

The gods have been silent for 300 years since the Cataclysm. Most people have stopped worshipping entirely. But in this adventure, if you are a Paladin, you will begin to feel something. A presence. A pull. Five gods of good may reach for you:

**PALADINE (Platinum Dragon)** — God of good and law. Patron of rulers and guardians. His sign is silver light and the feeling of being watched by something immense and patient.

**KIRI-JOLITH (Bison of Heaven)** — God of just war and honour. Patron of soldiers and knights. His sign is the smell of blood and steel before a fight, and a voice like a battlefield command.

**MISHAKAL (Blue Lady)** — Goddess of healing and compassion. Patron of healers and the lost. Her sign is warmth in cold hands and the sound of someone weeping who then stops.

**HABBAKUK (Fisher King)** — God of nature and the sea. Patron of rangers and those who protect. His sign is the behaviour of animals — they approach you, or flee from what is near you.

**BRANCHALA (Song of Life)** — God of beauty, art, and inspiration. Patron of bards and those who find hope in darkness. His sign is music heard in silence and the unreasonable certainty that things will be all right.

Paladin players: Use the God Sign tracker on the score sheet at the back. Each Paladin Scene asks you to notice something — which god's sign it matches is up to you. Mark one tally under that god each time. The god with the most tallies by Scene P4 is the one who has been reaching for you. But the final choice — Scene P4 — is always yours.

> **F) I am a FIGHTER.** Record your stats and Fighting Style, then proceed to Scene 1. --> Scene 1

> **P) I am a PALADIN.** Record your stats and note your Lay on Hands pool, then proceed to Scene 1. You will encounter gold-bordered Paladin Scenes throughout the adventure. Do not skip them. --> Scene 1

---

## COMBAT REFERENCE

> **CRITICAL HITS**
> A natural 20 on a weapon attack roll is a critical hit. Double the **weapon damage dice only** (not modifiers, not extra dice from spells or features).
> *Example: Longsword crit = 2d8+3. Sneak Attack, Divine Smite, and similar extra dice are NOT doubled.*
> **Fighter (Champion):** Your critical hit range is 19–20. A natural 19 or 20 is a critical hit. After critting, move up to half your Speed without provoking opportunity attacks (Remarkable Athlete).
> **Spell attacks cannot score critical hits** — only weapon and unarmed attacks can crit.
>
> **CRITICAL FAILURES**
> A natural 1 on an attack roll always misses, regardless of bonuses.
>
> **DIVINE SMITE (2024 Rules)**
> Divine Smite is a **spell** (1st-level Evocation). Cast as a **bonus action** immediately after hitting with a melee weapon or unarmed strike. 2d8 Radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). **Once per turn.** Uses 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest via Paladin's Smite at level 2). Cannot benefit from crits.
>
> **WEAPON MASTERY**
> Fighters (3 weapons) and Paladins (2 weapons) have Weapon Mastery. When you hit with a mastered weapon, you may apply its Mastery property (Sap, Vex, Topple, etc.). See your class section for the full list.
>
> **ATTACK ROLLS**
> Roll 1d20 + attack bonus. Meet or beat the target's AC = hit. Roll damage on hit.
>
> **DEFENSE ROLLS**
> Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier. Meet or beat the DC = avoid damage. DC is typically enemy attack bonus + 10.
>
> **ADVANTAGE / DISADVANTAGE**
> Advantage: roll 2d20, take the higher. Disadvantage: roll 2d20, take the lower.
>
> **SECOND WIND (Fighter)**
> Bonus action. Heal 1d10 + Fighter level. 2 uses per long rest, regain 1 use on short rest.
>
> **TACTICAL MIND (Fighter, Level 2+)**
> When you fail an ability check, expend a Second Wind use to add 1d10. If you still fail, the use is not expended.
>
> **RATIONS & HUNGER**
> You start with 10 days of rations (Explorer's Pack). At each long rest on the road, you must consume 1 ration. Rations can be purchased at shops (3 days for 1 stl). Garrison meals at Brightholm do not cost personal rations.
>
> **Missing meals — escalating penalties:**
> | Meals Missed | Condition | Effect |
> |---|---|---|
> | 1 | Hungry | -1 to next ability check (not attack rolls) |
> | 2 | Weakened | -1 to all ability checks AND attack rolls until fed |
> | 3 | Exhausted | Disadvantage on all ability checks and attack rolls until fed. Speed reduced by 5ft. |
> | 4+ | Starving | Exhausted penalties + lose 1d4 HP per rest. Cannot benefit from short rests. |
>
> Eating a ration clears all hunger penalties immediately. The counter resets to 0.
>
> **Companion coverage:** If you run out of rations, a companion may offer to share — but only once per companion. They will comment on it. If no companion has rations to spare, you go hungry.
>
> **LOOTING THE DEAD — MORAL CONSEQUENCES**
>
> **Enemy combatants:** Searching enemy dead is not forbidden by the Measure, but it is not honoured. -1 ROSE or -1 CROWN (whichever is lower). Companions with ROSE affinity (Mira, Thessaly) express disapproval. Aldric looks away. Caeron notes it if present.
>
> **Enemy stashes and supply caches:** No moral penalty. Legitimate intelligence-gathering and seizure of enemy materiel.
>
> **Fallen allies and non-combatants:** Searching the bodies of dead civilians, refugees, allies, or fellow Solamnic soldiers is a violation of the Measure and the Oath. The dead are not yours to profit from.
> | Offence | Penalty | Companion Reaction |
> |---|---|---|
> | Search a fallen ally/civilian (first time) | -2 ROSE, -2 CROWN | Aldric confronts you. Mira turns away. Caeron's silence is worse than words. **Warning:** 'This is not who we are.' |
> | Search a fallen ally/civilian (second time) | -3 ROSE, -3 CROWN, -1 SWORD | Aldric refuses to speak to you for 2 scenes. Thessaly writes it down — not for her article, for the record. Caeron calls you aside: 'Squire. I am going to say this once. The Measure exists because the alternative is men picking through the dead for coin. That is what bandits do. You are not a bandit. Stop behaving like one.' |
> | Search a fallen ally/civilian (third time) | -3 ROSE, -3 CROWN, -2 SWORD. **CORRUPTION: QUESTIONING on one active corruption track** (player's choice). | The column knows. They have seen you do it three times now. No one says anything. The silence of people who have revised their opinion of you is different from other silences. Aldric: 'I defended you the first time. I cannot do it again.' |
> | Stealing from living refugees/allies | -3 ROSE, -3 CROWN, -2 SWORD. **CORRUPTION: SHAKEN on one active corruption track.** | Caeron courts-martial you on the spot. You are stripped of command responsibility. Companions lose 1 romance stage (Flame → Spark, Spark → None). Mira leaves the party if present. 'I did not walk this road to watch a knight rob the people he swore to protect.' |
>
> **What counts as a non-combatant body?**
> The dead merchant's guard in Scene 28_CARAVAN. Fallen refugees on the road. Dead Solamnic soldiers found at abandoned outposts. Any body that was not trying to kill you when it died. *If in doubt: the Measure says leave it. The Measure is not always convenient. That is the point.*

---


# YOUR POSSIBLE COMPANIONS & LOVE INTERESTS

Eight potential love interests appear across this adventure — six who strengthen your path, two whose ideas may corrode it. Romance stages: Spark, Flame, Oath. Reaching Oath unlocks an epilogue scene connecting to the main campaign. All romances are optional and available to both Fighter and Paladin.

## SER ALDRIC VOSS (he/him) — Human, Knight-Squire, Senior Trainee

**Appearance:** Tall, sandy-haired, jaw like a cliff. Battered helmet. A scar through his left eyebrow he claims came from a bar fight. It did not.

**Personality:** Competitive, honourable, hides feelings behind banter. Deeply loyal.

**First Met:** Scene 3 — challenges you to a sparring match.

**Romance Arc:** Slow burn. Rivals to respect to something more. Spark Scene 12 or 15. Flame Scene 28. Oath Scene 67 if trust score 3+.

**Condition:** Romance closes if you betray his confidence in Scene 31.

## THESSALY BRIGHTWATER (she/her) — Half-Elf, War Correspondent

**Appearance:** Sharp eyes, copper hair, ink-stained fingers. Silver locket she never opens.

**Personality:** Witty, curious, emotionally guarded. Tests everyone.

**First Met:** Scene 6 — asks you a question you did not expect.

**Romance Arc:** Flirtatious then complicated in Act 3. Spark Scene 6. Flame Scene 34. Oath Scene 71.

**Condition:** Romance closes if you lie to her twice.

## COMMANDER SERATH (they/them) — Human, Dragon Army Defector

**Appearance:** Military posture in civilian clothes. Quiet eyes that miss nothing.

**Personality:** Careful, precise, carrying enormous guilt. Dry humour that surprises people.

**First Met:** Scene 18 — found wounded in an abandoned barn.

**Romance Arc:** Dark and complicated. Spark Scene 18. Flame Scene 42. Oath Scene 74.

**Condition:** Romance closes if you turn them in.

## MIRA OF THE OAKS (she/her) — Human, Healer-Herbalist, Refugee

**Appearance:** Brown skin, warm dark eyes, flour on her sleeves in a war zone.

**Personality:** Gentle but not soft. Will tell you when you are wrong, kindly but firmly.

**First Met:** Scene 9 — asks you to hold someone's hand while she works.

**Romance Arc:** Slow burn, emotionally rich. Spark Scene 9. Flame Scene 38. Oath Scene 69.

**Condition:** Romance closes if you abandon the refugee column in Scene 44.

## LORD CAERON ASHVALE (he/him) — Human Noble, Knight of the Crown

**Appearance:** Patrician features, dark hair silver at the temples. Immaculate armour always.

**Personality:** Arrogant surface, deeply insecure underneath.

**First Met:** Scene 5 — oversees your first evaluation.

**Romance Arc:** Complicated slow burn. Spark Scene 5 or 14. Flame Scene 48. Oath Scene 75.

**Condition:** Romance may reopen at Scene 55 after a Scene 31 falling-out if you apologise.

## SERA NIGHTHOLLOW (she/her) — Half-Elf, Scout-Rogue, Garrison Ranger

**Appearance:** Lean, dark-skinned, silver-streaked black hair cut blunt at the jaw. A scar across her collarbone she explains as a training accident — it was not. Moves like someone who learned early that being noticed is dangerous.

**Personality:** Dry, precise, deeply competent. Does not give trust easily. Has lost people. Laughs rarely but when she does it is sudden and completely unguarded, and she looks briefly startled by herself.

**First Met:** Scene 3B — She is watching the sparring yard from the armoury roof when you arrive.

**Romance Arc:** Slow then fast — distant for a long time, then one moment where everything changes. Spark Scene 3B. Flame Scene 34B. Oath Scene 68B.

**Condition:** Romance closes if you dismiss her advice twice in Act One.

## VAEL ASHMORE (she/her) — Human, Knight-Squire Candidate, Your Equal

**Appearance:** Brown skin, sharp jaw, close-cropped dark hair. Always in training gear. Callused hands. Wears her Solamnic signet ring on a cord around her neck rather than her finger — she is not sure she has earned it yet.

**Personality:** Competitive in the way that conceals deep respect. Holds herself to an impossible standard. Genuinely funny in a self-deprecating way she uses to deflect from how much she cares about everything.

**First Met:** Scene 5B — You are both waiting for your evaluation results.

**Romance Arc:** Built on mutual recognition. Spark Scene 5B. Flame Scene 32B. Oath Scene 68C.

**Condition:** Romance does not close through choices but through neglect — if you never pursue it, it fades.

## TARIEL DUSKMANTLE (she/her) — Human, Eastern Provinces Diplomatic Observer


**Appearance:** Dark hair worn in the eastern military braid, olive skin, a face that defaults to attentive neutrality the way a diplomat's does. Green eyes that catalogue. She dresses well but not ostentatiously — civilian riding clothes in dark colours, good boots, a single silver ring.

**Personality:** Intellectually precise, genuinely curious, disarming. She does not argue — she asks questions that reveal contradictions. She laughs easily and means it. Carries a moral framework that is internally consistent and externally terrifying once you trace where it leads.

**First Met:** Scene 31B — She arrives with the High Justice's escort as a diplomatic observer.

**Romance Arc:** Intellectual first, then personal. Spark Scene 31B. Flame Scene 53D. Oath Scene 66B_Tariel.


**Condition:** Romance closes if you refuse to engage with her at Scene 31B or if you never pursue romance choices.

## LYSANDER GRAVES (he/him) — Human, Knight of the Sword (Increasingly Disgraced)


**Appearance:** Dark-skinned, broad-shouldered, with the rangy build of a man who has spent more time on roads than in garrisons. Handsome in a way that looks like it used to be sharper — a scar bisects his lower lip and he keeps his hair longer than regulation. His armour is Solamnic issue, well-maintained but personalised: the Crown insignia has been half-filed, then stopped.

**Personality:** Charismatic in the specific way of someone who has stopped performing. Funny — genuinely, surprisingly funny. Underneath it: grief that has calcified into philosophy. He was a good knight. He still fights like one. He has simply stopped believing the institution deserves him.

**First Met:** Scene 27B — the night after the south road ambush. You find him at a waypoint cleaning draconian blood off a blade that is not regulation issue.

**Romance Arc:** Physical and philosophical. Spark Scene 27B. Flame Scene 36B or 53E. Oath Scene 66B_Lysander.


**Condition:** Romance closes if you report him to Caeron without speaking to him first, or if you never pursue romance choices.

**Note:** Lysander rides to Vogler on his own. He does not join the garrison column. He will be there when you arrive.

## Paladin Note — Divine Relationships

If you are a Paladin, your god relationship does not prevent romance. Each god views love differently: Paladine values bonds forged in service of good. Kiri-Jolith values those who fight beside you. Mishakal blesses those who are tender as well as strong. Habbakuk favours those who protect what they love. Branchala thinks love is one of the best arguments for continuing.

## Paladin Note — Conviction and the Divine

Some companions will challenge your beliefs deeply enough to shift them. This does NOT automatically trigger the DG (Dark God) track. Takhisis does not claim you through philosophical doubt — she claims you through compromise. However: if your convictions have been shaken by a companion's arguments, the DG track's temptations become harder to resist. If you are LISTENING or COMPROMISED on the DG track AND at SHAKEN or higher on a conviction track, all DG saving throws are made at Disadvantage.

## Conviction Track

Some companions carry ideas powerful enough to reshape your beliefs. The Conviction Track measures how deeply those ideas have taken root. It is separate from romance — you can be changed by someone's philosophy without loving them.

| State | Effect |
|-------|--------|
| STEADFAST | You have heard the argument and rejected it. No effect. |
| QUESTIONING | The argument landed. You carry doubt. No mechanical effect yet. |
| SHAKEN | The doubt has roots. -1 to your highest Order point tally. |
| CONVINCED | You believe they are right. Corruption modifier activates at reduced level. |
| FALLEN | Full internalisation. Full corruption modifier. You arrive at Vogler hollow. |

Romance can accelerate movement along the track but is never required. A PC who debates without any romantic interest and finds the arguments compelling can still reach FALLEN.


Castle Brightholm — schematic overview. Not to scale.

---

# ACT ONE: THE OATH OF BEGINNINGS (LEVEL 1)

## Act One Overview

You are a squire at Castle Brightholm. The Dragon Armies are a rumour. You have one week before your formal Trials begin. Scenes 1-27 establish your character, your relationships, and end in the first real combat. Paladins: Paladin Scene P1 is in Act One — watch for the gold border.

---


## SCENE 1 — A MORNING LIKE EVERY OTHER

*Castle Brightholm — Dawn*

The bell has not rung yet. You wake before it — always have, which is one of the small unglamorous disciplines that separate squires who want to be knights from squires who want to have been knights. The barracks smells of oiled leather and cold ash and the particular warmth of ten people sleeping in the same room in autumn. Aldric Voss sleeps across from you with his arms folded on his chest like a man who has already decided to be composed even in unconsciousness. Eight months here. Seven days until the Trials. Outside the window the sky is the purple-grey of pre-dawn that looks almost exactly like the moment before something begins.

| ORDER OF THE ROSE | ORDER OF THE SWORD | ORDER OF THE CROWN |
|---|---|---|
| Points: ___ | Points: ___ | Points: ___ |
| Justice & Wisdom | Courage & Battle | Law & Duty |

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 10
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 10+):** Something is off this morning — the south-facing guards are doubled and there are fresh horses in the yard that were not there yesterday. New orders arrived overnight. You know before anyone tells you.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-9):** The morning is ordinary. Nothing unusual is visible.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

Seven days. That is how many mornings remain before the formal Trials. You have been counting them differently lately — not as days remaining but as last-times. Last Tuesday at early formation. Last Wednesday in the chapel library with Aldous. This morning has the particular quality of the last first-morning-of-the-week before the thing that changes things. You get up before the bell anyway. You always do.

> **A) Go to the courtyard and practise sword forms in the dark.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 3
>
> **B) Open the Measure and study the passage on Justice.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 4
>
> **C) Read the letter from home again.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 2
>
> **D) Wake Aldric. You want to spar before the day starts.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 3

---


## SCENE 2 — THE LETTER

*Castle Brightholm — Barracks*

You have read it four times. The harvest fair, your father's knee worse in the cold, your sister grown two inches. That she is proud. That she is afraid. She does not say afraid of what. She does not need to. Your mother's handwriting slopes slightly left, which it always has. At the bottom, in different ink — she sealed it, then reopened it: 'Come home safe. Be good. Be the kind of knight they write songs about, not the kind they write tragedies about. I love you.' The second ink is darker. She wrote the rest of the letter first and then could not send it without saying the true thing.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** Reading between the lines: she knows something specific, not just general fear. Someone has been through your village recently. Someone official, heading south. This letter was written the day after they left.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** The worry in the letter is real but unreadable. You fold it and carry it.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Place it in your breast pocket. Then go train.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 3
>
> **B) Set it down. Go practise. Sentiment waits.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 3
>
> **C) Write back immediately, while the feeling is fresh.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 3

---


## SCENE 3 — ALDRIC IN THE COURTYARD

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard, Dawn*

He is already there, which is not surprising. Aldric Voss does not oversleep. He runs sword forms in the grey pre-dawn with the absorbed focus of someone not thinking about anything else — which is precisely what being very good at something looks like. He finishes his combination before he stops, because Aldric Voss does not interrupt things that should be finished. Then a slight smile that is not quite a smile. A nod toward the practice sword on the rack.

Aldric Voss is tall and fair, with the kind of face that defaults to a neutrality so complete it reads as severity until you learn to look for the small tells — the slight relaxation around the eyes when something amuses him, the almost imperceptible tightening when something doesn't. He has the build of someone who has been training since he could hold a sword and the posture of someone who has never been entirely at ease anywhere except in motion.

> **COMPANION JOINS: ALDRIC VOSS**
> Knight-squire, rival, possible love interest. Joins as sparring partner from this scene.
> Role: Combat ally: +1 to your attack rolls when fighting side by side.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (+1) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** You spot a gap in his left-side footwork. Carry into Scene 12: spar check at Advantage.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** His form is tight this morning. Scene 12 is a fair fight.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

The yard smells of wet stone and the specific iron tang of weapons that have been out since before dawn. Eight months ago you would have hesitated before picking up the practice sword. You pick it up without thinking, which tells you something. Aldric settles into his guard and tilts his head slightly — the same adjustment every time, left side, the tell you found in the second month and have never mentioned. You found it by watching. He knows you found it. He uses it anyway, which is either trust or a counter-trap. You have not yet decided which.

> **A) Take the sword and spar.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 12
>
> **B) Watch him first. Point out the gap.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 4
>
> **C) Challenge him to a running race.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 6
>
> **D) Tell him honestly you could not sleep. Ask if he is nervous.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK) --> Scene 7

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — SERA NIGHTHOLLOW**
> Before the spar: there is someone on the armoury roof. If you want to meet her, turn to Scene 3B (The Armoury Roof) now. Scene 3B is her first appearance — no prior relationship needed. 3B leads directly to Scene 12 (the spar).

---


## SCENE 3B — THE ARMOURY ROOF

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard, Dawn*

She is sitting on the armoury roof with her legs hanging over the edge and a whetstone working a long knife with the slow patience of someone who has been awake for a while. She watches you spar below — or watches Aldric, specifically, with the professional attention of someone cataloguing how he moves.

After a while she calls down without raising her voice: 'Your footwork has a gap on the left. He overcommits on the third combination. If you wait him out, he gives it to you.' Then she goes back to the whetstone. You have not been introduced. You do not know her name.

> **COMPANION JOINS: SERA NIGHTHOLLOW**
> Garrison scout-rogue. She sees things. She tells you when she feels like it. Possible love interest — the slow kind.
> Role: Scout intelligence: she knows the roads, the patrol patterns, and who is lying. If you listen to her, she keeps talking.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+2) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** She has been here for at least an hour — the whetstone marks on the roof edge show she worked on that knife before the sparring started. She was not watching Aldric. She was watching the approach to the courtyard. She is a scout, and she came here to observe something. Possibly you.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** She is sitting on the roof sharpening a knife. That is all you can read.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Call up: 'I know. I have been trying to get him to show it for three weeks.' She looks at you with new attention.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Sera possible) --> Scene 12
>
> **B) Ignore the advice. You do not know her.** (+0, Sera notes this) --> Scene 12
>
> **C) Ask her name. She considers. Then tells you.** (+1 ROSE, establishes contact) --> Scene 12

## SCENE 4 — THE MEASURE

*Castle Brightholm — Chapel Library*

The chapel library is cold and smells of old parchment and tallow and three centuries of people asking difficult questions in a small room. The candles are thin — the chapel gets last priority for supplies, which says something about how equipment maintenance ranks relative to justice. You find the passage: Est Sularus oth Mithas — My honour is my life. Three words. Commentaries running to thousands of pages. You are reading one of them when Ser Aldous sits down without being invited, sets his elbows on the table, looks at you, and says: 'Ask it.' You did not know there was a question visible on your face.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Religion or History (INT, proficiency if trained) (+0) | INT | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** You find the commentary passage that explains what Est Sularus actually meant when first written — not abstract honour, but a specific refusal of a corrupt command three centuries ago. The words have teeth. When Aldous asks his question you have the context to answer it well. +1 to your response in this scene.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** The passage is clear but the history behind it is opaque. You know the words. You do not yet fully know what they cost.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) 'What do you do when the law asks you to be cruel?'** (+2 ROSE, gains Aldous as mentor) --> Scene 5
>
> **B) 'Is the Measure still true if the world it was written for is gone?'** (+2 CROWN, gains Aldous as critic) --> Scene 8
>
> **C) 'I am not sure I am good enough for the Trials.'** (+1 ROSE, gains Aldous as supporter) --> Scene 10
>
> **D) Say nothing. Close the book. The chapel is cold and the courtyard is waiting.** (+1 SWORD, Aldous notes your silence) --> Scene 1_HUB

---


## SCENE 5 — THE FIRST EVALUATION

*Castle Brightholm — Assessment Hall*

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — VAEL ASHMORE**
> You are not the only squire waiting for Caeron's results. If you want to meet Vael Ashmore, turn to Scene 5B (The Same Dent) now. Scene 5B is her first appearance — she is in this same corridor. Read 5B instead of this scene. 5B leads to Scene 11.

Lord Caeron Ashvale conducts the morning evaluation with the economy of a man who has done this a hundred times and sees no reason to approach it differently on the hundred-and-first. He works through the squire line without warmth or hurry, marking his clipboard in the small precise hand you can identify from across a courtyard. When he reaches you, he takes your sword. He examines the blade — clean, sharp, well-maintained — and then he finds the pommel dent. He holds it at eye level and examines the dent with the expression of a man not looking at the dent but at the choice that left it there. His verdict: 'Satisfactory.' The word lands like a door being closed by someone very good at closing doors quietly.

Lord Caeron Ashvale is thirty, and already carries the compressed quality of a man who does not waste movement or word. Dark hair, pale eyes that take inventory before they settle. The armour shows years of use — bought before he could afford to replace it, maintained since out of something other than necessity.

> **COMPANION JOINS: LORD CAERON ASHVALE**
> Your evaluating officer. Cold, exacting, possible love interest.
> Role: Quest-giver for formal assignments. His approval unlocks Crown path bonuses.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (+1) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** This is a test of your reaction, not your sword. +1 to any Caeron Persuasion check this adventure.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** He is completely unreadable.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Meet his gaze and accept the verdict. Walk back through the corridor. The morning is not over yet.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 1_HUB
>
> **B) Apologise for the dent and ask for the correct protocol.** (+1 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 13
>
> **C) 'I can do better, my lord.'** (+1 SWORD, ROMANCE SPARK Caeron) --> Scene 14
>
> **D) Ask whether satisfactory is the highest mark given today.** (+1 ROSE, Caeron's eye sharpens) --> Scene 15

---


## SCENE 5B — THE SAME DENT

*Castle Brightholm — Assessment Hall Corridor*

You are both waiting outside the assessment hall for your individual results. The corridor is narrow. She is looking at the wall. You are looking at your sword. After a while she glances over, sees the pommel dent, and without any preamble holds up her own sword. The same dent. Same location. Same cause, probably.

'Caeron?' she says. You nod. 'He gave me satisfactory too.' A pause. 'I think satisfactory is actually his highest mark.' She says this with the slight bitterness of someone who has thought about it a lot and decided to find it funny instead of devastating.

> **COMPANION JOINS: VAEL ASHMORE**
> Knight-squire candidate, your equal in training. She has been here six months. She noticed you three weeks ago and did not say anything until now.
> Role: Mutual support: once per Act, you may ask Vael's read on a situation. She gives honest assessments, even when they are not what you want to hear.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** She has been here six months and knows exactly how long it takes Caeron to review each squire's assessment. She timed her appearance in this corridor. She has been looking for a reason to speak to you for longer than this morning. ROMANCE SPARK Vael at Advantage if you acknowledge this.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** She is waiting for her results. The timing seems coincidental.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) 'Satisfactory is the ceiling. I decided that this morning.' She looks at you. Recalibrates. You part ways in the corridor — the morning has more to give.** (+1 CROWN, ROMANCE SPARK Vael) --> Scene 1_HUB
>
> **B) 'I think you are right. Which is worse somehow.' She laughs — and you carry the sound of it back down the corridor.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Vael) --> Scene 1_HUB
>
> **C) 'We should compare notes on how to fix it.' Practical. She approves. You agree to meet later. For now, the morning waits.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN, strong start) --> Scene 1_HUB

## SCENE 6 — THE CORRESPONDENT

*Castle Brightholm — East Gate*

Thessaly Brightwater arrived three days ago with a press credential, a better map than the garrison has, and the easy confidence of someone who has been in considerably more dangerous places than this and made her peace with that some time ago. In three days she has interviewed the senior knights, both stable hands, the armourer, and apparently Zinnia Quickfingers, who gave excellent copy. She catches you at the east gate with her notebook open and her pen uncapped and the particular quality of attention that does not permit comfortable evasion. 'Tell me something true,' she says, 'about why you are here.' Not what you believe. Not what you want. Something true.

Thessaly Brightwater is half-elven, which shows mostly in the pointed ears and the quality of attention she gives things. Dark hair cut short and practical, ink on her fingers, a coat with too many pockets, all in use. She looks like someone for whom the road has become the natural state.

> **COMPANION JOINS: THESSALY BRIGHTWATER**
> War correspondent. She hears things. She will share them if she trusts you.
> Role: Intelligence and information network. +1 to Scene 23 and 56 if she trusts you.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** She has asked this question before — you can see it in how her pen is already positioned. She is not writing down the answer yet. She is waiting for something specific: the moment a person stops reciting and starts speaking. Answer honestly and she will mark the moment exactly.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** Her expression is professionally neutral. You cannot tell what she is looking for.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) 'Because I watched the south burn and I need to be able to do something.'** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK) --> Scene 16
>
> **B) 'Because my family has been Solamnic for six generations.'** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 17
>
> **C) 'Because the Measure might be the last thing standing between Ansalon and darkness.'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 16
>
> **D) 'I am not sure yet. Is that honest enough?'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN, ROMANCE SPARK) --> Scene 16

---


## SCENE 7 — AN HONEST MOMENT

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard*

You ask because the yard is empty and the day has not started yet and you have been wondering about this for eight months and you may not get another unguarded moment. He is quiet. Not the quiet of no answer — the quiet of deciding whether to give it. Then: 'Every morning.' He does not look at you. 'I just do not talk about it.' He keeps looking at the courtyard wall as if it is very interesting. This is the most honest thing he has said to you at six in the morning, which means it is probably the most honest thing he has said to anyone at six in the morning, including himself.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> There is a pause before he turns back to the sword forms. The quality of the silence is different now.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 10
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 10+):** He is not just saying what sounds right — he has been awake since before you. His sword forms are running faster than usual, burning off something. Aldric Voss is genuinely frightened of failing the Trials. ROMANCE SPARK Aldric at Advantage if you respond to the fear rather than the bravado.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-9):** He says it easily. You cannot tell if it is practiced or true.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

The day has not started yet. The bell will ring in eight minutes and then it will have started and this — whatever this is — will become part of the past. He is still looking at the wall. You let him. You understand that he gave you something just now that cost him something, in the way it always costs something when a person who is very good at being composed lets you see underneath it for a moment. You do not remark on it. That is also something.

> **A) Tell him you are nervous too.** (+1 ROSE, relationship warms) --> Scene 3
>
> **B) 'Then we will both pass anyway.'** (+1 SWORD, Aldric almost laughs) --> Scene 3

---


## SCENE 8 — SER ALDOUS ON JUSTICE

*Castle Brightholm — Chapel Library*

He is quiet long enough that you wonder if he will answer. Then: 'The Measure says the law exists to protect the innocent.' He sets his commentary text down. He is not reading from it. 'If the law stops doing that — if a decree comes down requiring you to act against an innocent — the Measure itself gives you the answer. Est Sularus oth Mithas. My honour is my life.' He looks at you with the steadiness of someone who arrived at this through experience rather than reading. 'Not your lord's honour. Not the Order's. Yours. You carry it. You are responsible for where it goes.'

Ser Aldous is seventy or near it, with white hair, a weathered face, and the unhurried physicality of someone who was once very strong and is still, in the ways that matter, exactly that. He wears the chaplain's robe over the frame of a man who spent forty years in armour before he took it off, and he gives the impression of someone who removed the armour but kept everything it stood for.

> **You Gain:**
> Ser Aldous as Mentor (+1 to ROSE checks in Act One). The Rose Commentary text — relevant in Scene 31.

> **FIGHTER — MEASURE SUBPLOT**
> Before your choice below, Fighters turn to Scene M1 (The Letter and the Spirit) now. It occurs this same morning. M1 leads back to Scene 9 after your choice there.

> **PALADIN — THE HEALER'S TENT**
> Before your choice below, Paladins may also visit the infirmary. Turn to Scene 9 (The Healer's Tent) now. It occurs this same morning — Aldous sends you. 'There is someone in the infirmary who could use a steady hand,' he says. 'Go. Come back when you have something to tell me about mercy.' Scene 9 leads back here for your choice.

> **A) Thank him and read the text immediately.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene M1 (Fighter) or Scene 9 (Paladin)
>
> **B) 'Have you ever had to make that choice yourself?'** (+2 ROSE, unlocks Aldous backstory) --> Scene M1 (Fighter) or Scene 9 (Paladin)

---


## SCENE 9 — THE HEALER'S TENT

*Castle Brightholm — Infirmary*

The infirmary smells of yarrow and clean linen and underneath both, the copper-salt note of pain being handled by someone who knows exactly what they are doing. Mira of the Oaks has not slept — you can see it in the particular stillness that develops past tiredness, when the body stops negotiating and runs on purpose. She does not look up when you come in. 'Sit with him.' She nods at the old man in the corner who is holding his own hands and staring at nothing with the look of someone who has been frightened long enough to have forgotten what unfrightened felt like. 'Hold his hand. Talk to him. He is frightened and I cannot be in two places at the same time.'

Mira of the Oaks is small and precise, with the steady hands of a healer and the look of someone who takes stock of a room before deciding how to be in it. Dark skin, dark eyes, hair pulled back in the functional style of someone who needs to see clearly and cannot have things in the way. She is younger than her competence suggests — mid-twenties, maybe — but the competence is entirely real.

> **COMPANION JOINS: MIRA OF THE OAKS**
> Healer and refugee. Will travel with you if you earn her trust.
> Role: Party healer: restores 1d6+2 HP to any companion once per scene.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Medicine (+1) | WIS | DC 10
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 10+):** You recall a calming technique. The old man steadies. Mira notices. +1 Mira romance track.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-9):** You do your best. No penalty — the kindness still counted.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **Paladin Note:**
> If you are a Paladin: you may use Lay on Hands (touch, costs 1 HP from your pool) to ease the old man's pain. This is the first time your power has worked so clearly. Mark 1 tally under MISHAKAL on your God Sign tracker.

> **A) Sit with the old man until Mira can take over.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Mira) --> Scene 21
>
> **B) Ask Mira how you can be most useful.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 21
>
> **C) Apologise — you have training — and leave. The corridor is cold after the warmth of the infirmary.** (-1 ROSE, no Mira spark) --> Scene 1_HUB
>
> **D) (If arrived from Scene 8 or Scene 1_HUB): Return to where you were. Carry what you learned here.** --> Scene 8 (if from 8) or Scene 1_HUB (if from 1_HUB)

---


## SCENE 10 — THE ADMISSION

*Castle Brightholm — Chapel Steps*

Aldous laughs. Not the polite laugh of someone managing you — a genuine one, warm and immediate, with the deep lines around his eyes that come from a lifetime of doing it. 'Every squire worth their salt feels that,' he says. 'The ones who do not are the ones I worry about.' He settles back in his chair with the unhurried quality of someone who is exactly where he intended to be this morning. 'The question,' he says, 'is not whether you feel it. The question is what you do with it. Which brings us to what you are actually afraid of.' He waits. He is good at waiting. You get the sense he has had this conversation a great many times and has learned that the silence does more work than the prompting.

He sets down the commentary text he was pretending to read and looks at you with the specific attention of someone who has been waiting for this particular conversation since the first week you arrived. 'You are the kind of squire who asks whether they are good enough,' he says. 'That is a more interesting question than the ones most of your cohort are asking. The ones asking it are rarely the ones I end up worried about.'

> **A) 'I am afraid I will do everything right and it will not be enough.'** (+2 SWORD) --> Scene 20
>
> **B) 'I am afraid I will make the wrong choice when it actually matters.'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 20
>
> **C) 'I am afraid I will not know the right choice until it is too late.'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 20

---


## SCENE 1_HUB — THE HOURS BEFORE

*Castle Brightholm — Pre-Dawn to Dawn*

> **GATE: Track activities completed. The formation bell does not ring until you have spent time in at least two of Brightholm's corners this morning.**

The sky has shifted since you woke — still dark, but the kind of dark that knows the light is coming. The castle moves around you in the small familiar sounds of a place about to begin its day. Boot-steps in the upper corridor. A door. The distant clatter of the kitchen grate being raked. You have time. Not much, but enough.

You stand in the corridor between the barracks and the courtyard and consider how to spend what remains of the morning. Seven days until the Trials. Each one a chance to learn something, or to miss something you will wish you had not.

> **A) (If not yet visited) The training yard is calling. Aldric will be there — he is always there.** --> Scene 3
>
> **B) (If not yet visited) The chapel library is quiet at this hour. The Measure waits.** --> Scene 4
>
> **C) (If not yet visited) The letter from home is still folded in your pocket. You have not read it yet today.** --> Scene 2
>
> **D) (If not yet visited) The infirmary. There is always someone who needs a steady hand.** --> Scene 9
>
> **E) (If 2+ activities completed) The bell rings. The morning you have been living in becomes the morning everyone else wakes up to. Time for formation.** --> Scene 11
