## SCENE 11 — THE DAY BEGINS

*Castle Brightholm — Main Courtyard, Dawn*

The bell rings at the same time it always does. Formation assembles in the main courtyard with the efficiency of people whose bodies have been doing this for eight months without consulting them. You find your place. Aldric finds his, three feet to your right, where he has been every morning for eight months.

**IF VAEL IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Vael is three positions to your left in formation. She does not look at you. She is looking at Caeron, with the same focused assessment you have seen her bring to her own sword dents — the attention of someone who is studying how a thing works so she can understand why it sometimes doesn't. After formation she catches your eye. A slight nod. Not casual. The nod of someone who has been paying attention and wants you to know it.

Lord Caeron reads out the day's assignments with the unhurried precision of a man who has already decided everything and is now informing you of the results. Field exercise. South road. Reported bandits. He reads out the pairs. Your name, then Aldric's. You feel Aldric absorb it without moving.

> **WAGES PAID — SQUIRE'S WEEKLY STIPEND**
> The garrison quartermaster distributes the weekly stipend after formation. Five steel pieces, pressed into your hand with the efficiency of a man who has done this eight hundred times. It is not much. It is yours.
> **Add 5 stl to your gold.**

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** History (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** You recall a garrison briefing from three weeks ago: there have been refugee reports on the south road for over a month, not just the past few days. Someone suppressed those earlier reports. The 'bandits' may have been there much longer than the official timeline suggests.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** You have no specific knowledge of the south road beyond what Caeron just said.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — DRAGONLANCE CAMEO**
> At the edge of the morning formation there is a young man you have not seen before — the Brightblade family crest on older armour. If you want to speak with him, turn to Scene 11B now. Return here after.

> **A) Head to the training yard. You and Aldric should spar before anything else.** --> Scene 12

---


## SCENE 11B — A FAMILIAR FACE IN THE COURTYARD

*Castle Brightholm — Main Courtyard*

> **DRAGONLANCE CAMEO — OPTIONAL SCENE**
> This scene is non-mandatory flavour. It introduces a canon character from the Dragonlance world who may reappear in the main campaign.

At the edge of the morning formation there is a young man you have not seen before. Not a garrison squire — his armour is older, a knight's kit that has been carefully maintained through years of use rather than stored and polished for ceremony. The Brightblade family crest. He stands in the formation anyway, because standing in formation is what you do, and he is clearly the kind of person who does what you do.

Ser Aldous speaks to him after formation. A brief exchange. The young man listens with the complete attention of someone who does not take instruction for granted. He nods once. He does not look as though things are going particularly well for him. He looks as though he intends to do the honourable thing regardless.

When formation breaks he catches your eye. A slight nod — not casual, formal. The greeting of one squire to another. His name is Sturm. He is passing through on his way south and needed a place to sleep. 'The Knighthood still stands,' he says, when you ask why he wears the armour when he could wear anything. 'Someone should act as though it does.'

> **Who Is Sturm Brightblade?**
> Sturm Brightblade is one of the Companions of the Lance — the heroes of the War of the Lance. At this point in the timeline he is a squire himself, working to prove himself worthy of the Knighthood his father abandoned. He takes the Oath of Measures more seriously than most knights. He will fight for anyone who cannot fight for themselves. He will die for it one day. Right now he is just a young man who sleeps in garrison stables when he has to and acts like a knight when he does not have to.

> **A) Tell him you admire the conviction. He looks surprised — not many say that.** (+1 ROSE, Sturm notes you) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) Ask him about his father. He is quiet a moment. 'He left the Order. I chose not to.'** (+1 ROSE, deep recognition) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) Nod back. Let the moment be what it is.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING

---


## SCENE 11_MORNING — THE MORNING

*Castle Brightholm — After the Spar*

The spar with Aldric is done and the bruises are already forming. Formation is over. Lord Caeron has given the assignments. The field exercise on the south road is not today — it is tomorrow, or the day after, depending on preparations. Today is yours to use. The garrison operates on a rhythm: mornings are for training and study, afternoons for practical work and intelligence, evenings for the quieter things — the watch, the forge, the conversations that happen when the day's noise settles. How you spend this time matters. It is the last of it you will have before things change.

> **MORNING — Choose how to spend the morning hours. You may return here after each activity.**
>
> **A) Seek out Ser Aldous in the chapel library. The Measure has questions you have not answered.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 4
>
> **B) Check the infirmary. There was mention of refugees arriving in the night.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 9
>
> **C) Train harder. You want to be sharp for tomorrow.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 24
>
> **D) Visit the garrison quartermaster. You have steel and tomorrow is the march.** --> Scene 11_QM
>
> **E) The morning is spent. Move on to the afternoon.** --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

---


## SCENE 11_QM — THE QUARTERMASTER

*Castle Brightholm — Quartermaster's Store, Morning*

The quartermaster is a broad woman named Hesta who has been supplying Solamnic garrisons since before the Cataclysm broke the supply lines. Her storeroom smells of oiled leather, lamp oil, and the particular dust of things that have been inventoried more often than they have been used. She looks at your tabard, your rank, your purse, and calculates exactly how much of your stipend you are about to leave on her counter.

'Squire,' she says, by way of greeting. 'What do you need?'

> **SHOP — BRIGHTHOLM QUARTERMASTER**
> Browse the wares. Prices in steel pieces (stl). Check your character sheet for current gold.
>
> | Item | Price | Notes |
> |------|-------|-------|
> | Bandage (1 use) | 1 stl | Stabilize at 1 HP |
> | Potion of Healing | 5 stl | 2d4+2 HP, bonus action in combat |
> | Rations (3 days) | 1 stl | Travel supplies |
> | Antitoxin | 3 stl | Advantage on poison saves for 1 hour |
> | Whetstone | 1 stl | +1 damage on next attack (single use) |
> | Caltrops (bag) | 2 stl | 10ft area, DC 12 DEX or 1 piercing + speed 0 |
> | Rope (50 ft) | 1 stl | Climbing, binding |
> | Torch (5) | 1 stl | Light source |
>
> **RARE STOCK ROLL (once per visit):**
> Roll 1d20 to see if Hesta has anything special today.
> 1–15: Standard stock only.
> 16–18: Uncommon — Greater Potion of Healing available (15 stl, 4d4+4 HP).
> 19: Uncommon — Masterwork dagger available (+1 damage, not magical, 20 stl).
> 20: RARE — +1 Shield available (50 stl). Dented, old, Solamnic make. Hesta found it in the deep stores.
>
> *Record purchases on your character sheet. Deduct steel spent.*

Hesta wraps your purchases in waxed cloth with garrison efficiency. 'Don't die,' she says. This is her version of good luck.

> **A) Done shopping. Return to the morning.** --> Scene 11_MORNING

---


## SCENE 11_AFTERNOON — THE AFTERNOON

*Castle Brightholm — Midday and After*

The sun is overhead and the garrison shifts into its afternoon rhythm. The morning's edge — training, study, the formality of formation — gives way to something looser. Squires move between tasks with less supervision. The mess hall fills. The forge fires are banked high. Somewhere in the east wing, Thessaly is interviewing someone. Somewhere else, Mira is tending whoever needs tending. The garrison is a small world and you are learning its geography.

Tomorrow you march south. The field exercise. 'Reported bandits.' Whatever that means, it means something different than it did three weeks ago. The south road has been in the briefings every morning and every morning the language has been slightly more careful, which is how you know the situation is slightly worse.

> **AFTERNOON — Choose how to spend the afternoon. You may return here after each activity.**
>
> **A) Go to the mess hall. Eat. Watch. Learn.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 33
>
> **B) Find Thessaly — she may have intelligence on the south road.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 23
>
> **C) Check on Mira before you march.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 25
>
> **D) Visit the forge. Your blade needs attention.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 35
>
> **E) Visit the armoury. Your gear could use an upgrade before the march.** --> Scene 11_ARMOURY
>
> **F) Shouts from the training yard. Something has come over the wall.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_YARD
>
> **G) The afternoon is spent. Move on to the evening.** --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_ARMOURY — THE ARMOURY

*Castle Brightholm — Armoury, Afternoon*

The armoury is in the east wing, past the forge. The heat hits you three steps before you reach the door. Inside, the walls are lined with racks — swords, shields, polearms, all maintained to Solamnic standard, which means they gleam even when nobody is looking. The armourer is a thin man named Garrett who moves with the precision of someone who has fitted a thousand suits of mail and knows exactly which rivet you will need replaced before you do.

He looks at your current equipment, frowns the professional frown of a man who sees room for improvement, and gestures at his stock.

> **SHOP — BRIGHTHOLM ARMOURY**
> Browse the wares. Prices in steel pieces (stl). Check your character sheet for current gold.
>
> **WEAPONS:**
> | Item | Price | Notes |
> |------|-------|-------|
> | Longsword | 15 stl | 1d8+STR, versatile (1d10) |
> | Greatsword | 20 stl | 2d6+STR, heavy, two-handed |
> | Shortsword | 10 stl | 1d6+STR, finesse, light |
> | Handaxe | 5 stl | 1d6+STR, thrown (20/60) |
> | Dagger | 2 stl | 1d4+STR, finesse, light, thrown (20/60) |
> | Javelin (3) | 3 stl | 1d6+STR, thrown (30/120) |
>
> **ARMOUR & SHIELDS:**
> | Item | Price | Notes |
> |------|-------|-------|
> | Shield | 10 stl | +2 AC |
> | Studded Leather | 12 stl | AC 12+DEX (lighter than chain) |
> | Chain Mail | 25 stl | AC 16 (upgrade/replacement) |
>
> **RARE STOCK ROLL (once per visit):**
> Roll 1d20 to see if Garrett has anything in the back.
> 1–15: Standard stock only.
> 16–18: Uncommon — Greater Potion of Healing available (15 stl, 4d4+4 HP). 'Left behind by a patrol.'
> 19: Uncommon — Masterwork longsword available (+1 damage, not magical, 20 stl). 'My best work this year.'
> 20: RARE — +1 Longsword available (50 stl). Old Solamnic steel, faintly warm to the touch. Garrett does not know what it is. You do.
>
> *Record purchases on your character sheet. Deduct steel spent.*

Garrett watches you test the balance of whatever you have chosen. He nods once if he approves. He nods once if he does not approve, too — you cannot tell the difference. 'The south road is not kind to cheap steel,' he says. 'Whatever you carry, carry it sharp.'

> **A) Done shopping. Return to the afternoon.** --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

---


## SCENE 11_YARD — THE THING IN THE TRAINING YARD

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard, Afternoon*

The shout comes from the yard — not a drill shout, not the bark of a training sergeant. A real shout. The kind that has fear in it. You are running before you identify the voice.

The training yard gate — the one that leads to the eastern slope, the one that is supposed to be barred at all times because the eastern slope leads to forest — is open. Not forced. Unbarred. Someone left it unlatched and the smell of the mess hall kitchen, which backs onto the yard, has drawn something in from the wild.

A dire boar. Not the farm boar you have seen in textbooks — a dire boar, chest-high, scarred, tusks the colour of old bone and the length of your forearm. It has overturned a weapons rack and is standing in the centre of the yard, sides heaving, eyes red with the particular rage of an animal that has been driven south by something worse than itself. The Dragon Army's advance is pushing wildlife north. This is what that looks like at ground level.

Two squires are pressed against the far wall. One of them is bleeding — a gash across the thigh from a tusk. The other is holding a practice sword that will not do a thing against an animal this size. They are both younger than you and they are both terrified.

**IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Aldric is already in the yard. He came from the armoury at a dead sprint and he is carrying his real sword, not a practice blade. He positions himself between the boar and the wounded squire without being told.

**IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** You can hear her boots on the corridor stone behind you. She will be here in thirty seconds. The squire's thigh wound needs her.

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run at your table. Skip to AFTER THE FIGHT.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow rounds below. Roll when prompted.
>
> **ENEMY:**
> **Dire Boar:** AC 12, HP 28, Speed 40 ft. Tusks +5 (2d6+3 piercing). Charge: if the boar moves 20+ ft in a straight line, tusks deal an extra 2d6 and target must make DC 13 STR save or be knocked prone. Relentless (1/day): if reduced to 0 HP by damage that would not kill outright, drops to 1 HP instead.
>
> **YOUR STATS:** Fighter: HP 12, AC 16, Longsword +5 1d8+3. Paladin: HP 11, AC 16, Longsword +5 1d8+3.
>
> **COMPANION ACTIONS (choose 1 per round):**
> | Companion | Action A | Action B | Action C |
> |-----------|----------|----------|----------|
> | Aldric (if present) | Flank (+1 attack) | Shield Wall (+1 AC) | Aggressive Strike (1d8+2, takes 1d4) |
> | Other squire | Distraction (boar -1 next attack) | Throw practice sword (1d4) | Flee with wounded squire (removes civilians from danger) |

> **ROUND 1 — THE CHARGE**
>
> *The boar lowers its head. The tusks catch the afternoon light. It charges — not at you, at the wounded squire. Forty feet of yard, four hundred pounds of animal, and two seconds to put yourself in the way.*
>
> **INTERCEPT:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Athletics (+3) | STR | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (13+):** You throw yourself into the boar's path. It hits you instead. Make a STR save DC 13 or be knocked prone. Either way, the squire is clear. +1 ROSE.
>
> **FAILURE (1-12):** You are too slow. The boar reaches the squire. The squire takes 2d6+3 damage. If Aldric is present, he intercepts instead (he takes the hit, -5 HP to Aldric). If Aldric is not present, the other squire drags the wounded one aside — barely.
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5) | DC 12 (Boar AC)
>
> **HIT:** Your blade bites into the boar's flank. It screams — a sound you did not know boars could make. Deal 1d8+3 damage.
>
> **MISS:** The boar is fast. Faster than something that size should be.
>
> **BOAR'S GORE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (Tusks +5)
>
> **SUCCESS:** You catch the tusks on your blade and turn them aside.
>
> **FAILURE:** Take 2d6+3 piercing damage. The tusks go through padding like it is not there.

> **ROUND 2 — CORNERED ANIMAL**
>
> *The boar is wounded and angry. It circles, head low, blood on its tusks — yours or the squire's or both. The training yard is not large enough for this. The walls make it worse. A cornered dire boar is the second most dangerous thing in the Solamnic lowlands. The first is what drove it here.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5) | DC 12
>
> **HIT:** Deal 1d8+3 damage. The boar staggers. If this reduces it to 0 HP, **Relentless triggers**: it drops to 1 HP instead, enraged.
>
> **MISS:** It dodges. For something this large, it moves like water.
>
> **(Paladin) OPTIONAL — DIVINE SMITE:** If your attack hit, add 2d8 radiant damage. The light of your conviction is visible. The boar flinches. One spell slot expended.
>
> **(Fighter) OPTIONAL — ACTION SURGE:** Take a second attack this round. One use expended.
>
> **BOAR'S GORE (if still standing):**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15
>
> **SUCCESS:** Turned aside.
>
> **FAILURE:** Take 2d6+3 piercing. If this drops you to 0 HP: **IF MIRA HAS ARRIVED** she stabilizes you. You wake up in the infirmary. The boar was finished by Aldric or the garrison watch. Proceed to AFTER THE FIGHT. **IF MIRA IS NOT PRESENT:** Aldric (if present) drags you clear. The garrison watch finishes the boar with crossbow bolts. You wake up on the yard stones.

> **ROUND 3 — THE KILL (if boar still standing)**
>
> *It is dying and it knows it and it does not care. The eyes are not red anymore — they are flat, animal, the eyes of a thing that has been running from something it cannot fight and has decided to stop running here, in this yard, against you. There is something terrible and honest in it.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5) | DC 12
>
> **HIT:** The blade goes in clean. The boar falls. The yard is suddenly, completely quiet except for the sound of two squires breathing and the distant clatter of the garrison responding to an alarm that is already over.
>
> **MISS:** Aldric finishes it. Or the garrison watch arrives with crossbows. Either way, it ends here.

> **AFTER THE FIGHT**
>
> The boar is dead in the training yard. Its blood is on the flagstones and will stain. The wounded squire — his name is Pell, you learn later — has a gash that will scar but will heal. Mira, if present, treats him on the yard stones with the efficient calm of someone who has been waiting to be needed.
>
> **IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She looks up from the wound. 'The gate was unlatched.' It is not an accusation. It is a diagnosis. Something drove this animal into the garrison and the garrison was not ready. She is already thinking about what else might come over the wall before morning.
>
> **IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He is cleaning his blade. He looks at you. He does not say anything about the fight — Aldric does not comment on combat performance when the combat was real. What he does is nod. Once. The nod of a man who has been fighting beside you and has decided that fighting beside you is where he belongs.
>
> Ser Aldous arrives. He studies the boar. He studies the gate. He studies you. 'The wildlife is moving north,' he says. 'The Dragon Army is pushing everything ahead of it. This will not be the last.' He pauses. 'You did well, Squire.'
>
> **LOOT — BOAR TUSKS (optional):**
> The dire boar's tusks are intact. They are valuable — ivory, old, dense enough to be worked into weapon grips or sold.
> **A) Take the tusks.** Gain: Dire Boar Tusks (worth 3 stl, or can be worked into a weapon grip: +1 to Intimidation checks in combat).
> **B) Leave them.** The garrison groundskeeper will deal with it. +1 ROSE (Pell thanks you for saving him, not for salvaging the thing that gored him).
>
> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots, Lay on Hands pool.
> **Short rest available:** Recover Second Wind, Action Surge.
> Record: XP earned: 15 XP.

> **A) Return to the afternoon.** --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

---


## SCENE 11_EVENING — THE EVENING

*Castle Brightholm — Dusk*

The light changes. The garrison at dusk is a different place than the garrison at noon — quieter, longer-shadowed, the kind of quiet where conversations happen that would not happen in daylight. The wall torches are lit. The mess hall empties. The courtyard belongs to the night watch now and the people who come out when the day's work is done and the real thinking begins.

Tomorrow. The word has weight now. You can feel it in the way people move — slightly more deliberately, slightly more aware of each other. Aldric cleaned his armour twice today. Thessaly's notebook has not left her hand since lunch. Even Caeron, who is never visibly affected by anything, paused at the window during the afternoon briefing and looked south for three seconds longer than a man looks at something he is not worried about.

> **EVENING — Choose how to spend the evening. You may return here after each activity.**
>
> **A) Take a night watch shift. The wall has things to teach you.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 34
>
> **B) Find a quiet place. Write a letter home. You may not get another chance before the march.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_LETTER
>
> **C) Seek out a companion for a quiet conversation by the fire.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_FIRE
>
> **D) Turn in early. Tomorrow matters and sleep is preparation.** --> Scene 11_NIGHT
>
> **E) The alarm bell. Goblins on the perimeter. Grab your weapon.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_PATROL
>
> **F) Spend the evening getting to know your companions better.** --> Scene BOND_CAMP

---


## SCENE 11_PATROL — THE NIGHT PATROL

*Castle Brightholm — South Perimeter, Night*

The alarm is a single bell, struck twice. Not the full garrison alarm — the sentry alarm, the one that means *something is here but we do not know what yet*. You are on your feet before the second strike fades. Your weapon is in your hand before you think about reaching for it. Training.

The south perimeter is a stretch of low wall between the garrison's main fortification and the old granary. The torches have been doused — deliberately, which means the sentries saw something and went dark. Aldric is beside you. He arrived at the same time you did, which means he was not sleeping either.

A garrison sentry — a man named Corwin — is crouched behind the wall. There is an arrow in his shoulder. It went through the mail at the joint, which means whoever shot it knew where to aim. 'Goblins,' he says through his teeth. 'Three, maybe four. They were probing the wall. Pulled back when I called it.'

Blood is running down his arm. The arrow is still in.

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run the encounter at your table, then skip to **AFTER THE FIGHT**.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow the rounds below. Roll when prompted.

> **INJURED NPC — SENTRY CORWIN**
> Arrow in shoulder, bleeding. Will collapse in 4 rounds without treatment.
> **Heal him:** Mira (if present, automatic), Paladin Cure Wounds (1 spell slot), Paladin Lay on Hands (5 HP from pool), Bandage (1 use, stabilize at 1 HP), Fighter Magic Initiate healing spell (if applicable).
> *Record any resources spent on your character sheet.*
> **If healed:** Corwin returns to the wall. +1 morale for garrison. He gives you his garrison watch token (+1 to one future Brightholm check).
> **If not healed:** Corwin is carried to the infirmary. He survives but cannot fight tomorrow. The south wall is short one sentry.

> **COMPANION SELECTION**
> Aldric is with you automatically. Choose one additional companion (if available):
> **Sera** — Scout advantage. +1 to your first attack roll (she spots them first).
> **Mira** — Heals Corwin automatically. Frees your action economy.
> **Lysander** — Veteran presence. +2 to your first attack roll. 'Watch the treeline.'

> **ENEMY STAT BLOCKS (Pen & Paper)**
> **Goblin Scout (3):** AC 13, HP 7, Speed 30ft. Scimitar +4 (1d6+2). Shortbow +4 (1d6+2, 80/320). Nimble Escape (Disengage/Hide as bonus action).
> **Goblin Boss:** AC 15, HP 12, Speed 30ft. Scimitar +4 (1d6+2). Shortbow +4 (1d6+2). Redirect Attack (reaction: when missed, redirect to adjacent goblin scout — the boss sacrifices his own). Multi-attack: 2 scimitar attacks.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 1

The treeline is forty feet south. Moonlight makes the grass silver and the shadows black. You can see shapes — low, hunched, moving with the particular scuttle of things that know they are smaller than you and have decided that numbers and darkness make up the difference.

Three goblins. They are fanned out across the approach — one left, one centre, one right. The centre one is bigger. Better armed. It is giving orders in a language that sounds like gravel being chewed.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Choose a target:**
> **Left goblin** / **Centre goblin (Boss)** / **Right goblin**
>
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC (Scouts: 13, Boss: 15)
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus. Meet or beat the DC = hit.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage (your weapon die + STR modifier).
>
> **IF SERA IS PRESENT:** +1 to this roll. She spotted them from the wall — you know exactly where they are.
> **IF LYSANDER IS PRESENT:** +2 to this roll. He is beside you, calm as a man watching rain. 'The big one. Always the big one first.'

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:**
> **Aldric:**
> A) Flank — Move to opposite side. +1 to your next attack.
> B) Shield Wall — Brace beside you. +1 AC until next round.
> C) Aggressive Strike — Charges the nearest goblin. 1d8+2 damage, but Aldric takes 1d4 damage from the engagement.
>
> **(If Sera):**
> A) Scout Shot — Fires from the wall. 1d6 damage to a goblin of your choice.
> B) Mark Target — Calls out movement. +2 to your next attack.
> C) Disengage Cover — Covers your retreat if needed. Safe withdrawal guaranteed.
>
> **(If Mira):**
> A) Heal Corwin — Removes the arrow, stops the bleeding. Corwin stabilized. (Frees your healing resources.)
> B) Bandage — Stabilizes Corwin at 1 HP. Less effective but faster.
> C) Herbal Boost — Gives you a poultice. +1 to your next saving throw.
>
> **(If Lysander):**
> A) Combat Instruction — Corrects your stance mid-fight. +2 to your next attack.
> B) Veteran Strike — Steps forward and cuts. 1d10+3 damage to the nearest goblin.
> C) Guard — Positions himself to take the next hit meant for you.

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):**
> • (Paladin) Cast Bless: +1d4 to attacks and saves for up to 3 targets, Concentration, lasts entire combat. 1 spell slot. Does not replace attack.
> • (Paladin) Divine Smite: Bonus action after hitting with a melee weapon. 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). Once per turn. 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest at level 2+).
> • (Paladin) Lay on Hands: Heal self or Corwin up to [pool] HP. Bonus action (does not replace attack).
> • (Paladin) Cure Wounds: Heal Corwin 2d8+CHA HP. 1 spell slot. Replaces your attack this round.
> • (Fighter) Action Surge: Take an additional Action this round (except Magic action). 1/short or long rest.
> • (Fighter) Second Wind: Heal 1d10+[level] HP. Bonus action. 2 uses/long rest, regain 1/short rest.
> • (Any) Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action. Consumes 1 potion.
> • (Any) Use Bandage on Corwin: Stabilize at 1 HP. Replaces your attack.

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 1

The right goblin fires its shortbow. The arrow comes out of the dark with a sound like a whispered threat.

> **DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14 (goblin attack +4, DC = attack bonus + 10)
> **SUCCESS (14+):** You deflect or dodge. No damage.
> **FAILURE (1-13):** The arrow hits. Take 1d6+2 piercing damage. Record on your character sheet.
> **IF ALDRIC CHOSE SHIELD WALL:** DC reduced to 13 (+1 AC).
> **IF LYSANDER CHOSE GUARD:** Lysander takes the hit instead. He grunts. 'That one was free.'

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 2

The goblins are fast. The one you did not target has circled right, looking for a flank. The boss is barking orders — sharper now, angrier. Whatever they expected to find at this wall, resistance was not it.

The night air smells of goblin — unwashed leather, rancid fat, something acrid that might be poison on the arrowheads. The grass is wet. Your boots slide. The torch on the wall behind you casts your shadow long and the goblins keep looking at it, tracking your position by the dark shape you throw.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Choose a target:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus. Meet or beat the DC = hit.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **PERCEPTION CHECK (free action):** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 13
> **SUCCESS:** You spot a fourth goblin — hidden in the ditch, flanking position. You can redirect your attack or warn Aldric.
> **FAILURE:** You do not see the fourth goblin. It will attack in Round 3 with advantage.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options as Round 1)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options as Round 1)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 2

The boss charges. It is faster than it should be, low to the ground, scimitar in each hand. It screams something that might be a war cry or might be an insult — with goblins, the distinction is academic.

> **DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS (14+):** You turn the blade. The boss snarls and recoils.
> **FAILURE (1-13):** The scimitar bites. Take 1d6+2 slashing damage.
>
> **BOSS ABILITY — REDIRECT ATTACK:** If you hit the boss this round and a goblin scout is adjacent, the boss shoves the scout into the blade path. The scout takes the damage instead. The boss survives. *This happens once.*

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 3

The fight is close now. Blood on the grass — yours, theirs, or both. The goblins are not retreating. They should be retreating. Three goblins do not hold against armoured Solamnic squires unless they are desperate, fanatical, or buying time for something else. The boss is still standing and still fighting and it occurs to you, between heartbeats, that this was never a raid. This was reconnaissance. They were counting your sentries.

**IF THE 4TH GOBLIN WAS NOT SPOTTED:** It emerges from the ditch behind you. Surprise attack with advantage.
> **SURPRISE DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14. The goblin rolls twice and takes the better result (advantage).
> **FAILURE:** Take 1d6+2 piercing damage. The goblin is now in melee range behind you.
**IF THE 4TH GOBLIN WAS SPOTTED:** You warned Aldric. He is already turning. The goblin's ambush fails.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Final round. End this.**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage. *If this kills the boss, describe it. This is your moment.*

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options as previous rounds)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options as previous rounds)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 3

Whatever remains fights with the desperation of things that know the mathematics have turned. If the boss is alive, it makes one final attack — not at you. At Corwin. Finishing what it started.

> **IF BOSS IS ALIVE — PROTECT CORWIN:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Athletics or DEX save | DC 13
> **SUCCESS:** You intercept. The boss's blade hits your shield or armour. Corwin is safe.
> **FAILURE:** The boss reaches Corwin. 1d6+2 damage to an already-wounded man. If Corwin has not been healed, he drops to 0 HP and begins death saves.

---

### AFTER THE FIGHT

The last goblin falls or flees. The night returns to its usual sounds — wind, distant water, the breathing of people who have just fought for the first time and are discovering what that does to the body. Your hands are shaking. This is normal. Aldric's hands are shaking too, and he does not try to hide it.

On the goblin boss: a crude map of the garrison perimeter. Marked in charcoal: the south wall, the granary, the sentry positions. Whoever sent these goblins knew what they were looking for.

> **SEARCH THE FALLEN (Optional — moral choice)**
> The goblins are dead. Their equipment is crude but they may carry coin or useful items.
> Searching enemy dead is not forbidden by the Measure, but it is not honoured either.
> Aldric looks at his boots. Corwin does not care — he is being bandaged.
>
> **A) Search them.** (-1 ROSE or -1 CROWN, whichever is lower. Roll below.)
> **B) Leave them. Report to the garrison.** (+1 ROSE or +1 CROWN. No loot.)

> **LOOT ROLL (if searched):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–5: Nothing useful. Goblin gear is garbage.
> 6–10: 1d4 stl in a belt pouch. Copper mixed with steel. 1 day rations (smoked rat meat — edible, barely).
> 11–14: 2d4 stl + a mundane item (whetstone, 10ft rope, 2 days rations).
> 15–17: 3d4 stl + a useful item (Potion of Healing, caltrops, a signal horn). 1 day rations.
> 18–19: 4d4 stl + a quality item (masterwork dagger, a map of the south road). 2 days rations.
> 20: 5d4 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL. 3 days rations.

> **RARE ITEM ROLL (only on natural 20 above):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–19: Quality mundane item (well-crafted goblin blade, usable as shortsword).
> 20: MAGIC ITEM — +1 Dagger. Elvish make. What a goblin was doing with it is a question you cannot answer tonight.

> **GOBLIN CAMP STASH:** The goblins had a camp in the treeline. Investigation DC 11.
> **SUCCESS:** Stash Loot Roll:
> 1–5: Empty. They ate everything.
> 6–10: Supplies (rations, crude bandages, 1d4 stl).
> 11–14: 2d6 stl + mundane item.
> 15–17: 3d6 stl + Potion of Healing.
> 18–19: 4d6 stl + quality weapon.
> 20: 5d6 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL.

> **NPC GRATITUDE — SENTRY CORWIN** (if healed)
> Corwin grips your arm with his good hand. His face is grey but his grip is strong. 'I owe you one, Squire. I mean that.'
>
> **ROLL:** Persuasion (+[bonus]) | CHA | DC 10
> *You are not haggling. The roll reflects how much Corwin has to give.*
>
> **10–12 (Modest):** 'Here.' He presses 1d4 stl into your hand. Sentry pay. It is all he carries.
> **13–15 (Grateful):** 2d4 stl and his garrison watch token (+1 to one future Brightholm check).
> **16–18 (Deeply Grateful):** 3d4 stl, the watch token, and a Potion of Healing from the sentry kit. 'I was saving it. You need it more.'
> **19+ (Indebted):** 4d4 stl, the watch token, and a family ring (5 stl value, or keep for +1 to one Persuasion check in Vogler — 'Corwin's family is from the lake region').
> **FAILURE (1–9):** Corwin has nothing to give. He clasps your arm. 'I will remember your name.' +1 ROSE.

> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots,
> Lay on Hands pool, bandages, potions consumed.
> Update gold if loot was found. Record any items gained.
> **Short rest available:** Recover Action Surge, regain 1 Second Wind use. HP: spend Hit Dice if desired.

> **XP:** 10 XP per goblin killed. 15 XP for the boss. Bonus 10 XP if Corwin was saved. Bonus 5 XP if the 4th goblin was spotted.

> **A) Return to the evening. The wall is secure. For now.** --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_LETTER — THE LETTER HOME

*Castle Brightholm — Barracks, Late Evening*

You sit on the edge of your bunk with a candle and a piece of parchment that cost you two coppers from the quartermaster's stores. The pen is borrowed from Thessaly, who lent it without comment and with the faintest smile that suggested she approved of what you were using it for.

You write. You cross out. You write again. The difficulty is not finding words — it is finding the right ones. You cannot tell them what you know about the south road. You cannot tell them about the doubled guard or the refugee reports or the way Caeron looks when he thinks no one is watching. What you can tell them is that you are well, that you are ready, that you have friends beside you and a purpose ahead of you. These things are true. They are not the whole truth. But they are the part of the truth that will let your mother sleep, and that is worth the two coppers.

Aldric walks past as you are sealing it. He stops. Reads your expression. 'Family?' You nod. He nods back — the nod of someone who understands exactly what that letter costs and does not need to say so. Then he is gone and the barracks is quiet and the candle burns low.

> **A) Seal it. Set it on the quartermaster's outbound pile. The evening is not over yet.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) Add a postscript. Something true. Something you have not said yet. Then seal it. The candle is lower now but the evening still has time.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_FIRE — EVENING BY THE FIRE

*Castle Brightholm — Courtyard Brazier, Night*

The courtyard brazier is where the garrison comes when the day is over and the barracks feel too close. Three squires are already there, talking in low voices about nothing — the food, the weather, a rumour about the south. They make room when you approach. This is how it works: the fire belongs to whoever needs it.

> **Choose a companion to sit with. Each conversation is its own moment.**
>
> **A) Aldric is here, arms crossed, watching the fire like it owes him something.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_FIRE_ALDRIC
>
> **B) Thessaly is at the edge, notebook closed for once, looking at the stars.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_FIRE_THESSALY
>
> **C) (If Mira is in your party) Mira is tending a small herb pouch by firelight.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_FIRE_MIRA
>
> **D) (If Caeron is nearby) Lord Caeron is standing at the edge of the light, alone.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_FIRE_CAERON
>
> **E) Sit alone. The fire is enough company.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_FIRE_ALDRIC — ALDRIC BY THE FIRE

*Castle Brightholm — Courtyard Brazier, Night*

He does not look up when you sit down. This is not unfriendliness — it is Aldric's way of saying he noticed and does not need to perform noticing. You sit in silence for a while. The fire crackles. Somewhere on the wall, the night watch changes.

'Do you think about what happens after?' he says, eventually. Not looking at you. 'After the Trials. After the oath. After all of this becomes — real.'

He means: after we are not squires anymore. After the practice swords are replaced by the ones that kill people. After the south road stops being a briefing and starts being a place we go.

> **A) 'Yes. Every night.' He looks at you. Something shifts. The fire pops. Neither of you moves to leave, but the silence has changed.** (+1 ROSE, relationship deepens) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) 'I try not to. It does not help.' He nods slowly. The fire burns lower. After a while he claps your shoulder once and stands.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **C) 'I think about who I want beside me when it does.' He is very still. The fire is between you. Then he exhales and you sit together until the coals dim.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Aldric if not already active) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_FIRE_THESSALY — THESSALY BY THE FIRE

*Castle Brightholm — Courtyard Brazier, Night*

Her notebook is closed. This is unusual enough that it constitutes an event. She is looking at the sky with an expression you have not seen on her before — not analytical, not professional. Wistful.

'Do you know what I was before this?' she says, when you sit down. 'A clerk. In a printing house in Palanthas. I wrote advertisements for soap. I was very good at it.' A pause. 'I left because I realised I was writing about clean things from a clean room while the world was getting dirty. The pen felt dishonest for the first time.'

> **A) 'And now?' 'Now the pen feels like a weapon. I have not decided if that is better.' She looks at the stars a moment longer. Then the notebook comes out and the moment is over, but something was exchanged.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) 'You are doing important work here.' She looks at you with sharp gratitude. Then the mask comes back — professional, precise — but warmer at the edges.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **C) 'What would you write about tonight, if you could write anything?' She opens the notebook. For a moment you read together by firelight. Then she closes it and the evening resumes.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Thessaly if not active) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_FIRE_MIRA — MIRA BY THE FIRE

*Castle Brightholm — Courtyard Brazier, Night*

> **CONDITIONAL — Mira must be in your party.**

She is sorting herbs by firelight with the focused efficiency of someone whose hands know the work better than her eyes do. Yarrow. Comfrey. Something you do not recognise. She does not stop when you sit down but she moves the herb pouch slightly closer to you — an invitation to watch, or to stay, or both.

'I learned this from my mother,' she says. 'She could identify forty plants by smell alone. I can do thirty-two. I keep a list of the eight I cannot.' She looks up. 'That is what a healer is, if you think about it. A person who keeps a list of what they cannot yet do and works on it.'

> **A) 'That sounds like a knight, too.' She smiles — genuinely. You sit together a while longer before the fire burns low and the night calls you both back.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) Ask her to teach you one. She does — carefully, patiently. By the time you can identify it by touch alone, the brazier has burned to embers.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Mira if not active) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **C) Sit quietly and watch her work. The silence is enough. When she finally ties the pouch closed, the fire has gone to coals and the courtyard is still.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_FIRE_CAERON — CAERON AT THE EDGE

*Castle Brightholm — Courtyard, Night*

> **CONDITIONAL — Lord Caeron is nearby.**

He is standing where the firelight meets the dark — precisely at the boundary, as though he has calculated the exact distance at which he can observe without participating. When you approach he does not move but something in his posture adjusts. An acknowledgement.

'You should be resting, squire.' It is not an order. It is the observation of a man who knows what tomorrow requires and is concerned you do not.

'So should you, my lord.'

A pause. Then, very quietly: 'I do not rest well before exercises. I have found it more useful to stand here and count the things that could go wrong and make a plan for each of them. I am currently on number fourteen.'

> **A) 'What is number fourteen?' He almost smiles. Almost. You stand there until he reaches number twenty-three, and then he says 'Goodnight, squire' in a voice that is almost warm.** (+1 ROSE, relationship deepens) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) 'You care more than you show, my lord.' He goes very still. A long silence. Then: 'Go and rest.' But his voice has changed, and you carry it with you back toward the firelight.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Caeron if not active) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **C) Stand with him. Count your own list. Say nothing. When you finally leave, he nods once — the nod of a man who understands that some things do not need to be spoken aloud.** (+1 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 11_NIGHT — THE NIGHT BEFORE

*Castle Brightholm — Barracks, Night*

The barracks settles. Boots off. Armour racked. The sounds of ten people finding sleep in the order they always find it — the heavy breather in the corner first, then the shuffler by the window, then one by one the others, until it is just you and the dark and the particular quality of silence that exists in a room full of people who are all pretending to be asleep while thinking about tomorrow.

Aldric's breathing evens out. He is either asleep or very good at pretending. You stare at the ceiling and count the beams and think about the south road and the field exercise and the word 'bandits' and what it means when the garrison doubles the guard and Lord Caeron looks south for three seconds too long.

Sleep comes eventually. It always does. The last thing you see before it takes you is the window — south-facing, dark, showing nothing. The morning bell will come. It always does.

> **A) Sleep comes. Dawn follows. The field exercise begins.** --> Scene 26_PREP

---


## SCENE 12 — THE SPAR

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard, Dawn*

The yard is empty except for the two of you. That is by design — Aldric arrives before the morning bell because he does not like audiences, and you arrive before the morning bell because you have learned that the gap between Aldric Voss and everyone else is smallest at dawn, when the cold makes his left shoulder stiff and his footwork honest.

He is already moving through warm-ups when you enter. Practice swords — blunted steel, heavy enough to bruise, light enough that bruises are the worst of it. He tosses you one without looking. He has been beating you in sparring for seven months by the specific margin of someone who is better and knows it and does not need to prove it further.

This morning, something is different. You can feel it in the first exchange — the timing is closer than it has been. His combinations land, but yours land too. He adjusts. You adjust back. Twenty minutes in and the margin has disappeared entirely. He pauses, breathing hard, and looks at you with an expression that takes a moment to identify because you have not seen it before: surprised. Not unhappy. Surprised.

'You have been watching me,' he says. Not an accusation. An assessment. He looks pleased in the way that people who take competition seriously look pleased when the competition is finally worth their attention. 'The tell. You found it.' You did. Three months ago. You said nothing. 'Good,' he says — and means it — and raises the practice sword again.

> **THE SPAR — CHOOSE YOUR APPROACH**
>
> **A) 'Est Sularus oth Mithas.' Raise your blade. No quarter asked, none given.**
> *This skips the combat tutorial. You fight Aldric with full combat rules — attack rolls, defense rolls, round-by-round. The outcome depends on your dice. Proceed to THE REAL FIGHT below.*
>
> **B) 'Show me what I am doing wrong.' Let him lead. Learn the system.**
> *Aldric walks you through combat basics — attack rolls, defense, companion actions. You learn by doing. He wins at the end, but the lesson is worth more than the victory. Proceed to THE TRAINING BOUT below.*

---

> **THE TRAINING BOUT (Tutorial)**
>
> Aldric grins. 'All right. From the top.'
>
> He steps back into a guard stance and slows down — not insultingly, but enough for you to read what he is doing. He has spent seven months beating you. He has apparently also spent seven months cataloguing exactly what you do wrong.
>
> **COMBAT TUTORIAL — HOW FIGHTING WORKS**
>
> Combat in The Knight's Oath uses rounds. Each round has three beats:
>
> **Beat 1 — THE SITUATION.** You read what is happening. The enemy's position, your options, the ground.
>
> **Beat 2 — YOUR ACTION.** You attack (roll to hit), choose a companion action, and optionally use an ability or item.
>
> **Beat 3 — ENEMY STRIKE.** The enemy attacks. You roll to defend. If you fail, you take damage.
>
> Aldric demonstrates each beat. Pay attention.

> **TUTORIAL ROUND 1 — THE BASICS**
>
> *Aldric shifts his weight left. His guard drops — deliberately. He is showing you an opening.*
>
> 'See it? The shoulder. When I shift left, the right side opens for half a second. In a real fight, you take that.'
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC 12 (Aldric's practice guard — he is letting you learn)
>
> **HIT (12+):** Your blade connects with his practice padding. The impact is solid. 'Good. That is how it feels when you commit.'
>
> **MISS (1-11):** Your swing goes wide. 'You hesitated. In a real fight, hesitation is a wound you give yourself. Again.'
>
> **ALDRIC'S COUNTER:**
> 'Now I hit back. You roll to defend.'
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (11+):** You catch his blade on yours. The vibration runs up your arm. 'Good. You read the angle.'
>
> **FAILURE (1-10):** His practice blade clips your ribs. It hurts. 'That is what a hit feels like. Remember it. Avoid it.'
>
> *Tutorial note: In real combat, a failed defense means you take damage (enemy's weapon damage). Track HP on your character sheet.*

> **TUTORIAL ROUND 2 — COMPANION ACTIONS**
>
> 'In a real fight, you will not be alone,' Aldric says. 'Your companions act with you — one action per round, your choice.'
>
> **COMPANION ACTIONS (example — Aldric):**
> | Action | Effect |
> |--------|--------|
> | Flank | +1 to your attack roll |
> | Shield Wall | +1 to your AC (defense) |
> | Aggressive Strike | Aldric attacks for 1d8+2, but takes 1d4 damage |
>
> 'Choose what I do. I will show you what it looks like.'
>
> *Tutorial note: Each companion has unique actions. Choose based on what the round needs — more offense, more defense, or utility.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK (with companion support):**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC 12 (apply companion bonus if Flank chosen)
>
> **ALDRIC'S COUNTER:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 12 (apply companion bonus if Shield Wall chosen)

> **TUTORIAL ROUND 3 — ABILITIES AND ITEMS**
>
> 'Last thing,' Aldric says. He is breathing harder now — the tutorial has been a real workout. 'Your class gives you abilities. Use them.'
>
> **ABILITY USE (optional, once per round):**
> • **(Paladin)** Divine Smite: After hitting, add 2d8 radiant damage. Costs 1 spell slot. Once per turn.
> • **(Paladin)** Lay on Hands: Heal HP from your pool. Bonus action — does not replace your attack.
> • **(Fighter)** Second Wind: Heal 1d10+level HP. Bonus action. 2 uses per long rest.
> • **(Fighter)** Action Surge: Take a second attack this round. 1 use per short/long rest.
> • **(Any)** Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action. Consumes 1 potion.
> • **(Any)** Use Bandage: Stabilize an ally at 1 HP. Replaces your attack.
>
> 'Use everything you have,' Aldric says. 'Honor is in the outcome, not the method.'
>
> *Tutorial note: After each fight, you will see an AFTER THE FIGHT box reminding you to update HP, spell slots, ability uses, and inventory on your character sheet.*

> **TUTORIAL FINISH**
>
> The third round, Aldric stops holding back. His combinations come fast — the shoulder tell is gone, the openings are gone, the patient teacher is gone and in his place is the best swordsman in the squire class doing what he does best. He drives you back three steps, finds the gap in your guard that you did not know existed, and puts his practice blade against your throat.
>
> 'Dead,' he says. Then he grins. 'But better than last month. Significantly better.'
>
> He pulls the blade back. Offers his hand. You take it. The morning bell is ringing and somewhere formation is assembling and the bruises are already forming and Aldric Voss has just taught you everything you need to know about combat, which is: commit, read, choose, and do not hesitate.
>
> **+1 SWORD. You now understand the combat system.**

> **A) 'Thank you. For the lesson and for not going easy.' Shake his hand.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) 'I will take that opening next time.' He almost smiles. 'I know,' he says.** (+2 SWORD) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) 'You are a good teacher, Aldric.' He did not expect that. The surprise on his face is worth the bruises.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Aldric) --> Scene 11_MORNING

---

> **THE REAL FIGHT**
>
> *You said the words. Aldric's eyes change — the teacher is gone. The competitor is here. He raises his blade with the economy of someone who has been waiting for this, and you understand: he has. Seven months of winning by a margin. Seven months of watching you close the gap. He wanted this. He wanted you to say the words.*
>
> 'Good,' he says. And nothing else.
>
> **COMBAT — ALDRIC VOSS, SPARRING MATCH**
>
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run as a 3-round spar. Blunted weapons: all damage is nonlethal.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow rounds below. Roll when prompted.
>
> **YOUR STATS:** HP 12, AC 14 (practice padding), Practice Sword +4, 1d6+2 bludgeoning.
> **ALDRIC:** HP 14, AC 15 (practice padding + superior footwork), Practice Sword +5, 1d6+3 bludgeoning.
> Aldric fights with **Riposte:** If you miss an attack, Aldric's next attack is at +2.
> Aldric has a **Tell:** His left shoulder drops before a high combination. Perception DC 13 to spot it — if spotted, +2 to your next defense roll.
>
> **No companion actions — this is a duel.**
>
> *Track HP for both fighters. The match ends when one fighter reaches 0 HP or after 3 rounds (whoever has more HP remaining wins). A tie is possible.*

> **ROUND 1 — FEELING EACH OTHER OUT**
>
> *The yard is quiet except for breathing and the scrape of boots on packed earth. Aldric circles left — always left, it is his pattern, the one you have spent three months memorizing. The practice blade is heavy in your hand and you are acutely aware that this is the first time in seven months you have faced him without a ceiling on your effort.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+4) | DC 15 (Aldric's AC)
>
> **HIT (15+):** Your blade connects. Aldric takes 1d6+2 damage. His eyes widen — respect, genuine, the kind that costs something to give. 'There it is.'
>
> **MISS (1-14):** He reads your angle and slips it. 'Committed. Good. But I have seen that combination before.' **Aldric's Riposte activates — +2 to his next attack.**
>
> **ALDRIC'S STRIKE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (Aldric's attack +5) or DC 17 (if Riposte active)
>
> **SUCCESS:** You catch his blade, turn it, reset. 'Fast,' he says.
>
> **FAILURE:** His practice sword catches your shoulder. Take 1d6+3 damage. The pain is clarifying.
>
> **OPTIONAL — SPOT THE TELL:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Perception (+2) | WIS | DC 13
> **SUCCESS:** You see it — the left shoulder drops a quarter-inch before the high combination. +2 to your defense rolls for the rest of the fight. You found his tell. He does not know you found it.
> **FAILURE:** His patterns are fast. You cannot isolate the tell yet.

> **ROUND 2 — THE MIDDLE**
>
> *Sweat now. Real sweat, the kind that comes from two people who are evenly matched and know it and are each trying to find the thing that makes the difference. Aldric is adjusting — he always adjusts, that is what makes him dangerous, he does not repeat patterns he learns from — and you are adjusting too, and the adjustment is the conversation, and the conversation is faster than words.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+4) | DC 15
>
> **HIT:** Another solid strike. Aldric takes 1d6+2 damage. He shakes it off. He is grinning. He is grinning because he is losing and for the first time in seven months, losing feels like competing.
>
> **MISS:** He weaves. 'Closer.' **Riposte activates.**
>
> **ALDRIC'S STRIKE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (or DC 17 with Riposte, apply Tell bonus if spotted)
>
> **SUCCESS:** Blade caught, turned. You are breathing hard. So is he.
>
> **FAILURE:** Take 1d6+3 damage. He is not holding back. Neither are you. That is the point.

> **ROUND 3 — THE LAST EXCHANGE**
>
> *Three rounds. The practice swords are dented. Your arms are burning. Aldric's left shoulder is doing the thing and you may or may not have noticed it and it does not matter because this is the last exchange and everything — seven months of losses, three months of watching, the gap you found and the gap he has been trying to close — comes down to two rolls.*
>
> **Check HP totals. Determine who is winning:**
>
> **IF YOU ARE AHEAD ON HP — THE WINNING STRIKE:**
> You see the opening. His guard shifts — fatigue, genuine fatigue, the first you have ever seen from him — and the path to the finishing blow is clear. Your practice sword can end this.
>
> **A) Take it. Win clean.** (+2 SWORD)
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+4) | DC 15
> **HIT:** Your blade stops at his throat. The yard is silent. Aldric Voss looks at you and his expression is complex — not defeat, not admiration, something that contains both and transcends both. 'Well,' he says. 'That answers that.'
> **MISS:** He slips your strike and the round ends. **Go to TIE result.**
>
> **B) Pull the strike. Turn it into a draw. You have proven your point — you do not need to prove his defeat.** (+1 ROSE, +2 CROWN)
> Your blade stops an inch from his guard. You step back. Reset. The message is clear: *I had you and I chose not to take it.* Aldric stares at you. For a long moment, nothing. Then something shifts in his face — not gratitude, not relief. Recognition. You have just told him something about who you are that no victory could have communicated.
> He reaches to his belt and unsheathes his dagger — not the practice blade, his real one. Solamnic steel, well-kept, the handle wrapped in leather he replaced himself. He holds it out to you, hilt-first.
> 'The Measure says honor is demonstrated in restraint,' he says. 'I have been reading the wrong chapters.' A pause. His voice is quieter when he adds: 'You almost had me.' But his eyes say: *You had me. We both know it.*
> **ITEM GAINED: ALDRIC'S DAGGER** — 1d4+STR, finesse, light, thrown (20/60). Solamnic make. It is heavier than a dagger should be. It carries the weight of something given, not won. **ROMANCE SPARK Aldric.**
>
> **IF ALDRIC IS AHEAD ON HP — THE LOSING BLOW:**
> He finds the opening you could not close. His practice blade connects and you stagger — not down, not beaten in the way that seven months of losses have beaten you. This is different. This was earned. You pushed him to the edge and he pushed back harder and the difference between you is not the gulf it was. It is a thread.
>
> 'Better,' he says, and offers his hand. He is breathing as hard as you are. 'Significantly better.'
> **+1 SWORD, +1 ROSE.** The loss costs nothing. The fight earned everything.
>
> **IF HP IS TIED — THE DRAW:**
> The practice swords lock. Neither of you can find the opening. Neither of you is willing to manufacture one. You are pressed together, guard to guard, breathing hard, and in the space between your faces there is something that seven months of competition has been building toward and neither of you has named.
>
> 'Draw,' Aldric says. He does not step back.
>
> 'Draw,' you agree. You do not step back either.
>
> The morning bell rings. Formation assembles. The draw stands. **+1 SWORD, +1 ROSE, +1 CROWN.** A tie, honestly earned, is worth more than a victory by margin.

> **AFTER THE SPAR**
>
> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> This was a practice bout. Restore HP to full (no real injuries). Record any items gained (Aldric's Dagger, if applicable).
> Record: SWORD, ROSE, CROWN points earned.

> **A) Walk to formation together. Whatever happened in the yard stays in the yard.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) 'Same time tomorrow?' He almost smiles. 'If you can walk.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING

## SCENE 13 — THE REPAIRED SWORD

*Castle Brightholm — Armoury*

The armoury smells of iron filings and neatsfoot oil and the particular efficiency of a woman who has been doing this work for longer than you have been alive and views every preventable problem as a small personal insult. She takes your sword without comment, examines the pommel dent with the expression of someone who has seen worse but finds worse no consolation, and sets it in the repair queue. While you wait, Lord Caeron arrives for his monthly equipment review. He acknowledges you with the absence of acknowledgment that means he has registered you and is thinking about it.

He works his way through the rack with the same clipboard efficiency. When he reaches your sword — the dent now smoothed, the pommel flush and clean — he holds it at eye level for exactly the same amount of time as every other sword. He makes his mark. He sets it down. He moves to the next one. He does not comment. You understand, from everything you know about Lord Caeron Ashvale, that not commenting is the comment. You collect your blade. The armoury is warm and the morning still has hours left.

> **A) 'Thank you, my lord.' Accept it quietly. Return to the morning's work.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) 'What do you look for in a squire, my lord?'** (+1 ROSE, opens Caeron path) --> Scene 28
>
> **C) 'I notice you inspect your own equipment personally.'** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Caeron) --> Scene 29

---


## SCENE 14 — I CAN DO BETTER

*Castle Brightholm — Assessment Hall*

He does not look up. He makes a small mark on his clipboard. Then: 'Then do.' You turn to go. You are almost at the door when he adds — same tone, almost to himself but not quite: 'The dent is a small thing. It is the attention to small things that determines a knight's character.' He is already looking at the next item on his list. The assessment is over. The other thing hangs in the empty hall.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> He watches you leave. The pause before he returns to his papers is slightly longer than necessary.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 14
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 14+):** He said it to your back because he cannot say it to your face — not yet. That addendum cost him something. He does not give unsolicited assessments. You are the first squire this year he has followed with an additional remark. ROMANCE SPARK Caeron activates at Advantage if you act on this knowledge.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-13):** He speaks to the room. You are not sure if the remark was for you or habit.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

You are in the corridor when you fully understand what he said. Not the 'then do' — that was expected, brisk, over. The other thing. The one he said almost to himself. The dent is a small thing. It is the attention to small things. He is not talking about the sword. You replay it three times in the next twenty steps and by the third time you have decided it is the most useful thing anyone has said to you this week, possibly this month.

> **A) Go directly to the armoury and fix the dent today.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 13
>
> **B) Find Aldric — spar and work off the feeling.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 3

---


## SCENE 15 — THE POINTED QUESTION

*Castle Brightholm — Assessment Hall*

'Satisfactory is not the highest mark given today,' he says. 'Ser Voss received the same. You and he are currently equal. That answer will be the last one that surprises me from you. I would advise you not to lose the instinct that generated it.'

He leaves before you can respond. The hall is briefly, completely quiet. The other squire who was waiting for their result has apparently vanished. You stand in the empty corridor with the feeling of someone who has just been told something important in a language they are still learning. The morning light is strengthening through the east windows. The garrison is waking up around you.

> **A) File it away and move on. The morning has more to offer.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) Find Aldric and tell him. He will find it funny or annoying. Probably both.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) Ask around about Lord Caeron. Who is he really?** (+1 ROSE, opens Caeron background) --> Scene 30

---


## SCENE 16 — WHAT THESSALY WRITES DOWN

*Castle Brightholm — East Gate*

'That is the first honest answer I have gotten all week.' She asks if she can follow your progress through the Trials. In exchange, she will share what she hears.

There is something in how she frames it — not 'may I follow your progress' but a genuine exchange, an offer of her own access for yours. She has better intelligence than the garrison. You can see that from the map she carries and the ink still drying on the page she just turned. She has been here three days and she already knows things Lord Caeron does not. Whatever she is writing down, it is worth having her write it.

> **A) Yes. An ally who hears everything is valuable. You part ways — she has interviews, you have a morning to spend.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) Yes, but you want to read what she writes first. She agrees, and you leave her to her work.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) You would rather she observed and formed her own conclusions.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 19

## SCENE 17 — THE FAMILY NAME

*Castle Brightholm — East Gate*

'Six generations. Does that feel like a gift or a weight?'

It is the kind of question that sounds simple and isn't. Thessaly asks it the way she asks everything — without judgment already loaded into it, genuinely waiting to see what you say. Her pen is not moving. Whatever you answer, she is listening, not transcribing.

She found you near the east wall, which is not a coincidence. Thessaly Brightwater does not accidentally find people. The evening is cold and the torches have been lit and the garrison has the quieter particular quality of a place preparing for something. She has her notebook closed, which means this is not on the record, and her pen behind her ear, which means she might change her mind.

> **A) 'Both. Always both.'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 16
>
> **B) 'A gift. I carry it proudly.' She nods, pen still behind her ear. The conversation ends on its own terms. The morning continues.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) 'Mostly a weight lately.'** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Thessaly) --> Scene 16

## SCENE 18 — THE STRANGER IN THE BARN

*South Road — Night*

The barn was supposed to be empty. Night patrol sweep, routine, you have done a hundred of these. Your lantern finds them behind the hay bales: dark clothes, a wound managed for at least a day without proper materials, eyes that come up to meet yours with the calm of someone who has set fear aside for later as a matter of function. The clothes are civilian. The cuts where insignia were removed are still visible in the fabric.

> **COMPANION JOINS: COMMANDER SERATH (CONDITIONAL)**
> Dragon Army defector, possible love interest. Joins ONLY if you hide them.
> Role: Intelligence on Dragon Army movements and patrol schedules.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Insight (+1) | WIS | DC 14
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 14+):** They are telling the truth. The fear points south, not at you. Choose with full knowledge.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-13):** You cannot read them. You decide blind.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **Paladin Note:**
> If you are a Paladin: something stirs in you — not a class feature, not yet, but an instinct that will become Divine Sense at Level 3. You feel no fiendish presence, no undead taint. This is a person in genuine distress. The reading is clean. This is a human who is afraid. Mark 1 tally under MISHAKAL (the god of mercy toward the wounded).

> **A) Hide them. Treat the wound. Sort the implications later.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Serath, joins) --> Scene 36
>
> **B) Ask them to prove the defection first.** (+1 ROSE, conditional join) --> Scene 37
>
> **C) Tell Aldric — this is a two-person decision.** (Aldric's reaction varies) --> Scene 38
>
> **D) Report them immediately.** (+2 CROWN, Serath captured, romance closes) --> Scene 39

## SCENE 19 — THE FIRM WORD

*Castle Brightholm — Squire Quarters*

You stand in the restored quiet of your tent. The quill is back on the footlocker. Everything is exactly where it should be. You are not sure why this is unsatisfying.

The interaction with Zinnia — who borrowed your quill to write something she called 'extremely urgent correspondence' and returned it covered in blue ink — was brief, entirely reasonable on your part, and is now sitting oddly. You were polite. You were clear. She left without apparent offense. None of this explains the specific quality of the silence she left behind.

> **A) Go after her and apologise — you were too stiff.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 7
>
> **B) Let it go. She understood. You have other things to attend to this morning.** (neutral) --> Scene 11_MORNING

## SCENE 20 — WHAT ALDOUS KNOWS

*Castle Brightholm — Chapel Steps*

'A village. Twenty years ago. I had orders that were legal. That followed the Measure to the letter. And they were wrong. I followed them anyway because I told myself it was not my place to decide. The village is not there anymore.' He says it the way someone says a thing they have said before — out loud, to themselves, in the dark — enough times that the words are worn smooth. Not healed. Smooth.

> **You Gain:**
> Aldous's Trust. Unlocks a critical path in Scene 31.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** He has told this story before — not often, but deliberately. He chose to tell it to you now and not six months ago. Something about how you asked made him think you were ready for it. He is giving you the most important thing he can: evidence that the Measure can become a shield if you let it. This is instruction, not confession.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** It is a heavy story told plainly. You receive it as such.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

He is quiet for a moment. The chapel library is cold and the candle between you is down to its last inch and neither of you moves to replace it. 'I tell you this,' he says finally, 'not because it is a cautionary tale. It is not a cautionary tale. It is a true story about what happens when you let the law do your thinking. The Measure exists to protect people. If you ever hold the Measure in one hand and a person in the other and you are not certain which one matters more — that uncertainty is the answer.' He closes the commentary text. The lesson is over. The weight of it is not.

> **A) Thank him. Mean it. You leave the chapel carrying something heavier than when you entered. The morning light outside feels different now.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) Sit with him in silence a while longer. The candle gutters. When you finally rise, the morning has moved on without you, but you are not the same person who sat down.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING

## SCENE 21 — THE HEALER'S GIFT

*Castle Brightholm — Infirmary*

She prepared it before you asked — before the assignment was formally posted, even. Dried yarrow. Clean bandages rolled tight. A small clay jar of salve smelling of pine and something you cannot name. 'The yarrow slows bleeding. Press hard and do not move them until it stops. The salve is for infection — draconian wounds tend to close wrong without it.' She says this the way she says everything medical: factual, complete, without drama. Her hand is warm when yours brush taking the bundle. She does not pull away immediately.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> Her hand is warm when yours brush. 'Be careful,' she says — two words carrying more weight than their purpose.

> **ADD TO INVENTORY — MIRA'S TRAVEL BUNDLE**
> Mira prepared this before you asked. Native PC and CPC: add to your inventory or equipment list. • Dried yarrow (press hard: slows bleeding, DC 10 Medicine to apply) • Clean bandages (2 uses, each stabilises at 1 HP) • Pine salve (prevents infection in draconian wounds — use within 1 hour of injury)

> **A) 'I will. Thank you.' Hold her gaze. Then you are back in the courtyard with the afternoon sun on your face and the yarrow bundle warm in your hand.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Mira if first meeting warm) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) Ask her to come as a field medic. She considers. 'If they will have me.' You leave the infirmary knowing something about tomorrow has changed.** (+2 ROSE, joins if Rose 3+) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **C) Accept efficiently and leave. The afternoon is waiting. You have things to prepare.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

## SCENE 26_PREP — THE SOUTH GATE

*Castle Brightholm — South Gate, Dawn*

The armoury was open before the bell. Someone — you suspect Aldric — laid out your field kit on the bench with the particular arrangement of someone who has opinions about how equipment should be packed and has decided to express them through action rather than conversation. Sword oiled. Rations for three days. Waterskin. The practice blade replaced by the real one, which has a different weight — not heavier, exactly, but more serious, the weight of a thing that has a purpose beyond training.

The south gate is smaller than the main entrance — a working exit, not a ceremonial one. The stones are darker here, stained by centuries of departures that did not require an audience. Lord Caeron is already mounted, reviewing a field map with the compressed focus of a man who has been awake since before the bell and considers this normal. Aldric falls in beside you without discussion, the way he has fallen in beside you for eight months, and the familiarity of it steadies something.

**IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She appears from a direction you did not see her arrive from, already packed, already mounted. She nods once.

**IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She is checking medical supplies in the saddlebag with the focus of someone cataloguing what she has against what she might need. The list in her head is longer than the one in the bag.

Caeron gives the briefing in the shadow of the gate: south road, field exercise, assess and report. The words are formal. The tone is not. He looks south for one second too long before he gives the order to move.

> **WAGES PAID — FIELD EXERCISE PAY**
> The quartermaster hands you a leather pouch as you pass through the gate. Ten steel pieces — field exercise rate. 'Bring back receipts,' he says, deadpan. He has never once asked anyone for receipts.
> **Add 10 stl to your gold.**

> **A) Ride out. The south road is waiting.** --> Scene 22

## SCENE 22 — ALDRIC'S PLAN

*Castle Brightholm — Map Room*

He already has a plan. Aldric Voss does not arrive at planning sessions — he arrives to them. The approach routes are sketched in charcoal on the back of his exercise schedule with timing estimates and threat assessments in his small precise handwriting. 'Three approaches. Direct is fastest but visible from the ridge. East through the treeline is slower but quiet. West crosses the river and needs a ford.' He looks at you after each one. Not for permission. For what you think. This is what trust looks like when Aldric Voss demonstrates it.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** History (+3) | INT | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** The eastern treeline has a hidden ford — the route is faster than Aldric thinks.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** You have no useful knowledge of this terrain.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) 'East. Agreed.'** (+1 CROWN, relationship warms) --> Scene 40
>
> **B) 'Direct. We are knights, not scouts.'** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 41
>
> **C) 'What is on the west bank? I want more information.'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 42
>
> **D) 'East — but split up. Meet at the ridge.'** (+1 SWORD, +1 ROSE, risky) --> Scene 43
>
> **E) 'Wait. Let me check with Sera first — she has been watching the south road.'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN. If Sera is in your party: she gives you intelligence that makes the eastern route clearly the best option. Skip the roll — you already have the information.) --> Scene 40

## SCENE 23 — THESSALY'S INTELLIGENCE

*Castle Brightholm — East Gate*

Thessaly has a better map than the garrison does. Not better as in more detailed — better as in updated, with marks the garrison does not have, from sources the garrison has not consulted. She spreads it on the table in the field tent and shows you a red mark. 'Refugees,' she says. 'About thirty. Here, not here' — she taps the bandit location — 'here.' The second location is further south. 'The bandit report and the refugee report are from the same place. Draw your own conclusions.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Investigation (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** Thessaly's map has three additional marks she did not explain. Cross-referencing with garrison road records: the Dragon Army has made at least two probing passes on this road in the last month. The refugees are not just fleeing the war — they are fleeing something that has been methodically clearing the area ahead of the main advance.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** The map shows what Thessaly told you. Nothing more is visible.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Take the map directly to Lord Caeron before the exercise. He needs to see this. You leave Thessaly at the east gate and cross the courtyard with purpose. The afternoon light is sharp.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) Share it with Aldric and plan together. This changes everything. You fold the map carefully and go to find him. The afternoon has new weight.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **C) Ask Thessaly to come with you as an observer tomorrow. She agrees without hesitation. You part ways — the afternoon still has hours in it.** (+1 ROSE, Thessaly joins the field exercise) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

## SCENE 24 — SHARPENING THE BLADE

*Castle Brightholm — Training Yard*

You train until the light fails. Running forms. Working the gap in your guard that you spotted in Scene 3 and have been quietly furious about ever since. The yard empties around you. The evening bell rings. You keep going.

There is a particular quality to training when no one is watching — no evaluation marks, no Caeron with his clipboard, no Aldric to compete with. Just you and the forms and the steady accumulation of marginally better. It is not exciting. It is the point. Aldric finds you packing up. 'You have improved,' he says. From Aldric Voss, this is equivalent to a sonnet.

> **A) 'Yes.' You mean it. You rack the practice sword and walk back toward the garrison. The morning sun is high now.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) 'Ask me at the end of tomorrow.' He laughs. You head back together, the sweat cooling on your neck.** (+1 ROSE, Aldric laughs) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **C) 'I will not be ready until I am there.' He considers this. Nods. The yard is emptying around you.** (+1 ROSE, honest) --> Scene 11_MORNING

## SCENE 25 — BEFORE THE MARCH

*Castle Brightholm — Infirmary, Dawn*

She is awake before you come. The infirmary at pre-dawn has the quality of somewhere that has been working all night without anyone noticing. She hands you the folded paper before you speak — the yarrow directions in her careful hand. 'I prepared it this morning. Just in case.' She looks away when she says it. Not evasively — the way people look away when they are giving you something they cannot take back and they need a moment to finish releasing it. 'Be careful today.'

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> You stand in the infirmary doorway with morning light behind you and Mira will not quite look at you and you will not quite leave.

> **A) 'I will come back and tell you how it went.' She watches you go. The infirmary door closes behind you and the afternoon light is waiting.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Mira if Spark active) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) Nod. Say nothing. It means the same thing. You step out of the infirmary into the afternoon. The yarrow directions are folded in your pocket.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
