## SCENE 33 — THE MESS HALL

*Castle Brightholm — Midday*

The mess hall operates on a schedule that has not changed in forty years, which is either a testament to institutional consistency or evidence that no one with authority has eaten here recently. Long trestle tables, benches worn smooth, the smell of bread and something involving turnips that has been a source of garrison debate since before you arrived. The bread is good. The bread has always been good. The rest is a matter of opinion held by people who have stopped expecting otherwise.

Aldric eats like he does everything else — efficiently, without wasted motion, finishing before you are half done. Across the hall, Thessaly is interviewing one of the kitchen staff. Whatever she is learning about turnip procurement is, knowing Thessaly, somehow connected to garrison supply routes and by extension the Dragon Army's logistical capacity. Two tables down, Ser Aldous eats alone with a book open beside his plate and the comfortable air of a man who considers a meal without reading a meal wasted.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 10
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 10+):** At the corner table, partly hidden by the pillar: Lord Caeron is eating alone. He is not reading. He is watching the room — specifically, the squires. Specifically, for slightly longer than the others, you. When your eyes meet he looks down at his plate with the speed of someone who was not expecting to be caught. +1 to any Caeron Insight check this Act.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-9):** The mess hall is busy and loud and you notice nothing beyond the turnips.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **NPC CROSS-TALK — ALDRIC AND THESSALY**
> Aldric and Thessaly are arguing — not loudly, but with the focused energy of two people who are both certain they are correct. The subject, as far as you can tell: whether the garrison's intelligence on the south road is adequate. Thessaly thinks it is catastrophically insufficient. Aldric thinks the chain of command will provide. They are both, in different ways, right. Thessaly catches your eye mid-argument and raises one eyebrow — an invitation to weigh in, or permission to enjoy the show.

> **A) Join the argument. Side with Thessaly — the intelligence is inadequate. The argument burns itself out over bread and you leave the mess hall with the afternoon ahead of you.** (+1 ROSE, Thessaly approves, Aldric reconsiders) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) Join the argument. Side with Aldric — the chain of command exists for a reason. Thessaly makes a note. You finish eating and step back into the afternoon light.** (+1 CROWN, Aldric approves, Thessaly notes it) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **C) Listen. Do not weigh in. Take the bread. You leave them still arguing and walk into the courtyard. The afternoon is warm and there is still time.** (+1 ROSE — you are learning when to speak and when to watch) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **D) Sit with Aldous instead. You want to ask about something.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 4

---


## SCENE 34 — THE WATCH

*Castle Brightholm — East Wall, Night*

The night watch is four hours of looking at darkness and learning what darkness sounds like when nothing is in it. The east wall faces the road and the road faces south and south is where, at some indeterminate distance, something is happening that has not reached you yet. The stars are Solinari, half-full, and whatever scattered light the lesser moons provide. The wall is cold stone and you lean against it and breathe and the air smells of pine and frost and the particular mineral quality of a late autumn night in northern Solamnia.

You are alone for the first hour. Then you are not.

**IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Sera appears without announcement, as she does. She sits on the wall rather than leaning against it, legs dangling over the dark, and for ten minutes she says nothing. Then: 'Listen.' You listen. Wind. Pine. The creak of the gate timber. Nothing. 'Exactly,' she says. 'That is what worries me. No night birds. They stopped two days ago.' She looks at you with the flat professional gaze that means she is trusting you with something she has not told the senior officers yet. 'Something is on the south road. Something that frightened the wildlife before the patrols noticed.'

**IF SERA IS NOT IN YOUR PARTY:** You are alone for the four hours. This is not a hardship. There is a particular quality to standing watch that you have come to value — the suspension of the day's noise, the reduction to essentials: eyes, ears, the dark, the question of what is in it. You learn more about Castle Brightholm from its silence than from its bustle. The stone cools at a rate that tells you the season. The wind shifts at the second hour, carrying something from the south that is not quite smoke and not quite nothing.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** Just before the third hour: a light on the south road. Brief — a lantern uncovered and covered again, the signal pattern used by Solamnic scouts to report all-clear. But the garrison did not send a scout tonight. Someone is using Solamnic signals on the south road and the garrison did not authorise it. This is relevant in Scene 53B.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** The night is dark and clear and empty. Four hours. Nothing to report.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **Paladin Note:**
> If you are a Paladin: at the quietest part of the watch — the hour between two and three when even the wind stops — something happens. Not a vision. Not a voice. A feeling, behind your sternum, of being accompanied. Of someone standing watch with you who is not visible and not intrusive and simply: present. It lasts ten minutes. When it ends the cold feels less cold and you are certain, without evidence, that whatever is on the south road will not arrive tonight. Mark 1 tally under whichever god feels right. This is a small sign. Small signs count.

> **A) Report the light (if seen) to Caeron at dawn. Your watch ends. The relief arrives. You descend the wall into the torchlit courtyard, the evening's quiet still in your ears.** (+1 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) Tell no one. Watch more carefully tomorrow. Four hours pass. The relief arrives. You climb down from the wall with the night still on your skin.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **C) Share it with Sera (if present). Two sets of eyes are better. The watch passes faster with company. When it ends you descend together.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_EVENING

---


## SCENE 35 — THE FORGE

*Castle Brightholm — Armoury Forge, Afternoon*

The forge is the loudest place in Brightholm and the warmest. Bronwyn — the armourer, who has been here longer than Ser Aldous and sees no reason to say so — works the bellows with the steady rhythm of someone whose body stopped distinguishing between work and breathing years ago. The heat is a wall. The sound is a heartbeat. The smell is hot iron, coal, neatsfoot oil, and the specific human smell of someone who has been sweating productively since before dawn.

She does not acknowledge you for three minutes. This is not rudeness — Bronwyn has standards, and one of them is that she finishes what she is doing before she decides whether the interruption is worth her attention. When she does look up, she looks at your sword first and you second. This tells you everything about Bronwyn's hierarchy of values.

'Let me see it.' Not a request. She takes the sword, holds it to the light, turns it twice. Examines the edge where you have been sharpening it yourself. Makes a sound that is not approval but is the absence of disapproval, which from Bronwyn is considerable.

'You sharpen it too far forward,' she says. 'Two inches behind the point is where the work happens in a real fight. Not the tip. The belly.' She shows you. Her hands on the blade are as precise as a surgeon's. In three strokes she changes something you cannot quite identify and when she hands it back the balance is different. Better. You wonder how long the sword has been wrong and how long she has been waiting for you to bring it in.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Investigation (INT, proficiency if trained) (+0) | INT | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** While she works, you notice something on the forge wall — a Solamnic Knight's insignia, old, scorched. Not displayed. Set aside. 'My husband's,' she says, without being asked. 'Knight of the Rose. Died at Vingaard. The insignia survived the fire.' She does not say anything else about it. She does not need to. The forge is hot and the hammer falls and someone who loved a Knight of the Rose is still here, maintaining the swords, and has been for a very long time.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** She finishes her work. You learn about sword maintenance. The forge is loud and hot and that is all.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **ADD TO KNOWLEDGE — SWORD MAINTENANCE**
> Bronwyn's correction is permanent. Your longsword now has a +1 bonus to damage rolls against enemies in medium armour or heavier (you know where to aim). This bonus stacks with existing weapon modifiers. Mark this on your character sheet.

> **A) Ask her about the insignia. She talks while she works and you listen until the heat drives you back into the afternoon air.** (+1 ROSE — she tells you about Vingaard and what the Order used to be) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) Ask her to teach you more about blade work. An hour passes. You leave the forge smelling of iron and knowing something you did not know before.** (+1 SWORD — a practical lesson) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **C) Thank her and leave. She has work to do and the afternoon is not finished yet.** (+1 CROWN — she respects this) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

---


## SCENE M1 — THE LETTER AND THE SPIRIT

*Castle Brightholm — During Act One (Fighter Only)*

> **FIGHTER ONLY**
> This scene becomes available after Scene 8 (Ser Aldous on Justice). Read Scene 8 first. Paladins: your divine scenes (P-track) cover this ground differently — skip to Scene 9.

Ser Aldous stops you in the corridor two days after your conversation in the library. He has a book under his arm — not the Measure, something older, the binding cracked. 'Walk with me,' he says. He takes you to the garrison's east wall and shows you the southern road. A traveller is being turned away at the gate. The traveller has valid papers. The gate guard has a standing order: no travellers past the third bell. It is not yet the third bell by four minutes. The gate guard is being technically correct and functionally unkind.

> **THE MEASURE: THE MEASURE ON INTERPRETATION**
> The Measure was written to govern knights, not gate guards. But the same logic applies: the law is only as good as its interpretation. A law followed with malice is not the Measure. A law followed with judgment is. The question Aldous is asking, without asking it: when you hold the Measure, will you hold the letter or the intention?

> **A) Speak to the gate guard. The traveller has valid papers and the bell has not rung. The order should be followed as written — which means the traveller passes.** (+2 CROWN, +1 ROSE. Aldous: 'The letter, used well.') --> Scene M1_letter
>
> **B) Let it go. The guard is following orders. The traveller will find lodging. This is not a Measure problem.** (+1 CROWN. Aldous: 'Sometimes the correct thing is restraint.') --> Scene M1_restrain
>
> **C) Ask the guard why. Not to correct him — to understand his reasoning. Then, depending on the answer, decide.** (+2 ROSE. Aldous: 'That is the harder version of the right question.') --> Scene M1_ask

---


## SCENE M1_letter — THE LETTER WELL USED

*Castle Brightholm East Gate*

The guard is annoyed but cannot argue. The traveller passes. Aldous watches you the whole time with the expression of someone marking a test paper he expected to be harder. 'The letter well used,' he says. 'You can defend that decision at any Measure tribunal in Solamnia. You can also defend it to the traveller. Both matter.' He hands you the old book. 'Read the third chapter when you have time. It is about what happens when the letter is used badly.'

> **MEASURE TRACK: +2 — THE LETTER**
> You are learning the Measure as a tool. Mark +2 on your Measure track. How you use this learning in M3 and M4 will shape your gift.

> **A) Continue to Scene 9.** --> Scene 9

---


## SCENE M1_restrain — THE RESTRAINT

*Castle Brightholm East Gate*

You let it go. The guard is following his orders. The traveller leaves. Aldous nods slowly. 'Restraint is its own form of judgment,' he says. 'The Measure does not require you to intervene in everything. Knowing when not to act is as important as knowing when to act.' He pauses. 'The traveller will be fine. The guard will keep doing this. At some point you will have to decide whether that concerns you.'

> **MEASURE TRACK: +1 — RESTRAINT**
> Mark +1. Your path leans toward deliberate judgment over immediate action. This will matter at M3.

> **A) Continue to Scene 9.** --> Scene 9

---


## SCENE M1_ask — THE QUESTION

*Castle Brightholm East Gate*

The guard's reason: he was told the order means no exceptions and he does not want trouble. You let the traveller through. Then you tell the guard, simply: 'The order says third bell. Four minutes before the bell is before the bell.' You do not report him. You do not lecture him. Aldous says nothing for a while. Then: 'You asked why before you judged. Most people do it the other way around. Most of the time that is a mistake.'

> **MEASURE TRACK: +3 — THE QUESTION**
> Highest first-scene gain. Mark +3. You are learning the Measure through understanding, not just rule. This path is the hardest and the most useful.

> **A) Continue to Scene 9.** --> Scene 9

## SCENE 26 — THE SOUTH ROAD AMBUSH

*South Road — Day 1 of Exercise*

The south road is pine-scented and cold and then the treeline erupts. Three miles from Brightholm — close enough that you could still, if you strained, hear the morning bell — four Baaz Draconians come out of the trees with the businesslike certainty of a unit that has done this before and expects it to work. They cut off the road. They advance. No parley. Aldric's hand is on his sword hilt. So is yours, you notice, before you consciously decided.

> **Paladin Note: Before the Fight**
> If you are a Paladin: in the half-second before the draconians move, you hear something — a voice, barely there, like a command shouted across a great distance. It is one word. You cannot quite catch it. But your hand is already on your sword and you feel no fear. Mark 1 tally under KIRI-JOLITH (the god who steadies soldiers before battle).

> **COMBAT ENCOUNTER — DRAGON ARMY SCOUT PATROL**
>
> Setup: Four Baaz Draconians block the road. Aldric fights beside you.
>
> **ENEMIES:**
> • Baaz Draconian x4: AC 13, HP 18 each, Speed 30 ft.
> • Shortsword +3, 1d6+1 piercing. Or Javelin +3, range 30/120 ft., 1d6+1.
> • Death Throes: Turns to stone at 0 HP. DC 10 DEX save or restrained 1 min.
>
> **YOUR STATS THIS FIGHT:** Fighter: HP 12, AC 16, Longsword +5 1d8+3. Second Wind available. Aldric: AC 15, HP 14, +1 to your rolls. Paladin: HP 11, AC 16, Longsword +5 1d8+3. Lay on Hands pool available (bonus action). Divine Smite: bonus action spell after hit, 2d8 radiant, once per turn, 1 spell slot (at Level 2+).
>
> Enemy Tactics: Two draconians rush the closest target. Two hang back with javelins. Killing two causes the remaining two to spread rather than retreat.
>
> Fleeing: Disengage + Dash action. DC 12 Athletics or one free attack as you run.
>
> Rewards: 15 XP per draconian. Satchel on patrol leader: sealed dispatch pouch.
>
> Victory: Road clear. Aldric claps your shoulder. 'I did not expect that.' Proceed to Scene 27.
>
> Fallen (0 HP): 0 HP. Aldric drags you clear and stabilises you. Proceed to Scene 27 with 1 HP, one exhaustion.

> **BAAZ DRACONIAN (CR 1/2)** AC 13 | HP 18 | Speed 30 ft.
> Attacks: Shortsword +3, 1d6+1 piercing. Javelin +3, range 30/120 ft., 1d6+1 piercing.
> Special: Death Throes: Stone at 0 HP. Creature within 5 ft. DC 10 DEX save or restrained 1 min.

> **A) The draconians are stone. Continue to Scene 27.** --> Scene 27

---


## SCENE 27 — AFTER THE AMBUSH

*South Road*

Four Baaz, stone now. The dispatch pouch from the patrol leader bears a Black Wing seal. This is an advance element. They were mapping the road to the garrison. Aldric looks at you with a new calculation in his eyes.

> **TRACK YOUR HP**
> After the ambush: update your current HP on your sheet. Native PC starting HP: Fighter 12, Paladin 11. Each Baaz hit deals 1d6+1 (average 4). CPC: record any HP lost. Rest opportunity before Scene 27 if you need it.

> **LEVEL UP — YOU ARE NOW LEVEL 2**
> **Fighter:** Action Surge (one additional Action, except Magic action, 1/short or long rest). Tactical Mind (expend a Second Wind use to add 1d10 to a failed ability check; if you still fail, the use is not expended). Choose Subclass: Champion (Improved Critical 19–20, Remarkable Athlete), Battle Master (4 Superiority Dice d8, 3 manoeuvres), or Eldritch Knight (2 cantrips, 3 prepared 1st-level Wizard spells, 2 spell slots, War Bond).
> **Paladin:** Fighting Style feat (Dueling, Defence, Great Weapon Fighting, or Blessed Warrior). Paladin's Smite (cast Divine Smite once per long rest without expending a spell slot). Divine Smite is a bonus action spell: cast after hitting with a melee weapon, 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead), once per turn, 1 spell slot.
>
> HP: Native PC — Fighter: HP +7 (total 19). Paladin: HP +7 (total 18). CPC: add your Level 2 HP roll (1d10+CON) to your sheet.
>
> Record this on your character sheet before continuing.

> **PALADIN — DIVINE TRACK**
> Before making your choice below, Paladins turn to Scene P1 (The First Sign) now. It occurs this same night — you are on watch and something happens. After P1 and DG1, return here and choose your path forward.

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — THE WAYPOINT FIRE**
> The night after the ambush, on the road back: there is someone at the waypoint mile-marker who should not be there. If you want to investigate, turn to Scene 27B now. Scene 27B introduces Lysander Graves. It leads to Scene 36.

> **DARK SCENE — SCENE 32B**
> Scene 32B (What the Army Left Behind) is available now. It depicts what the Dragon Army did in the village of Thresh — you will find it before Scene 31. It leads to Scene 36. NOTE: Vael Ashmore appears in 32B.

> **E) Turn to Scene 32B now — what the army left in Thresh.** --> Scene 32B
>
> **A) Turn to Scene P1 now (Paladin).** --> Scene P1
>
> **B) Take the dispatch immediately to Lord Caeron.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 31
>
> **C) Read it yourself first.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 31
>
> **D) Hide it and find the nearest refugee camp.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44

## SCENE 27B — THE WAYPOINT FIRE

*South Road — Night After the Ambush*

You find him at the waypoint mile-marker, which the garrison uses for overnight stops on extended patrols. A fire, built well — the economical kind that throws heat in one direction and minimal light in every other, the fire of someone who knows what sees fire in the dark. A man sitting against the marker stone, cleaning a blade. He looks up when you approach without alarm, which means he heard you a hundred yards ago and decided you were not a threat.

The blade is not regulation. Solamnic steel, yes — you recognise the fuller line — but the grip has been rewrapped in dark leather, and the crossguard has been modified. The armour, too: Solamnic issue, Knight of the Sword markings half-filed and then left, as if the filing was an impulse he reconsidered or an argument he abandoned.

There are two dead Baaz Draconians at the tree line. They are very recently dead. He did this alone.

'You are from Brightholm,' he says. Not a question. He has seen your tabard. 'Squires.' He looks at Aldric, then at you, the assessment of a professional cataloguing what he is working with. 'How many did you fight today?' You tell him. Four. He nods. 'I had two. They are getting sloppy or I am getting faster. Both are bad signs, for different reasons.'

> **COMPANION JOINS: LYSANDER GRAVES**
> Knight of the Sword — technically. Currently operating as an independent. He is brilliant, charismatic, and carrying something he has not set down in years. Possible love interest — the dangerous kind.
> **Role:** Combat instructor: once per Act, Lysander teaches you a technique. +1 to your next attack roll after receiving instruction.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** The half-filed insignia. He started removing his Order markings and stopped. Not because he changed his mind about leaving — his body language is clear: he has left. He stopped filing because erasing it felt dishonest. He earned it. He does not want to serve under it. He does not want to pretend he never wore it. This is a man for whom honesty is the last principle standing, and he is holding onto it with both hands.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** He is a Knight, or was. He fights well. That is all you can read in the firelight.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

'Sit,' he says. 'The road is clear for two miles and I have more food than one person needs. That is not generosity — it is logistical efficiency. I stole it from a Dragon Army supply drop an hour ago and it is going to spoil.'

> **RATIONS — EVENING MEAL (Waypoint)**
> Lysander's stolen Dragon Army supplies cover tonight's meal. No personal ration consumed.

He eats the way soldiers eat — fast, without tasting it, the habit of someone who has been eating between things for long enough that meals have become fuel rather than events. Between bites he tells you, without being asked, that he has been on the south road for three weeks. Alone. He has killed more draconians in that time than most patrols. He has reported none of it because there is no one to report it to, or rather there is, but the report would involve explaining why he is here and who sent him and the answer to both is: no one.

**CONVICTION CHOICE (Lysander Corruption Track — Experience 1):**

> **A) 'You fight like a Knight of the Sword.' 'I fight like a man who was one.'** (+1 SWORD. CONVICTION: QUESTIONING — you have seen the skill without the system.) --> Scene 36
>
> **B) 'The half-filed insignia. You stopped.' 'I stopped.'** (+1 ROSE. CONVICTION: QUESTIONING — you have seen the conflict he carries.) --> Scene 36
>
> **C) 'You should report to the garrison. There is a chain of command.' He laughs — genuinely.** (+1 CROWN. CONVICTION: STEADFAST — you have asserted the system. He remembers you. The arc continues.) --> Scene 36
>
> **D) Say nothing. Share the fire.** (+1 ROSE. CONVICTION: QUESTIONING — you chose presence over judgment.) --> Scene 36

**ROMANCE CHOICE (optional — after conviction choice):**

> **R1) There is something about the firelight and the competence and the half-filed insignia. You notice him differently than you notice other people.** (ROMANCE SPARK Lysander)
>
> **R2) You share the fire. It is what it is.** (No romance.)

---


## PALADIN SCENE P1 — THE FIRST SIGN

*South Road — Night After the Ambush*

> **PALADIN ONLY**
> Fighters: skip to Scene 27 or wherever the story sends you next. Paladins: read this scene before continuing.

You are keeping watch after the ambush. The fire is low. Aldric is asleep. The night is ordinary in every way except one: the wound on your arm — a graze from a javelin you barely noticed during the fight — has stopped bleeding. You look at it in the firelight. The skin is closed. Not healed over days. Closed, as if it were a week old.

You did not do this. You do not have magic like this. Not yet. There is no spell, no prayer, nothing you can point to as a cause. Just: you were hurt, and now you are less hurt than you should be.

> **DIVINE SIGN**
> The wound is closed. The night is still. Somewhere very far away, something is paying attention to you. It does not feel like a threat. It does not feel like a gift either. It feels like: a gaze. Patient. Vast. Waiting to see what you do next.

You sit with this for a while. Then you decide what it means:

| PALADINE | KIRI-JOLITH | MISHAKAL | HABBAKUK | BRANCHALA |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ |
| Good/Law | War/Honour | Healing | Nature/Sea | Art/Inspiration |

> **A) A sign of protection from a god of good and law — silver light, a guardian's gaze.** Mark 1 tally: PALADINE. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene DG1
>
> **B) A sign from a god of battle — the warrior's body sustained so it can fight again.** Mark 1 tally: KIRI-JOLITH. (+1 SWORD) --> Scene DG1
>
> **C) A sign from a god of healing — the body made whole by something that values wholeness.** Mark 1 tally: MISHAKAL. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene DG1
>
> **D) A sign from a god of nature — living things mend; this is just that, applied.** Mark 1 tally: HABBAKUK. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene DG1
>
> **E) You are not sure what it means. Mark nothing. Carry the question.** (No tally. +1 ROSE for honest uncertainty.) --> Scene DG1

---


## SCENE DG1 — THE WHISPER IN THE WOUND

*South Road — Night After the Ambush (Paladin Only)*

> **PALADIN ONLY**
> This scene occurs the same night as P1. Read P1 first. Then read this. Fighters: skip to Scene 28.

The wound is closed. That is what you know. What you do not know is what closed it. You are sitting alone at the edge of the firelight when you first hear it — not a voice exactly, more like the shape a voice leaves behind. Something that knows your name and the weight of your ambitions and has been waiting for a moment when you were alone and questioning.

> **DARK TEMPTATION — TAKHISIS WHISPERS**
> You have been chosen. Not by your little gods of law and healing — by something older. Something that does not ask you to serve. That wound? I closed it. Not them. I saw what you could become and I preserved it. Your gods of good ask you to give. I offer you to take. The Dragon Armies will reshape this world. You could reshape them. One word is all it needs. One small yes.

> **A) Refuse. Directly, clearly, with the Oath. You know what this is.** (+2 to DG track: HELD, no effect on god tallies) --> Scene DG1_held
>
> **B) Refuse but you are shaken. The voice knew things.** (+1 DG track: HELD, -1 from your highest god tally — the doubt is real) --> Scene DG1_shaken
>
> **C) Ask who is speaking. Not agreement — but you engage with it.** (+1 DG track: LISTENING — mark this as your first step toward the fall) --> Scene DG1_listen
>
> **D) The wound is real. The help is real. You do not say yes — but you do not say no.** (DG track: COMPROMISED — mark this) --> Scene DG1_silent

---


## SCENE DG1_held — THE REFUSAL

*South Road — The Same Night*

The voice does not argue. It simply goes. That is what tells you it was real — a voice inside your head would have argued. This one left clean, the way things leave when they have been told no by someone who means it. You sit with the silence for a while. It smells of cold pine and the road and something faintly metallic that might be the aftermath of a divine voice or might just be the night air near a weapon.

> **DG TRACK: HELD**
> You have refused the first temptation cleanly. Mark HELD on your God Sign notes. This choice compounds — each refusal makes the next easier.

> **A) Continue to Scene 28.** --> Scene 28

---


## SCENE DG1_shaken — THE SHAKEN REFUSAL

*South Road — The Same Night*

You said no. That matters. But it knew your name. It knew about the ambition you have not told anyone — the one that lives just under the dedication, the one that might be what actually drives you. You cannot sleep. Somewhere between watch changes you make yourself say the Oath aloud, quietly, to no one. Just to hear it in your own voice. Just to check it is still yours.

> **DG TRACK: HELD (SHAKEN)**
> You refused, but the temptation landed. Reduce your highest god tally by 1 — the doubt is real. The Dark Queen will find the crack next time.

> **A) Continue to Scene 28.** --> Scene 28

---


## SCENE DG1_listen — THE FIRST STEP

*South Road — The Same Night*

You asked. The voice told you: Someone who sees what you are capable of. Then it went quiet, not because you refused it but because it had planted what it wanted to plant. You will think about this in the morning. You will tell yourself you were just gathering information. You will almost believe it.

> **DG TRACK: LISTENING ■**
> You engaged. This is not a fall — yet. But Takhisis does not need agreement. She needs attention. You have given her yours. Mark LISTENING. If you reach FALLEN by DG3 without recovery, your divine abilities are affected.

> **A) Continue to Scene 28.** --> Scene 28

---


## SCENE DG1_silent — THE SILENT COMPROMISE

*South Road — The Same Night*

You did not say yes. But you let the silence be the answer, and the voice heard that silence the way it was listening for — not as refusal. In the morning the wound is still closed and you are still yourself and the world is still the same world. Almost.

> **DG TRACK: COMPROMISED ■■**
> Silence was acceptance enough. Mark COMPROMISED. Your Lay on Hands pool is reduced by 2 HP until you find recovery. The connection to your true god has been partially muffled.

> **A) Continue to Scene 28.** --> Scene 28

---

*End of Act One.*

# ACT TWO: THE FIELD EXERCISE (LEVEL 2)

## Act Two Overview

The field exercise has become something far more serious. The 'bandits' are refugees. The Dragon Army has a scout presence within two hours. Scenes 28-52 cover the refugee crisis, a major command decision, two more combat encounters, and the aftermath that defines your Order path. Paladins: Paladin Scene P2 is in Act Two.

---


## SCENE 28 — WHAT CAERON LOOKS FOR

*Castle Brightholm — Armoury*

'Someone who can hold two truths at once — that the law matters and that people matter more. Most can only hold one.'

He says it the way someone says a thing they have thought about very carefully and arrived at through experience rather than reading. You have the sense that this answer cost him something — that there was a version of Lord Caeron Ashvale who could only hold one truth at a time, and the version in front of you is the result of learning, painfully, to hold two.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> He meets your eyes with unusual directness. 'Ask me something harder.'

> **A) 'What do you do when your orders conflict with your conscience?'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 29
>
> **B) 'What made you a knight rather than a lord?'** (+1 ROSE, Caeron backstory) --> Scene 29
>
> **C) Thank him and leave.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 11_MORNING

---


## SCENE 29 — CAERON'S ANSWER

*Castle Brightholm — Armoury*

He says it when he thinks you are not watching — which means he says it when he thinks the conversation is over and the thing he was holding back while it was not over can now be safely set down. 'I became a knight because being a lord meant staying behind walls when the bad things came.' A pause while he examines the hilt of his sword. 'I have not always been correct about what constitutes a bad thing. That is something I have had to learn at intervals. I prefer not to keep learning it.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (WIS, proficiency if trained) (+1) | WIS | DC 15
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 15+):** He is describing a specific incident, not a general philosophy. There is a moment in his past where he made a command decision he still questions — not the same as Aldous's, but adjacent. If you note this and ask carefully in a later scene, he will tell you what it was.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-14):** He is speaking generally. The history behind the words is not visible.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Leave quietly.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_MORNING
>
> **B) 'I think you are more correct about it than you believe.'** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE SPARK Caeron) --> Scene 11_MORNING

---


## SCENE 30 — WHO IS CAERON

*Castle Brightholm*

Third son of a minor noble house, passed over for inheritance. Became a knight because there was nothing else and found out he was exceptional at it. His house considers knighthood beneath them. He considers them beneath the Measure.

What you piece together: the armour he wears is paid for out of his own salary, not the family estate. The saddle on his horse is older than most of the garrison squires. He does not mention his family. No one who knows him mentions it either — which tells you something about how that subject was closed. A man who chose this life at real cost, and will not let it be anything less than exactly what it should be.

> **A) This makes you respect him differently. You carry the knowledge back into the afternoon, aware that the garrison looks slightly different now you know who built it.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON
>
> **B) This makes you understand him. There is a difference. The afternoon continues, but you see Caeron's clipboard differently now.** (+1 CROWN, ROMANCE SPARK Caeron) --> Scene 11_AFTERNOON

---


## SCENE 31 — THE HIGH JUSTICE ARRIVES

*South Road Camp — Day 2*

> **DRAGONLANCE CAMEO — LORD GUNTHAR UTH WISTAN**
> The High Justice who arrives with the decree is Lord Gunthar uth Wistan, Grand Master of the Knights of Solamnia. He is a man of genuine honour caught between the law he serves and the world that law was written for, and they are no longer the same world.

He rides in with six escort soldiers and the expression of a man carrying something heavy that he did not choose to carry. The decree is formal — sealed, High Justice mark, legally binding and structurally unambiguous. He reads it out in the field camp: The refugee group is to be turned back south. Roads must remain clear for military movement. Crown law overrides field commander discretion. Thirty people. Families. Two wounded from yesterday. The Dragon Army, on a map, is approximately one day south of where they will be sent.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Persuasion (+0) | CHA | DC 15
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 15+):** You find wording in the decree permitting a 24-hour field assessment delay. Caeron approves. The refugees have time. +2 ROSE, +1 CROWN.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-14):** The decree is airtight. You must choose: comply or refuse.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — THE OBSERVER**
> A woman arrived with Lord Gunthar's escort who is not part of it. If you want to meet her, turn to Scene 31B (The Observer) now. Scene 31B introduces Tariel Duskmantle.

> **PALADIN — DARK TEMPTATION TRACK**
> Tonight, Takhisis speaks again. Before making your choice below, Paladins with the DG track active turn to Scene DG2 (The Offer) now.

> **A) Comply. The decree is the law.** (+3 CROWN, refugees turned back) --> Scene 46
>
> **B) Ask Caeron privately if he believes it is right.** (+2 ROSE, Caeron's mask cracks) --> Scene 47
>
> **C) Refuse outright.** (+3 ROSE, formal reprimand — they live) --> Scene 48
>
> **D) Use the dispatch pouch from Scene 27 as leverage.** (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 49

---


## SCENE 31B — THE OBSERVER

*South Road Camp — Day of the High Justice's Arrival*

She arrives with Lord Gunthar's escort, though she is clearly not part of it — positioned at the rear, riding a civilian horse, wearing no insignia. Her credential, when Caeron examines it with the unhurried scepticism he brings to all documents, identifies her as a diplomatic observer from the eastern provinces, authorised by the Council of Whitestone to monitor Solamnic field operations during the current crisis. The credential is genuine. Caeron's expression when he hands it back suggests he wishes it were not.

Tariel Duskmantle dismounts with the easy competence of someone who has been in considerably more militarised situations than this and adjusted to each of them within the hour. She surveys the camp — not the defences, which she clearly assessed on approach, but the people. How they stand. How they respond to Gunthar's presence. How the squires look at the knights and the knights look at the decree and the decree looks at the refugees and no one is looking at the same thing.

Then she looks at you. Not past you to Aldric, or through you to Caeron. At you. With the particular attention of someone who has identified the interesting person in the room and intends to have a conversation with them whether they like it or not.

> **COMPANION JOINS: TARIEL DUSKMANTLE**
> Diplomatic observer. She is watching everything. She will share her observations if you engage with them — and her observations will make you uncomfortable.
> **Role:** Political intelligence: +1 to any Persuasion or Insight check involving authority figures if you consult her first.

'The decree,' she says, when she finds you after the reading. No preamble. 'Thirty people sent south into the path of the army that displaced them. The Measure permits this?'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Persuasion (CHA) (+0) | CHA | DC 14
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 14+):** You articulate a response that accounts for the Measure's tension between law and protection. +1 to all future Tariel interactions.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-13):** 'The standard answer,' she says, without contempt.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

**CONVICTION CHOICE (Tariel Corruption Track — Debate 1):**

> **A) 'The Measure does not permit it. The decree does. There is a difference.'** (+2 ROSE. CONVICTION: QUESTIONING) --> Scene 31
>
> **B) 'The Measure is imperfect. All law is imperfect. That does not make it worthless.'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN. CONVICTION: STEADFAST) --> Scene 31
>
> **C) 'You are right. The Measure failed those people. I do not know how to reconcile that.'** (+1 ROSE. CONVICTION: SHAKEN. -1 to your highest Order tally.) --> Scene 31
>
> **D) 'You are an observer. Observe.'** (+1 CROWN. CONVICTION: STEADFAST.) --> Scene 31

**ROMANCE CHOICE (optional — after conviction choice, if you chose A or C):**

> **R1) Hold her gaze a moment longer than the argument requires.** (ROMANCE SPARK Tariel)
>
> **R2) Do not.** (No romance.)

---


## SCENE DG2 — THE OFFER

*Field Camp — Night of the Refugee Decree (Paladin Only)*

> **PALADIN ONLY**
> This scene triggers after Scene 31 (The High Justice Arrives), on the night before you must act on the decree. Fighters: skip to Scene 36.

Thirty people. The decree in one hand. The Measure in the other. Tomorrow you will have to choose — follow the law that is supposed to protect people but tonight is asking you to destroy them, or break it. You are still awake at the second watch when the voice returns. It sounds different this time. Patient. Almost kind.

> **DARK TEMPTATION — TAKHISIS WHISPERS — THE SWEET OFFER**
> You see the problem with your little code? The law is wrong and you know it and you have to obey anyway or break it and be punished. I am offering you a third path. Serve me — just this once — and those thirty people live. I will arrange it. No one will be punished. The decree will be satisfied. The refugees will disappear from the road in a way no one questions. All it costs is this: you carry my mark. Just a small one. No one will know but you.

> **A) No. You will find your own way to protect them, inside the Measure or outside it. The answer is no.** (+2 DG: HELD FIRM) --> Scene DG2_held
>
> **B) No — but you ask how she would arrange it. Just information.** (+1 DG: LISTENING, if already LISTENING this becomes COMPROMISED) --> Scene DG2_listen
>
> **C) You ask for a day to think.** (DG: COMPROMISED — she hears this as yes) --> Scene DG2_delay
>
> **D) You accept. The refugees will be safe. That is what matters.** (DG: FALLEN — your Lay on Hands heals, but the healing feels wrong) --> Scene DG2_fall

---


## SCENE DG2_held — THE REFUSAL — SECOND TIME

*Field Camp — The Same Night*

The voice goes. You are alone with the decree and thirty people and no clean answer. This is what the Measure does not account for — the moments when the law fails the people it was written to protect and you are the only person standing between them. You will figure it out yourself. That is the point of the oath. Not to be given the answer. To find it.

> **DG TRACK: HELD FIRM ✓**
> Second refusal. Your connection to your god strengthens. +1 to your highest god tally (faith proved under pressure).

> **A) Continue to Scene 36.** --> Scene 36

---


## SCENE DG2_listen — THE QUESTION

*Field Camp — The Same Night*

She tells you. Casually, as if the answer costs her nothing. The refugees would simply... find another road. One that leads somewhere safe. The decree would be satisfied by their absence from this road specifically. It is, technically, not wrong. You catch yourself thinking: that is actually clever. Then you catch yourself having thought that. You say no. But later.

> **DG TRACK: LISTENING DEEPENS ■**
> You are reasoning with a dark god. This is dangerous. If already LISTENING: mark COMPROMISED. If first LISTENING: stay at LISTENING but -1 to any one god tally.

> **A) Continue to Scene 36.** --> Scene 36

---


## SCENE DG2_delay — THE DELAY

*Field Camp — The Same Night*

She takes your pause as what it was — consideration. By morning the refugees are gone from the road. Quietly, without your involvement. The decree is technically satisfied. You did not agree. You just did not say no in time. That distinction matters. It also does not matter at all. Your Lay on Hands heals. The healing feels the same. You test it three times to be sure.

> **DG TRACK: COMPROMISED ■■**
> She acted on your silence. The debt is recorded even if you didn't sign it. Your Lay on Hands pool is reduced by 3 HP. You are aware of a faint wrongness when you use it.

> **A) Continue to Scene 36.** --> Scene 36

---


## SCENE DG2_fall — THE FIRST FALL

*Field Camp — The Same Night*

The refugees are safe. You told yourself that is what matters. You still believe this. But there is something different about the divine warmth in your hands now — not absent, not cold, but filtered. As if it is coming through something. The healing works. The prayers feel answered. But there is a quality to the answer that is new and you cannot quite name what the quality is.

> **DG TRACK: FALLEN ■■■**
> You have accepted the Dark Queen's help with full awareness. This is recoverable — but only through Scene DG4 (The Reckoning). Until recovery: Lay on Hands heals half normal HP (round up). Divine Smite does full damage but leaves a faint shadow-bruise on targets. Your god tallies are frozen until you recover.

> **A) Continue to Scene 36.** --> Scene 36

---


## SCENE 32B — WHAT THE ARMY LEFT BEHIND

*South Road — Abandoned Village of Thresh, Day 2*

> **VAEL ASHMORE**
> Vael Ashmore is already here. If you have not read Scene 5B, this is where you meet her. She was scouting ahead. She found this first. She has been standing here for a while.

You smell it before you see it. Woodsmoke that has been burning too long. The village of Thresh is eight buildings around a well and it is mostly still standing, which is worse than if it had burned. What the Dragon Army did here did not require fire.

> **DARK SCENE — This scene contains depictions of war atrocities.**

There are bodies. The Dragon Army did not take prisoners here — or they took some and left the rest as a message. The message is: this is what happens when you do not comply quickly enough. The village elder is still at his table. The door is still open. Someone's dog is still waiting outside a house whose occupants are not coming back. The well has been fouled. This was not a battle. This was an afternoon's work.

There is one survivor. An old woman sitting behind the mill, uninjured, who watched from there and who has not spoken since.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> Vael does not cry in front of you. Later — when you make camp and she thinks you are asleep — you hear her. It is brief and very quiet and when it stops she is silent for a long time. You do not tell her you heard. But in the morning you make sure you are the one who brings her water, and she takes it without looking at you, and that is also a kind of closeness.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Investigation (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** Four days ago — but the supplies show three days of consumption after the army passed. Some people survived the initial visit and stayed or left afterward. The casualty count is lower than it first appears.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** The village shows you what happened. You cannot read more than the obvious.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Bury the dead before you move on.** (+2 ROSE, Vael looks at you differently. ROMANCE FLAME Vael if Spark active) --> Scene 36
>
> **B) Get the survivor moving north.** (+1 SWORD, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 36
>
> **C) Find something to mark the place.** (+1 ROSE, +1 ROSE — you remember it.) --> Scene 36
>
> **D) Report the coordinates to Caeron. Document it precisely. This is evidence.** (+2 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 36

---


## SCENE 34B — WHAT SCOUTS DO BEFORE A MARCH

*Field Camp — Night Before Moving the Column*

The watch at midnight has its own texture: coals where the fire was, stars very bright, the camp breathing in the slow rhythm of people genuinely asleep. Sera finds you here not because she was assigned this post but because she walked the perimeter and here is where she ended up. She sits a foot away and does not speak for a while.

She has been doing reconnaissance on the south road and what she found she has already reported. What she has not reported is what it did to her. She has the flat stillness of someone who has been holding something at arm's length all day and is now, in the dark, letting themselves feel the weight.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> She does not ask for anything. She is simply — present. Near you. After a while her shoulder finds yours and stays there. That is all. It is not nothing.

> **A) Stay still. Let her have the silence she came here for.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Sera if Spark active) --> Scene 51
>
> **B) Ask quietly: 'What did you find out there?'** (+1 ROSE, she tells you something she told no one else) --> Scene 51
>
> **C) Cover her hand with yours for a moment. No words.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Sera — she goes very still, then turns her palm up) --> Scene 51

---


## SCENE 36 — WOUND AND TRUST

*South Road — Abandoned Barn, Night*

The barn smells of old hay and damp and the copper-salt note of a wound managed without proper materials. You work by lantern light. Serath watches you work with the careful attention of someone building a file on you in real time. They do not speak while you work. When it is done: 'You did not have to do that.' Not gratitude. Not manipulation. An honest observation.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Medicine (+1) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** Clean technique. Serath will be mobile by morning. +1 to all Serath trust checks.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** Adequate work. They will be slow for two days.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> 'You could still report me,' Serath says. 'I want you to know I understand that.' Not manipulation. Just honesty.

> **A) 'I know. I am not going to.'** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Serath if Spark active) --> Scene 50
>
> **B) 'I have not decided yet. But I treated the wound first.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 50
>
> **C) 'Tell me something the Dragon Army is planning. For the people in its path.'** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 50

---


## SCENE 36B — LYSANDER'S PHILOSOPHY

*South Road — Camp, Night (Conditional: Lysander in party)*

> **CONDITIONAL SCENE**
> This scene occurs only if Lysander Graves is in your party.

He finds you at the edge of the firelight. He is sitting on a rock with his modified sword across his knees and the stillness of someone who has been sitting like this for years and has stopped noticing the cold.

'Let me ask you something,' he says. 'The man with the barrel-stave splint. At the refugee column. You saw him try to stand at attention when he saw the tabard.' You nod. 'Why did he do that?'

'No,' he says. 'He did it because three hundred years of Solamnic presence taught civilians that the tabard means safety. And it did, once. Before the Cataclysm, before the Order turned inward, before the Measure became a text people quote instead of a thing people do.' He is not angry. That is the dangerous part. He is calm. 'The man stood at attention for a symbol. You — specifically you — chose to live up to it. The institution chose to send him south.'

'I am not saying the Oath is worthless,' he says. 'I am saying it is insufficient. I am saying a good person does not need it to do the right thing, and a bad person will not be stopped by it. I am saying the Measure is beautiful and I loved it and it told me to let people drown. I did not let them drown. The Measure told me I was wrong. Which of us do you believe?'

**CONVICTION CHOICE (Lysander Corruption Track — Experience 2):**

> **A) 'I believe you. And I believe the Measure. Both at the same time.'** (+2 ROSE. CONVICTION: remains at current level.) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) 'The Measure was wrong. You were right. But walking away means no one fixes it from inside.'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN. CONVICTION: remains or improves toward STEADFAST.) --> Scene 44
>
> **C) 'You asked me which I believe — you or the Measure. I believe you.'** (+1 ROSE, -1 CROWN. CONVICTION: advances one step toward FALLEN.) --> Scene 44
>
> **D) 'The Oath exists because individual judgment is not enough.' He walks away.** (+2 CROWN. CONVICTION: STEADFAST. Romance cools.) --> Scene 44
>
> **E) 'I do not know. I am a squire who has been at this for three weeks. But I am listening.'** (+1 ROSE. CONVICTION: QUESTIONING.) --> Scene 44

**ROMANCE CHOICE (optional — if at SPARK or higher):**

> **R1) The dark and the fire and the honesty have created something. Lean into it.** (ROMANCE FLAME Lysander)
>
> **R2) Keep the distance.** (Romance holds.)

---


## SCENE 37 — PROOF OF DEFECTION

*Abandoned Barn*

Serath gives you the patrol schedules by drawing them — a grid in the dirt with a stick, the specific rotations that tell you where the Dragon Army pickets are and more importantly where the gaps are.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Investigation (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** The patrol schedules are genuine. But there is something else: the description of Commander Hestrix's seal matches what is on the dispatch pouch from Scene 27 exactly. Serath knew about that pouch before you mentioned it.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** The information checks out.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Enough. Treat the wound and hide them.** (Serath joins, ROMANCE SPARK possible) --> Scene 36
>
> **B) Use the information but turn them in.** (Intelligence gained, Serath captured) --> Scene 39

## SCENE 38 — ALDRIC AND THE QUESTION

*South Road*

He has been quiet since the barn. Now he asks: 'What do you want to do?' Not: what does protocol say. Not: what would Caeron decide. What do you want.

> **A) 'Hide them.'** (+1 ROSE, Aldric nods. Serath joins) --> Scene 36
>
> **B) 'Report them.'** (+2 CROWN, Aldric nods.) --> Scene 39
>
> **C) 'I honestly do not know.'** (+1 ROSE, Aldric chooses to hide them) --> Scene 36

## SCENE 39 — THE REPORT

*Garrison*

You report Serath. They are detained. Lord Caeron commends your adherence to protocol. The paperwork is filed. The garrison moves on.

You think about the village they described. You think about the way they said it — flat precision, no performance of grief, worse than if they had been crying. You hear later they survived captivity and escaped three months after.

> **A) You made the right call by the law.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) It sits poorly.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 40 — THE EASTERN APPROACH

*South Road — Treeline*

You reach the ridge by midmorning. The treeline here is old growth — pine and ash, light coming through in long diagonals. Below: not bandits. A camp. Cooking fires. The smell of something being boiled. Children. There are perhaps thirty people. None of them look like bandits. All of them look frightened.

> **A) Observe before descending.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Descend and approach openly.** (+1 SWORD, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 40B — THE STORM

*South Road — Field Exercise, Day 2*

The storm comes from the west with the particular speed that storms have when they are not interested in your schedule. One hour of grey sky, then thirty minutes of wind that turns the treeline into a sound you have never heard trees make, then rain that is not rain so much as a quantity of water that has decided to be somewhere lower and does not care what is in the way.

Aldric has his back against a pine and his arms folded with the focused patience of someone who has decided that being wet is a temporary condition he refuses to acknowledge. Mira, if present, is already working — redistributing supplies with calm efficiency. Caeron stands in the rain without appearing to notice it.

**IF TARIEL IS IN YOUR PARTY:** 'The rain is useful — it reveals who adapts and who endures. Both are valuable. The Knights of Solamnia, in my experience, default to endure.'

**IF LYSANDER IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He appears from the treeline with dry deadwood gathered before the rain started. He builds a fire with offhand competence. 'The garrison teaches you to endure discomfort. I have found it more useful to eliminate discomfort and save the enduring for things that actually require it.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Survival (WIS) (+1) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** This will pass in ninety minutes. The treeline ridge path will dry faster than the road.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** The storm is a storm. You endure it.

> **A) Endure. Stand in the rain with Caeron.** (+1 CROWN, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Adapt. Help Mira redistribute supplies.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **C) Build shelter.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 44
>
> **D) (If Lysander present) Join Lysander at the fire.** (+1 SWORD, -1 CROWN) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 41 — THE DIRECT APPROACH

*South Road*

The direct road means you are visible from half a mile. You watch them see you. A cluster of adults moves without discussion, putting themselves between the children and your approach. Then one of them sees the tabard — the Solamnic sun — and says something low to the group, and the posture changes. An elderly woman starts crying with the specific relief of someone who has been holding something for too long.

> **A) Identify yourself and explain the routine exercise.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Ask them where they have come from. Let them talk first.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 42 — THE WEST BANK

*South Road — River Ford*

Three farmsteads on the west bank, recently abandoned. Not weeks — days. Tables still set for a meal that was not finished. A child's wooden horse on the floor near the hearth.

> **You Learn:** The Dragon Army has already crossed the river at least once.

> **A) Take the boot prints evidence and head back to the road. On the way, you pass the refugee column — you cannot avoid it.** (+2 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Proceed to the refugee camp with this information.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 43 — THE SPLIT

*South Road*

You come up the ridge from the east and find Aldric already there. He has a Baaz Draconian bound at the wrists.

> **COMBAT ENCOUNTER — THE DETAINED SCOUT**
> One wounded Baaz breaks free. You fight alone for 2 rounds before Aldric arrives.
>
> **ENEMIES:** Baaz Draconian: AC 13, HP 14 (wounded), Speed 30 ft.
>
> Enemy Tactics: It tries to disengage and run. If it escapes (not downed in 3 rounds) the patrol arrives early in Scene 44.
>
> Rewards: 5 XP. Aldric arrives just after.
>
> Fallen (0 HP): Aldric arrives to finish the fight. 1 HP and one exhaustion.

> **ADD TO INVENTORY — DRAGON ARMY PATROL SKETCH**
> From the detained draconian: a hide map of patrol routes. Show this to Caeron: +1 bonus to the Scene 52 defensive position check.

> **A) Report the scout to Caeron.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Continue to the refugee camp immediately.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 44

---


## SCENE 44 — THE REFUGEE COLUMN

*South Road — Day of Exercise*

The waystation is the skeleton of a building — three walls standing, the fourth a pile of useful stone. Thirty-one people in a space meant for one night's passing have been here for three days. Three children. Eight elderly. A man with a barrel-stave splint.

When they see you, the able-bodied step forward and the children are moved to the back. Then the man with the splint tries to stand at attention when he sees the Solamnic tabard.

**IF VAEL IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Vael is already here. She scouted ahead and is standing very still at the edge of the column. 'I counted. Thirty-one. Three children. We have to do something.' Not a suggestion. A fact about who she is.

**IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Sera has been scouting ahead. She gives you the tactical picture: patrol distances, terrain cover, the window you have. 'You have about four hours,' she says. 'Use them.' +1 to the Perception roll.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Perception (+2) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** Scout still half a mile back. All options available without time pressure.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** Patrol is closer than you thought. Options B and C cost one extra round.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — THE WAYSTATION**
> There is someone inside who should not be here. Turn to Scene 18 (The Stranger in the Barn).

> **OPTIONAL NIGHT SCENE — SCENE 34B**
> If you met Sera in Scene 3B: turn to Scene 34B now.

> **A) Report and wait for garrison orders.** (+2 CROWN) --> Scene 44_REPORT
>
> **B) Move them north yourself, now.** (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 44_REPORT
>
> **C) Set a defensive position. Hold scouts while they move.** (+2 SWORD, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 44_REPORT
>
> **D) Find Caeron first.** (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 44_REPORT
>
> **E) (Hidden choice — only if you look) The dead.** There are two bodies at the edge of the column, covered with blankets. An old man who did not survive the march. A woman who carried her child until her body gave out — the child is alive, being held by a stranger now. Their belongings are beside them: a pack, a water skin, a pouch that might contain steel. No one is guarding the dead. Everyone is watching you.
>
> **E1) Take what they carried.** You are taking from refugees who died on a road fleeing the army that is burning their homes. There is no version of this that the Measure permits. There is no version that any god, old or new, endorses. **-3 ROSE, -3 CROWN, -2 SWORD. CORRUPTION: QUESTIONING on one active corruption track.** The pack contains: 1d4 stl, 3 days rations, a wooden toy (the child's — worthless in steel, invaluable in meaning). Aldric sees you do it. He does not speak to you for the remainder of the field exercise. Mira, if present: 'I walked this road to help people. I am watching you rob the dead in front of their families. I need you to understand what I am seeing.' She does not leave. The fact that she stays is worse.
> **E2) No. Walk away.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN. You did not take from the dead. That should not feel like an accomplishment but the fact that you hesitated means it is.)

---


## SCENE 44B — THE OLD RUINS

*South Road — Between the Column and the March, Day 2*

There is a ruin on the ridge that the garrison maps mark as 'Solamnic watchtower (inactive).' The walls are chest-high. The archway is intact. Someone carved Est Sularus oth Mithas into the keystone at a date you can identify by the letter forms as pre-Cataclysmic.

Inside: grass growing through flagstones. A fire pit long cold. And carved into the inner wall at about knee height, a child's handprint in mud, dried hard. Someone sheltered here on the way north. Someone very young left their mark because that is what very young people do when they are in a place they will not come back to.

> **Paladin Note:**
> The Est Sularus oth Mithas carved in the keystone warms when you pass under the archway. Not the stone — the words themselves. Mark 1 tally under PALADINE or KIRI-JOLITH.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** History (INT) (+0) | INT | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** This was a Solamnic chapter house. Before the Cataclysm, one of hundreds. Now it is grass and stone and the handprint of a child.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** Old ruin. Old words.

> **A) Touch the handprint.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Read the keystone aloud.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 44
>
> **C) Make camp here for the night.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **D) Wait. There are fresh bootprints in the fire pit. Someone has been here recently — and they were not refugees.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 44C

---


## SCENE 44C — THE RUINS AT NIGHT

*South Road — Old Watchtower Ruins, Night*

You wait. Aldric waits with you because that is what Aldric does — he does not question it, he simply crouches beside you in the dark and matches your breathing to the silence. The bootprints in the fire pit were military. Hobnailed. Heavier than refugee sandals. And they went deeper into the ruin, toward the collapsed cellar that the garrison maps do not show.

The moon is a sliver. The wind carries the smell of old stone and something else — smoke, very faint, from below the ruin. Someone has a fire in the cellar. Someone who does not want to be seen from the road.

You hear the voice before you see the light. Not Common. Not Solamnic. A language that clicks and hisses and makes the hair on your arms stand up. Then: a child's voice. Small. Frightened. Speaking Common in fragments: 'Please. I want to go home. Please.'

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run the encounter at your table, then skip to **AFTER THE FIGHT**.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow the rounds below. Roll when prompted.

> **INJURED NPC — REFUGEE CHILD LINNA**
> Age 8. Dehydration + fever. Captured by Dragon Army foragers using the ruins as a supply cache.
> **Heal her:** Mira (if present, automatic — herbs + care), Paladin Cure Wounds (1 spell slot), Paladin Lay on Hands (from pool), Bandage + water (stabilize, but fever needs herbs or magic), Potion of Healing (2d4+2 HP, cures fever).
> *Record any resources spent.*
> **If healed:** Linna recovers. She is returned to the refugee column or carried north. She appears in Vogler (Scene 70B) — she and her family recognize you. +2 ROSE.
> **If not healed:** Linna survives the night but the fever worsens. She reaches Vogler but is bedridden. The family does not know who found her.

> **COMPANION SELECTION**
> Aldric is with you automatically. Choose up to 2 additional companions:
> **Vael** — Reveals the Kapak's poison ability before combat. 'The one with the dark scales — its blade is coated. Do not let it cut you.'
> **Thessaly** — +1 to all saving throws vs poison. She identified the antidote herbs in her research. Also +1 ROSE after the fight (she documents Linna's rescue).
> **Mira** — Heals Linna automatically. Carries herbs that break the fever.
> **Sera** — Stealth approach. If present, your Stealth DC is reduced by 2.
> **Serath** — Knows Dragon Army patrol patterns. Warns you of timing: 'We have fifteen minutes before the next rotation.'

> **ENEMY STAT BLOCKS (Pen & Paper)**
> **Human Soldier (2):** AC 14 (chain shirt + shield), HP 14, Speed 30ft. Longsword +4 (1d8+2). Javelin +4 (1d6+2, 30/120). Formation: +1 AC when adjacent to another soldier.
> **Kapak Draconian:** AC 14 (natural), HP 26, Speed 30ft. Poisoned Shortsword +5 (1d6+3 + DC 11 CON save or 1d6 poison and poisoned condition for 1 round). Claw +5 (1d4+3). Lick Blade (bonus action, re-poisons weapon). Death Throes: dissolves into acid pool (5ft radius, 2d4 acid damage, DC 12 DEX to avoid).

> **STEALTH APPROACH:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14 (DC 12 if Sera present)
> **SUCCESS:** Surprise round. You attack before they know you are there. One free attack with advantage.
> **FAILURE:** They hear you. No surprise. The Kapak hisses and draws its blade. The soldiers form up. Linna screams.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 1

The cellar is lit by a single low fire. Three figures: two humans in patchwork armour — Dragon Army regulars, not elite, the kind that hold supply lines and guard things that matter — and something else. The Kapak is crouched by the far wall, running its tongue along a short blade with the slow, deliberate care of a thing that is tasting its own poison. Its scales are dark, almost black, and its eyes reflect the firelight like a cat's.

Linna is tied to a support beam. She is small and filthy and her eyes are enormous. She sees you and her mouth opens but no sound comes out. She has learned that sound brings attention and attention brings pain.

**IF STEALTH SUCCEEDED:** They do not see you. The moment is yours. Take it.

> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC (Soldiers: 14, Kapak: 14)
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus. (Advantage if stealth succeeded — roll twice, take higher.)
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **IF VAEL IS PRESENT:** 'The Kapak's poison lasts one round. If it cuts you, disengage and let it fade. Do not panic.' (You know to expect the poison — tactical advantage.)

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:**
> **Aldric:** A) Flank (+1 next attack) | B) Shield Wall — blocks the cellar entrance (+1 AC, enemies cannot flee) | C) Aggressive Strike (1d8+2, takes 1d4)
> **Vael:** A) Flanking Shot (1d6 dmg) | B) Honest Assessment — reveals Kapak's remaining HP | C) Cover Fire (+1 AC)
> **Thessaly:** A) Encourage (+1 next roll) | B) Document (+1 ROSE after fight) | C) Distraction — she calls out in Draconic, the Kapak hesitates (enemy skips next attack)
> **Mira:** A) Rush to Linna — begins healing immediately | B) Herbal Boost (+1 save vs poison) | C) Bandage Linna (stabilize)
> **Sera:** A) Scout Shot (1d6 dmg) | B) Mark Target (+2 next attack) | C) Block retreat route (enemies cannot flee)
> **Serath:** A) Intel (+2 one attack) | B) Dagger Strike (1d4+2 from the shadows) | C) Feint (enemy -1 next attack)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):**
> • (Paladin) Cast Bless: +1d4 to attacks and saves for up to 3 targets, Concentration, lasts entire combat. 1 spell slot.
> • (Paladin) Divine Smite: Bonus action after hitting with a melee weapon. 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). Once per turn. 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest at level 2+).
> • (Paladin) Lay on Hands: Heal self or Linna. Bonus action.
> • (Paladin) Cure Wounds: Heal Linna 2d8+CHA. 1 spell slot. Replaces attack.
> • (Fighter) Action Surge: Additional Action this round (except Magic). 1/short or long rest.
> • (Fighter) Second Wind: 1d10+[level] HP. Bonus action. 2 uses/long rest, regain 1/short rest.
> • (Any) Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action.
> • (Any) Use Antitoxin: Advantage on poison saves for 1 hour. Bonus action.

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 1

The Kapak moves first. It is faster than the humans, faster than something that size should be, and it comes at you low — beneath your guard, blade leading. The poison on the shortsword glistens in the firelight, wet and dark.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (Kapak):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15
> **SUCCESS:** You evade. The blade passes close enough to smell — bitter, chemical, wrong.
> **FAILURE:** 1d6+3 slashing damage. **POISON:** CON save DC 11. **Failure:** +1d6 poison damage and poisoned (disadvantage on attacks and ability checks) until end of your next turn. **Success:** Half poison damage, not poisoned.
> **IF THESSALY IS PRESENT:** +1 to CON save. She told you what to expect.
>
> **DEFENSE ROLL (Soldier):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS:** The longsword clangs off your armour.
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+2 slashing damage.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 2

The cellar is too small for this. The fire throws shadows that multiply everyone — you are fighting six enemies instead of three, or that is what your eyes tell you. The Kapak licks its blade again, a gesture that is both practical and theatrical, and the soldiers press you toward the wall. They are trained. Not well, but enough. Formation fighting: one attacks while the other defends.

Linna has her eyes closed. She is not watching. She has decided that if she cannot see, it is not happening.

> **ATHLETICS CHECK (optional, replaces attack):** Roll 1d20 + STR modifier | DC 13
> Cut Linna's bonds. She can crawl to safety behind Aldric's shield wall.
> **SUCCESS:** Linna is free. She runs behind the nearest cover. If Mira is present, Mira pulls her to safety.
> **FAILURE:** The bonds are thick rope. You need another round or a blade.

> **YOUR ATTACK:** (if not freeing Linna)
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options as Round 1)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options as Round 1)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 2

The second soldier circles. He is trying to get behind you — standard pincer, textbook, and you know it is textbook because you have practised defending against it and the knowing does not make it less dangerous. The Kapak hangs back, letting the soldiers do the work, waiting for an opening. It is the smart one.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (Soldier flanking):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15 (flanking, +1 DC)
> **SUCCESS:** You turn to meet the flank. Textbook defence against textbook attack.
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+2 slashing damage from behind. The formation works.
>
> **IF ALDRIC CHOSE SHIELD WALL:** The flank fails. Aldric blocks the cellar entrance. DC remains 14.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 3

The Kapak decides it has waited long enough. It makes a sound — not a roar, not a hiss, something between — and charges. The soldiers press from both sides. This is the moment the fight tips: either you break them here or the cellar becomes a trap with you inside it.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Everything you have.**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **KAPAK DEATH THROES:** If the Kapak drops to 0 HP, it dissolves into a pool of acid (5ft radius). **DEX save DC 12** or take 2d4 acid damage. *Move or be burned.*

> **MEDICINE CHECK (optional):** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 12
> Treat Kapak poison on yourself or a companion. Requires herbs or antitoxin.
> **SUCCESS:** Poisoned condition removed. The bitterness fades.
> **FAILURE:** The poison runs its course naturally (1 round remaining).

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 3

What remains fights or breaks. The soldiers, if alive, look at each other — the look of men calculating whether dying here is worth what they are being paid. The Kapak does not calculate. It fights until it cannot.

> **DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS:** You hold.
> **FAILURE:** 1d6+3 damage (Kapak) or 1d8+2 damage (soldier).

---

### AFTER THE FIGHT

The Kapak is dead — a pool of steaming acid where a living thing used to be. The soldiers are dead or gone. The cellar smells of acid, blood, and the musty dampness of old stone. The fire is still burning and by its light you can see the supply cache: crates marked with Dragon Army insignia, stacked against the far wall.

Linna is shaking. She is eight years old and she has been tied to a beam in a cellar with a Kapak draconian for what she will later say was 'a long time,' which could mean two hours or two days. She does not cry. She has gone past crying into the quiet place that children go when the world has exceeded their capacity to process it.

> **DRAGON ARMY SUPPLY CACHE:** Investigation is not needed — the crates are right there. Stash Loot Roll (no moral penalty — enemy supplies):
> 1–5: Empty crates. They already moved the good stuff.
> 6–10: Supplies (rations, crude maps, 1d4 stl).
> 11–14: 2d6 stl + mundane item (Dragon Army patrol schedule, signal flags).
> 15–17: 3d6 stl + a useful item (Potion of Healing, military-grade rope, antitoxin).
> 18–19: 4d6 stl + quality item (Dragon Army officer's spyglass, coded orders — Caeron will want these).
> 20: 5d6 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL.

> **RARE ITEM ROLL:** Roll 1d20.
> 1–19: Quality mundane item (Dragon Army officer's cloak, +1 to Stealth in wilderness — good camouflage).
> 20: MAGIC ITEM — +1 Chain Mail. Solamnic make, stripped from a fallen knight. The rose is still visible. Wearing it feels like a responsibility.

> **SEARCH THE BODIES (Optional — moral choice):**
> The soldiers and the Kapak remains. Searching Dragon Army dead is enemy intelligence, but the Kapak's acid makes it unpleasant.
>
> **A) Search them.** (-1 CROWN. Loot Roll below.)
> **B) Leave them. You have what you came for.** (+1 CROWN. No loot.)

> **LOOT ROLL (if searched):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–5: Nothing. The Kapak acid dissolved most of it.
> 6–10: 1d4 stl from soldier belt pouches. 1 day rations (Dragon Army field bread, stale but edible).
> 11–14: 2d4 stl + mundane item (a locket with a portrait — the soldier was someone's son). 2 days rations.
> 15–17: 3d4 stl + Potion of Healing (the soldiers had supplies the Kapak did not share). 1 day rations.
> 18–19: 4d4 stl + Kapak venom vial (single-use: +1d4 poison damage on next weapon attack). 2 days rations.
> 20: 5d4 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL. 3 days rations.

> **KAPAK VENOM VIAL** (if found): Single use. Apply to weapon as a bonus action. Next successful hit deals +1d4 poison damage. The vial is small, black, and warm to the touch. Using it is not forbidden. It is not honoured either.

> **NPC GRATITUDE — LINNA**
> Linna is a child. She has nothing to give you. She presses her face into your tabard and holds on and does not let go for a very long time. You can feel her heartbeat through the cloth. It is fast and small.
>
> +1 ROSE. No roll. Some debts are not paid in steel.
>
> *Her family finds you in Vogler (Scene 70B). They offer a meal, a blanket, and 2d4 stl — everything they have. You may refuse the steel (+1 ROSE) or accept it (no penalty — they insist).*

> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots,
> Lay on Hands pool, bandages, potions, antitoxin consumed.
> Update gold if loot was found. Record any items gained.
> Note if Linna was healed (affects Scene 70B recognition).
> **Short rest available:** Recover Action Surge, regain 1 Second Wind use. HP: spend Hit Dice.

> **XP:** 15 XP per soldier. 25 XP for the Kapak. Bonus 15 XP if Linna healed. Bonus 10 XP if stealth approach succeeded.

> **A) Carry Linna back to camp. She weighs almost nothing.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44_REPORT

## SCENE 45 — THESSALY IN THE FIELD

*South Road*

Thessaly moves through the exercise area with practiced near-invisibility. She has her notebook inside her jacket rather than out. She is watching everything and taking no notes yet.

> **A) Brief her on the refugees.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 44
>
> **B) Ask her to observe only — do not report yet.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 44

## SCENE 45B — THE BOY WITH THE BLUE COAT

*South Road — The Refugee Camp, Evening (if Mira is in your party)*

> **CONDITIONAL SCENE — Mira must be in your party.**

His name was Aldren. He was eleven years old and he had a blue coat with brass buttons. He was the one who kept the other children calm during the march. The infection moved faster than she expected. She did everything correctly. She did not have the medicines she would have had in a proper infirmary. In the morning he was gone.

Mira is sitting outside the camp. She is not crying. She is somewhere past crying — the place where grief becomes a very quiet, very heavy thing that does not make noise.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Medicine (WIS) (+1) | WIS | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** She needs witness: someone to simply confirm that what happened was real and that it mattered. Ask his name. That is the correct thing.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** She is in pain and very still.

> **A) Stay beside her until she is ready to move.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Mira if Spark active) --> Scene 46
>
> **B) 'You did everything right. This was not your failure.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 46
>
> **C) Ask her his name. Make her say it aloud.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Mira) --> Scene 46
