## SCENE 44_REPORT — THE FIRE AND THE RECKONING

*South Road — Camp, Evening After the Refugee Column*

The fire is the small, efficient kind that field exercises teach — enough light to see faces, not enough to see from a distance. The refugee column is behind you now, in every sense. What remains is the weight of it: thirty-one people, three children, the man with the barrel-stave splint who stood at attention for a tabard. You are learning that some things become heavier after you stop carrying them.

Aldric sits across from you, cleaning his blade with the particular focus of a man who is processing something by giving his hands work. He has not spoken since the column. After a while: 'I keep thinking about the children.' He says this to the blade, not to you.

Lord Caeron arrives at the fire and does what officers do — takes the report, asks the right questions, writes the answers in his small precise hand. Casualties: none. Contact: confirmed Dragon Army presence. Assessment: the south road is not safe for civilian movement.

Then he closes the report book and does something you have not seen before. He sits. Not at the fire — at the edge of it, half in the dark, the way people sit when they want to be present without being the centre. He looks south. He does not say anything about what he is looking at.

> **OPTIONAL SCENE — SERATH'S BARN**
> If you have not yet encountered Serath: there is a figure in the barn at the edge of the camp clearing. Turn to Scene 36 (Wound and Trust) now. If you have already met Serath, skip this.

> **A) (If you chose to report) Take the full report to the command tent. The chain of command will decide what happens next.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 31
>
> **B) (If you chose to move them) You already acted. The column is moving north. Face the consequences.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 51
>
> **C) (If you chose to defend) You held the waystation. The refugees had time. Now you need to report what you found.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 52
>
> **D) (If you chose to find Caeron) Present your assessment directly. He is listening.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 31
>
> **E) There is a peddler camped at the edge of the firelight. He has been following the column.** --> Scene 44_PEDDLER
>
> **F) Smoke on the south road. Something is burning. Caeron nods once — investigate.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 28_CARAVAN

---


## SCENE 28_CARAVAN — THE AMBUSHED CARAVAN

*South Road — Half a Mile South of Camp, Night*

The smoke is thicker than cookfire. You smell it before you see it — wood, canvas, something chemical that makes your eyes water. The overturned cart is in the road ditch, one wheel still turning slowly. The mule is dead. The cargo is scattered across the verge: bolts of cloth, iron nails, a cask of something that has spilled into the dirt and smells of vinegar.

One body on the road. A merchant's guard — throat cut, eyes open, hand still on the hilt of a sword he never drew. He has been dead less than an hour.

The second figure is alive. Barely. He is under the cart, one leg pinned by the axle, and there is a compound fracture below the knee — bone through skin, blood soaking the road dust black. His breathing is the shallow, rapid kind that means shock. His name, you will learn, is Dorren. He is a merchant from Gateway. He was bringing supplies south because someone told him Vogler would pay double for iron and salt.

He has three rounds before the bleeding kills him.

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run the encounter at your table, then skip to **AFTER THE FIGHT**.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow the rounds below. Roll when prompted.

> **INJURED NPC — MERCHANT DORREN**
> Compound leg fracture, bleeding heavily. Dies in 3 rounds without healing.
> **Heal him:** Medicine DC 13 (stabilize only), Mira (if present, automatic stabilize + 1d6+2 heal), Paladin Cure Wounds (1 spell slot, heals 2d8+CHA), Paladin Lay on Hands (from pool), Bandage (stabilize at 1 HP), Potion of Healing (2d4+2).
> *Record any resources spent on your character sheet.*
> **If healed:** Dorren survives. He appears in Vogler with supplies. +1 ROSE. His shop in Vogler offers 10% discount (Scene 70C_SHOP).
> **If not healed:** Dorren bleeds out. You bury him by the road. The supplies are salvageable but the man is not.

> **COMPANION SELECTION**
> Choose up to 2 companions (if available):
> **Lysander** — +2 to your first attack. 'They are still close. I can smell the draconian.'
> **Mira** — Heals Dorren automatically in Round 1. Essential if you lack healing.
> **Serath** — Scouts the perimeter. Warns you of reinforcements (prevents surprise in Round 3).
> **Sera** — Marks the first target. +2 to your second attack roll.
> **Aldric** — Shield wall. Solid. Reliable. Angry about the dead guard.

> **ENEMY STAT BLOCKS (Pen & Paper)**
> **Baaz Draconian (2):** AC 13, HP 18, Speed 30ft. Scimitar +4 (1d6+2). Claw +4 (1d4+2). Death Throes: on death, turns to stone, weapon stuck (DC 11 STR to free). Disguise Self (used to look human at distance).
> **Human Deserter:** AC 12, HP 11, Speed 30ft. Shortsword +3 (1d6+1). Light crossbow +3 (1d8+1, 80/320). Cowardly: flees at half HP or if both draconians fall. Surrender possible (Persuasion DC 11).

> **INVESTIGATION CHECK (before or during combat):** Roll 1d20 + INT modifier | DC 12
> **SUCCESS:** Hidden under the cart's false bottom — a Potion of Healing and 2d4 stl. Dorren was smuggling it. He will not mind if it saves his life.
> **FAILURE:** You do not find the hidden compartment.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 1

They are still here. That is the first wrong thing — whoever attacked the caravan should have taken what they wanted and gone. Instead, they are standing over the wreckage as if waiting. When you come around the cart, you understand why. They were not robbing the caravan. They were using it as bait.

Two draconians. You have read the reports but the reports did not prepare you for the reality: seven feet tall, scaled, the wings vestigial but the claws very real. They are wearing scavenged armour and their eyes have the flat, predatory patience of things that are confident in what they are. Between them: a human. Deserter's gear — Solamnic-issue mail with the tabard torn off. He has the look of a man who made a choice six months ago and has been living inside the consequences ever since.

The draconians see you and do not react with surprise. They react with hunger.

> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC (Baaz: 13, Deserter: 12)
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **IF LYSANDER IS PRESENT:** +2 to this attack. He moves beside you like a shadow with a sword.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:**
> **Aldric:** A) Flank (+1 next attack) | B) Shield Wall (+1 AC) | C) Aggressive Strike (1d8+2, takes 1d4)
> **Sera:** A) Scout Shot (1d6 dmg) | B) Mark Target (+2 next attack) | C) Disengage Cover (safe retreat)
> **Mira:** A) Heal Dorren (automatic stabilize + 1d6+2) | B) Bandage Dorren (stabilize 1 HP) | C) Herbal Boost (+1 save)
> **Serath:** A) Intel (+2 one attack) | B) Dagger Strike (1d4+2) | C) Feint (enemy -1 next attack)
> **Lysander:** A) Combat Instruction (+2 attack) | B) Veteran Strike (1d10+3) | C) Guard (takes next hit)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):**
> • (Paladin) Cast Bless: +1d4 to attacks and saves for up to 3 targets, Concentration, lasts entire combat. 1 spell slot.
> • (Paladin) Divine Smite: Bonus action after hitting with a melee weapon. 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). Once per turn. 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest at level 2+). *Draconians recoil from radiant damage.*
> • (Paladin) Lay on Hands: Heal self or Dorren. Bonus action.
> • (Paladin) Cure Wounds: Heal Dorren 2d8+CHA. 1 spell slot. Replaces attack.
> • (Fighter) Action Surge: Additional Action this round (except Magic). 1/short or long rest.
> • (Fighter) Second Wind: 1d10+[level] HP. Bonus action. 2 uses/long rest, regain 1/short rest.
> • (Any) Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action.
> • (Any) Use Bandage on Dorren: Stabilize at 1 HP. Replaces attack.

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 1

The first Baaz attacks with its claws — not the scimitar. The claws. It wants you to understand what it is. The second flanks, moving with a speed that the armour should prevent but doesn't. The deserter hangs back, crossbow raised, and fires.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (Baaz claw):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS:** Deflected. The claws scrape armour.
> **FAILURE:** 1d4+2 slashing damage. The claw is filthy — describe the sensation.
>
> **DEFENSE ROLL (Crossbow):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 13
> **SUCCESS:** The bolt goes wide.
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+1 piercing damage.

> *Dorren has 2 rounds remaining if not healed.*

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 2

The draconian you hit is bleeding something that is not quite blood — thicker, darker, and it steams when it hits the cold ground. It does not slow down. It gets angrier. The scimitar comes out now, held in a grip that says the claws were an introduction and this is the real conversation.

The deserter is retreating, step by step. He does not want to be here. His hands are shaking. He aimed for your head and hit the cart behind you. He is not a soldier anymore — he is a man with a crossbow and no courage left.

> **PERSUASION CHECK (optional, replaces attack):** Roll 1d20 + CHA modifier | DC 11
> Target the deserter. 'Drop it. Surrender. You know how this ends.'
> **SUCCESS:** The deserter drops the crossbow. Falls to his knees. He is done. One less enemy. (+1 ROSE if you accept the surrender, +1 CROWN if you take him prisoner for trial.)
> **FAILURE:** He fires again. Fear makes his aim worse but luck is not guaranteed.

> **YOUR ATTACK:** (if not using Persuasion)
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
> **BAAZ DEATH THROES:** If a Baaz drops to 0 HP, it turns to stone. Your weapon is stuck in the stone corpse. DC 11 STR check to free it, or draw a backup weapon.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options as Round 1)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options as Round 1)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 2

The remaining Baaz presses the attack. It is stronger than it looks, and it looks very strong. The scimitar comes from the left — a feint — then the claw from the right, aimed at the gap between your breastplate and pauldron. It knows where armour fails. It has done this before.

> **DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS:** You read the feint. Block the claw. Hold your ground.
> **FAILURE:** 1d6+2 slashing damage. The scimitar finds the gap.
>
> **IF DESERTER DID NOT SURRENDER:** Another bolt. DC 13 DEX save or 1d8+1 piercing.

> *Dorren has 1 round remaining if not healed. His breathing is getting worse.*

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 3

The fight has the quality of something that needs to end. The road is dark and the draconian smells of copper and sulfur and its eyes have not blinked once. You are learning that the things you trained to fight are real and they do not care about your training — they care about whether you can survive the next ten seconds.

**IF SERATH IS NOT PRESENT:** Movement at the treeline. A third shape — another draconian, drawn by the noise, emerging from the south. It will arrive in 2 rounds if you do not end this now.
**IF SERATH IS PRESENT:** 'Movement south. We have two minutes before company arrives. Finish this.' Serath's warning gives you time but not much.

> **YOUR ATTACK — End it.**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage. *If this kills the last Baaz, the stone death throes are your signal to move.*

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 3

The draconian makes its final play — a lunging thrust aimed at your chest, all weight behind it, the kind of attack that sacrifices defence for the chance to end you.

> **DEFENSE ROLL:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15 (lunging attack, +1 DC)
> **SUCCESS:** You sidestep. The blade buries in the cart. The draconian is overextended.
> **FAILURE:** 1d6+3 slashing damage. The lunge has power behind it.

---

### AFTER THE FIGHT

The last draconian turns to stone. The statue steams in the cold air and you will remember that sound — the hissing of hot rock meeting night dew — for the rest of your life. The deserter is on his knees or dead or fled. The road is quiet again, the way roads are quiet after violence — not peaceful, just emptied.

Dorren, if he is alive, is staring at you with the expression of a man who has just been given back the remainder of his life and has not yet decided what to do with it.

> **SEARCH THE FALLEN (Optional — moral choice)**
> The draconians are stone. The deserter's gear is scattered. You could search them.
> Aldric is looking at the dead merchant's guard. He does not look at you.
>
> **A) Search the bodies.** (-1 ROSE or -1 CROWN. Loot Roll below.)
> **B) Leave them. The road has taken enough.** (+1 ROSE or +1 CROWN. No loot.)

> **LOOT ROLL (if searched):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–5: Nothing useful. Draconian gear crumbles with the stone.
> 6–10: 1d4 stl from the deserter's belt pouch. 1 day rations (hardtack and dried meat).
> 11–14: 2d4 stl + a mundane item (whetstone, 2 days rations, a battered compass).
> 15–17: 3d4 stl + Potion of Healing from the deserter's kit. 2 days rations.
> 18–19: 4d4 stl + a quality item (the deserter's shortsword is well-made, or a map of Dragon Army patrol routes). 3 days rations.
> 20: 5d4 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL. 3 days rations.

> **RARE ITEM ROLL (only on natural 20 above):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–19: Quality mundane item (the deserter's mail is Solamnic-issue, AC 16, good condition).
> 20: MAGIC ITEM — +1 Shield. The deserter took it when he left. The rose emblem has been scratched off but the enchantment remains.

> **THE DEAD GUARD (Optional — NON-COMBATANT)**
> The guard is still on the road. His sword is in its scabbard. He never drew it. His eyes are open. He was a man with a job and the job killed him and his employer is twenty feet away bleeding out from a compound fracture. He has a belt pouch, a water skin, and a locket around his neck.
>
> **A) Search the guard's body.** You are searching the body of a man who was not your enemy. He was protecting a merchant on a road that should have been safe. See **Looting the Dead — Non-Combatant** penalties in Combat Reference. (-2 ROSE, -2 CROWN. 1d4 stl + 2 days rations + the locket contains a portrait of a woman and a child.)
> Aldric's voice, quiet: 'He was on our side.' It is not an accusation. It is worse — it is a fact.
> **B) Leave him.** (+1 ROSE. The guard deserves better than this road. You cannot give him better. You can give him the dignity of not being searched.)

> **CARAVAN WRECKAGE:** Investigation DC 12. (No moral penalty — legitimate scouting.)
> **SUCCESS:** Stash Loot Roll:
> 1–5: Spoiled supplies. Nothing salvageable.
> 6–10: Supplies (rations, bandages, 1d4 stl).
> 11–14: 2d6 stl + mundane item (iron nails, salt — trade goods).
> 15–17: 3d6 stl + Potion of Healing (hidden in cargo).
> 18–19: 4d6 stl + quality item (merchant's ledger — intel on Dragon Army supply disruption).
> 20: 5d6 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL.

> **MERCHANT'S STRONGBOX:** Visible in the wreckage. Contains 3d6 stl. *Taking it is theft — Dorren's property, whether he lives or dies.* (-2 ROSE, -2 CROWN. Aldric will not speak to you for a scene. Caeron will hear of it.)

> **NPC GRATITUDE — MERCHANT DORREN** (if healed)
> Dorren cannot stand but he can grip your hand. He grips it like a man holding a rope over a cliff. 'I will be in Vogler,' he says. 'If I have anything left when I get there, it is yours.'
>
> **ROLL:** Persuasion (+[bonus]) | CHA | DC 10
>
> **10–12 (Modest):** 1d4 stl. 'It is all I have on me. I am sorry.'
> **13–15 (Grateful):** 2d4 stl and a promise: 10% discount at his Vogler shop.
> **16–18 (Deeply Grateful):** 3d4 stl, the shop discount, and a Potion of Healing from his personal stash. 'I was saving it. You are the reason I do not need it.'
> **19+ (Indebted):** 4d4 stl, the discount, and a merchant's ring (10 stl value, or +1 to Persuasion checks with merchants — 'Tell them Dorren sent you').
> **FAILURE (1–9):** Dorren has nothing. He is a merchant with no goods and no money on a road that almost killed him. He looks at you with wet eyes. 'I will find a way to repay you.' +1 ROSE.

> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots,
> Lay on Hands pool, bandages, potions consumed.
> Update gold if loot was found. Record any items gained.
> Note if Dorren was saved (affects Scene 70C_SHOP).
> **Short rest available:** Recover Action Surge, regain 1 Second Wind use. HP: spend Hit Dice.

> **XP:** 15 XP per draconian. 10 XP for the deserter (killed or captured). Bonus 15 XP if Dorren saved. Bonus 5 XP if deserter surrendered peacefully.

> **A) Return to camp. Report what you found.** --> Scene 44_REPORT

---


## SCENE 44_PEDDLER — THE SOUTH ROAD PEDDLER

*South Road — Camp, Edge of Firelight*

He has the look of a man who has been on the road longer than the road has been safe. A mule. A cart with a canvas cover patched in three places. A smile that has sold things to people who did not know they needed them. He introduces himself as Torvin and he does not explain why a merchant is travelling south when everyone with sense is travelling north. Perhaps he is brave. Perhaps he is foolish. Perhaps the margins are better where the danger is, and Torvin has calculated the risk.

'Solamnic steel,' he says, looking at your tabard. 'You lot always need something. Let me see what I have.'

He pulls back the canvas. The cart is better stocked than it has any right to be.

> **SHOP — SOUTH ROAD PEDDLER**
> Browse the wares. Prices in steel pieces (stl). Check your character sheet for current gold.
>
> | Item | Price | Notes |
> |------|-------|-------|
> | Bandage (1 use) | 1 stl | Stabilize at 1 HP |
> | Potion of Healing | 5 stl | 2d4+2 HP, bonus action in combat |
> | Rations (3 days) | 1 stl | Travel supplies |
> | Antitoxin | 3 stl | Advantage on poison saves for 1 hour |
> | Whetstone | 1 stl | +1 damage on next attack (single use) |
> | Rope (50 ft) | 1 stl | Climbing, binding |
> | Healer's Kit (10 uses) | 5 stl | Stabilize without Medicine check |
> | Oil Flask (3) | 1 stl | Burn, lubricate, improvise |
>
> **RARE STOCK ROLL (once per visit):**
> Roll 1d20. Torvin reaches deeper into the cart.
> 1–15: Standard stock only. 'That is all I have. Honest.'
> 16–18: Uncommon — Greater Potion of Healing available (15 stl, 4d4+4 HP). 'Found it in a ruin. Intact. Miracle.'
> 19: Uncommon — Masterwork shortbow available (+1 damage, not magical, 20 stl). 'Qualinesti craft. Do not ask.'
> 20: RARE — +1 Chain Mail available (50 stl). The links are too fine for human smithing. Torvin's eyes go careful. 'I know what this is. So do you. Fifty steel and we never speak of it.'
>
> *Record purchases on your character sheet. Deduct steel spent.*

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (+1) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (13+):** Torvin is not just a merchant. He is counting soldiers — yours, and the ones he has seen on the road. He is keeping a tally. For whom, you cannot say, but the information flows north.
>
> **FAILURE (1-12):** He seems like a man making a living. Nothing more.

'Safe travels, Squire,' Torvin says, already repacking. 'Or whatever the opposite of safe is, with you lot. Purposeful travels.'

> **A) Return to the fire.** --> Scene 44_REPORT

---


## SCENE 46 — THE DECREE STANDS

*South Road Camp*

The refugees are escorted south. The man with the splinted leg is helped by one of the escort soldiers who does not look at him while doing it. The children do not fully understand what is happening.

> **Consequence:** If Mira is in your party, she leaves quietly that evening.

> **FIGHTER — MEASURE SUBPLOT**
> Fighters turn to Scene M2 (The Wrong Order) now.

> **A) You obeyed the law. You will live with that.** (+3 CROWN) --> Scene 53
>
> **B) You will never make that choice again.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53

---


## SCENE M2 — THE WRONG ORDER

*Field Camp — During the Refugee Crisis (Fighter Only)*

> **FIGHTER ONLY**
> This scene occurs alongside Scene 46 (The Decree Stands). Paladins: you have the divine scenes instead — skip to Scene 47.

You have seen the decree enforced. You have your choice on record. Now you have six hours before the column moves and Ser Aldous has found you at the camp perimeter. He is not here to debrief you. He looks, if anything, like he has been thinking very hard about something he should have said years ago.

> **THE MEASURE: THE MEASURE ON UNJUST ORDERS**
> Est Sularus oth Mithas. My honour is my life. The Measure is explicit: a decree that requires acting against innocents is an improper decree and a Knight is not bound by it — but must be prepared to defend that judgment at tribunal. This is not the easy clause. It puts the burden of judgment on the individual Knight in the exact moment when the individual Knight is most afraid.

'I want to ask you something,' Aldous says. 'Not as a senior officer. As a man who got this wrong once. What do you do when the Measure is clear and the order contradicts it?' He waits. He wants your answer, not the textbook one.

> **A) 'You follow the Measure. That is the point of it. The order is wrong and the Measure says so.'** (+3 MEASURE TRACK. Aldous: 'Yes. That is what it says.') --> Scene M2_measure
>
> **B) 'You follow the order and argue at tribunal. The moment of conflict is not the time to make policy.'** (+1 MEASURE TRACK. Aldous: 'That is defensible. It is not right, but it is defensible.') --> Scene M2_order
>
> **C) 'You try to find a path that satisfies both. The 24-hour delay, the technical argument. You use the law against itself.'** (+2 MEASURE TRACK. Aldous: 'Clever. And sometimes correct. Know when it isn't.') --> Scene M2_clever

---


## SCENE M2_measure — THE MEASURE IS CLEAR

*Field Camp*

Aldous is quiet for a long time. Then: 'I got it wrong the first time. I followed the order. The village is not there anymore.' He looks at you. 'The Measure gave me the answer. I chose the safer path anyway. I have had a long time to understand why that was wrong. You worked it out in one conversation.' He stands. 'You will be a good knight. What matters now is making sure the good is worth the trouble it causes.'

> **MEASURE TRACK: +3**

> **A) Continue to Scene 47.** --> Scene 47

---


## SCENE M2_order — DEFENSIBLE

*Field Camp*

'Defensible,' Aldous says. 'Not right. Defensible.' He does not push further. He does not need to. You know the difference and he knows you know. The conversation ends there and you carry the word defensible with you for the rest of the exercise, testing things against it, checking whether what you are about to do is merely defensible or actually correct.

> **MEASURE TRACK: +1**

> **A) Continue to Scene 47.** --> Scene 47

---


## SCENE M2_clever — USING THE LAW

*Field Camp*

'Sometimes correct,' Aldous says. 'Know when it isn't.' He lets that sit. Then: 'The people who use the law against itself are necessary. They are also the ones who eventually find a case where the clever solution does not exist and they have to make the same choice you avoided making. Know which kind of case that was. Know it before you need to.'

> **MEASURE TRACK: +2**

> **A) Continue to Scene 47.** --> Scene 47

## SCENE 47 — CAERON'S PRIVATE ANSWER

*South Road Camp*

'No. I do not believe it is right.' He does not look at you when he says this. 'It is, however, the law. And I am bound by the law I swore to serve.' A pause. 'I am telling you this because I think you should know where I actually stand.'

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> His eyes hold yours one second longer than the conversation requires.

> **A) 'Then find a way to do both.'** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Caeron if Spark active) --> Scene 49
>
> **B) 'I respect the honesty.'** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 31
>
> **C) 'What would you do if you were a squire right now?'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 49

*South Road Camp*

> **Consequence:** +3 ROSE. Formal reprimand. The refugees live. Aldric looks at you differently.

> **B) Tell Caeron privately you would do it again.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 53

> **B) Make sure Caeron knows exactly what you did and why.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 53

*End of Act Two.*

## PALADIN SCENE P2 — THE CHAPEL VISION

*Castle Brightholm — Old Chapel, Night*

> **PALADIN ONLY**
> This scene occurs the night before the formal Trials begin. Fighters: proceed directly to Scene 53 after Scene 51 or 52.

You cannot sleep. The old chapel of the garrison is not the official chapel — the official one is clean and regularly used. This one is behind the armoury, half the roof gone, grass growing through the floor stones. The garrison uses it for storage now. But the altar is still there, uncovered, and the stone that was once the offering bowl is still the shape of a bowl.

You did not mean to come here. You were walking and ended up here. That is different from choosing.

You sit in front of the altar for a while. Nothing happens. Then you put your hand in the offering bowl — an absurd thing to do, and you do not know why you do it — and the stone is warm. Not the warmth of stone that has been sitting in an enclosed space. Warm like something living.

> **DIVINE SIGN**
> The warmth travels up your arm and settles behind your sternum. Not painful. Not frightening. It feels like: the moment before you speak the correct answer to something important. Certainty that has not yet found words. The stone is warm and the grass is still growing through the floor and the stars are visible through the broken roof and you understand, in the part of you below language, that you are not alone in this room.

You speak aloud. You have not decided to do this — it simply happens. You say: 'Who are you?' No answer in words. But the warmth in your chest becomes, briefly, the specific warmth of something smiling. Then it fades to ordinary stone temperature and you are alone again.

You think about what kind of warmth that was:

| PALADINE | KIRI-JOLITH | MISHAKAL | HABBAKUK | BRANCHALA |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ |

> **A) The warmth of law and order — a gentle judge's certainty, high and patient.** Mark 1 tally: PALADINE. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53
>
> **B) The warmth of a forge before battle — practical, purposeful, directed.** Mark 1 tally: KIRI-JOLITH. (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 53
>
> **C) The warmth of a healer's hands — soft, focused on what hurts.** Mark 1 tally: MISHAKAL. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53
>
> **D) The warmth of sunlight through trees — wide, un-directed, alive.** Mark 1 tally: HABBAKUK. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53
>
> **E) The warmth of music heard from another room — joyful, reaching, optimistic.** Mark 1 tally: BRANCHALA. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53
>
> **F) You cannot read it. The warmth was just warmth. Mark nothing.** (+1 CROWN for not assuming you understand what you do not yet understand.) --> Scene 53

---


# ACT THREE: THE ROAD NARROWS (LEVEL 2)

## Act Three Overview

The Dragon Army is confirmed within twenty miles. The formal Trials are accelerated. Scenes 53-70 cover the crisis, the condensed Trials, and the road south to Vogler. You gain Level 3 at Scene 61. Paladins: Paladin Scene P3 is in Act Three.

---


## SCENE 53 — THE NEWS ARRIVES

*Castle Brightholm — Great Hall, Night*

Three bells at midnight — the signal everyone knows and hopes never to hear at this hour. The rider is at the back being given water. Lord Caeron is at the front with the dispatch. He reads it through twice. In the moment before he turns, before he chooses his expression, you see what is underneath it. Then he turns. 'The Dragon Army's Blue Wing has been confirmed south of Lake Akh-Tiel. Approximately two thousand. Moving north. Three days from Vogler. Possibly two.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Composure (WIS Save) (+1) | WIS | DC 11
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 11+):** Your face stays neutral. Caeron holds your gaze a half-second longer. +1 CROWN.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-10):** Something crosses your expression. No penalty, but it was seen.

> **RELATIONSHIP CHECK — ACT 2**
> If you are pursuing **two or more romances**, turn to Scene REST_ROMANCE now before choosing below. Resolve that scene, then return here.

> **A) Go to your companions.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 54
>
> **B) Stay for the full briefing.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 55
>
> **C) Find Thessaly.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 56
>
> **D) Find Aldric.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Aldric if Spark) --> Scene 57
>
> **E) Something is wrong about the timing. Find out who knew first.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 53B
>
> **F) Find Tariel, if present.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53D
>
> **G) Find Lysander, if present.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 53E

---


## SCENE 53B — THE SOURCE

*Castle Brightholm — Records Room, Night After the News*

Thessaly finds you an hour after Caeron's briefing. She has been in the records room and her face has the specific quality it gets when she has found something she did not want to find.

The Dragon Army knew the refugees were on the south road before the patrol found them. The dispatch pouch from the patrol — if you kept it — contains a reference code that matches a garrison communication cipher. The Blue Wing had intelligence on the garrison's movements. Current intelligence. Not intercepted — given.

Thessaly lays it out carefully: the timing, the cipher reference, the two officers who had access to that level of communication. One is dead — killed in the ambush on the south road. The other is Ser Aldous.

> **DARK SCENE — BETRAYAL**
> Ser Aldous, who told you about the village he could not save. Who mentored you on the Measure. Thessaly's evidence is circumstantial but strong. What you do with this is yours to decide. Caeron does not know yet.

There is another possibility Thessaly offers, quietly: the cipher reference could have been planted to implicate Aldous. By the Dragon Army, if they knew his history with that village. If someone wanted a trusted garrison mentor removed. She does not know which is true. She has given you everything she has.

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Investigation (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 14
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 14+):** The cipher reference uses a secondary field code, not the primary garrison cipher. A traitor using the primary code would be caught by standard security sweeps. Using the secondary requires counter-intelligence knowledge — this narrows the suspect list significantly and rules out the obvious names.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-13):** The evidence is what Thessaly described. You cannot evaluate it further without more information.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Take the evidence to Lord Caeron immediately. Let the command structure decide. You leave the records room carrying less than you arrived with.** (+2 CROWN. Aldous is investigated. If guilty, imprisoned. If framed, exonerated — but the investigation takes two weeks the garrison does not have.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) Confront Aldous directly, alone, before going to Caeron. Give him the chance to explain.** (+2 ROSE — this could go very badly.) --> Scene 53C
>
> **C) Tell no one yet. Keep it between you and Thessaly and watch Aldous closely. The night has more to give.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD — dangerous. But if he is innocent, you have protected him.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **D) Destroy the evidence. Aldous has given you too much for this to be what it looks like. The papers burn quickly.** (+1 ROSE — this is also a moral failure. You may be wrong.) --> Scene 53_HUB

---


## SCENE 53C — ALDOUS ALONE

*Castle Brightholm — Chapel Steps, Night*

He is exactly where he always is late at night: the chapel steps, watching whatever hawk or star he watches when he cannot sleep. He sees you coming and he looks at what you are carrying — the papers — and something in his face shifts. Not guilt. Something more complicated.

He is quiet for a long time after you show him. Then: 'I did not give them information about the refugees. I would tell you if I had. I have been honest with you about worse things than this.' He looks at the cipher reference. 'I know who used this code. And I know who had reason to make it look like me.'

He gives you a name. A garrison officer you know slightly — someone whose brother is a Dragon Army officer. Someone who has been sending private correspondence south. Someone Aldous has been watching for three weeks and has not yet had enough evidence to bring to Caeron.

> **The Real Traitor**
> Aldous was right. The officer is the source. If you went to Aldous first, you now have the actual name. You can bring this to Caeron with full context — but it means admitting you sat on Thessaly's evidence for a night before reporting it. Caeron will know. He will not say anything. He will remember.

> **A) Take everything to Caeron immediately — Thessaly's evidence, Aldous's name, all of it. The chapel steps are empty when you leave Aldous there.** (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN. The traitor is caught. Aldous is cleared. Caeron gives you a look that means: you handled that correctly even if imperfectly.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) Deal with the officer yourself, tonight, before Caeron is involved. It is done before the next bell.** (+1 SWORD — dangerous, legally questionable. But fast. The garrison is not compromised further.) --> Scene 53_HUB

---


## SCENE 53D — TARIEL AFTER THE NEWS

*Castle Brightholm — Map Room, Night (Conditional: Tariel in party)*

'Two thousand soldiers,' she says. 'Moving north. The garrison has — what — eighty? The decree sent thirty refugees south into their path. And the Order's response is to accelerate your Trials so you can ride to Vogler as a sworn squire rather than an unsworn one.' She looks at you. 'Does the title make your sword sharper?'

Then she opens the locket. A portrait. A young man in Dragon Army colours. Dark hair like hers. Her eyes.

'My brother,' she says. 'Aldren. He joined the Dragon Army because the Knights would not have him — wrong province, wrong politics, wrong family name. He tried to leave after Thresh. They do not let people leave. He is dead. Both institutions failed him. He was twenty-three.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Insight (+1) | WIS | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** The locket portrait is recent. The grief is not old. The diplomatic observer role is a response. She is not your enemy. She is something more complicated.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** She is grieving. The arguments are a form of grief.

**CONVICTION CHOICE (Tariel Corruption Track — Debate 2):**

> **A) 'Neither system killed your brother. People did. The Measure exists to hold those people accountable.' She closes the locket. The map room is quiet when you leave.** (CONVICTION: remains or improves toward STEADFAST. +1 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) 'I am sorry about Aldren. The Order should have been better. I intend to make it better.' She looks at you for a long time. Then nods.** (CONVICTION: remains. +1 ROSE.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **C) 'You are right. Both systems failed. I do not know what replaces them but I know they are not enough.' She watches you say this with the attention of someone who has been waiting to hear it.** (CONVICTION: advances toward FALLEN. +1 ROSE, -1 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **D) 'The Order can be reformed. Your brother's death is an argument for reform, not abandonment.' She does not agree. But she does not argue. That is new.** (CONVICTION: improves toward STEADFAST. +2 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB

**ROMANCE CHOICE (optional — if at SPARK or higher):**

> **R1) 'I am sorry about Aldren.' Name him. Touch her hand.** (ROMANCE FLAME Tariel)
>
> **R2) Maintain professional distance.** (Romance holds.)

---


## SCENE 53E — LYSANDER'S TRUTH

*Castle Brightholm — Garrison Wall, Night (Conditional: Lysander in party)*

He tells you. The bridge. The refugees. The court-martial. The Knight who filed the court-martial was promoted to Commander.

He tells this story the way Aldous told his — flat, worn smooth. But where Aldous carries the weight as penance, Lysander carries it as evidence.

**CONVICTION CHOICE (Lysander Corruption Track — Experience 3):**

> **A) 'File the appeal. I will speak on your behalf.' He stares at you. Then: 'You mean that.' You do.** (CONVICTION: improves toward STEADFAST. +1 ROSE, +1 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) 'The system that punished you is broken. It needs people like you inside it.' He turns this over like a stone in his hand.** (CONVICTION: remains. +1 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **C) 'They promoted the man who let people drown. I do not know how to defend that.' He looks at you with something like relief.** (CONVICTION: advances toward FALLEN. +1 ROSE, -1 CROWN.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **D) 'You did the right thing. The institution did the wrong thing. Both are true and I can hold both.' The garrison wall is cold. You stand there until the silence becomes its own answer.** (CONVICTION: QUESTIONING. +2 ROSE.) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **E) 'I want to believe the Order would have done differently if it knew.' He does not reply. The wall is enough.** (CONVICTION: SHAKEN. +1 ROSE. -1 to highest Order tally.) --> Scene 53_HUB

**ROMANCE CHOICE (optional — if at SPARK or higher):**

> **R1) Put your hand on his arm.** (ROMANCE FLAME Lysander)
>
> **R2) Carry it with him through witness.** (Romance holds.)

## SCENE 54 — TENDING THE COMPANIONS

Aldric is in the armoury, re-checking equipment. Mira — if present — is doubling her medical supplies. Serath — if present — is watching the south road.

## SCENE 54B — MIRA TENDS SERATH

*Castle Brightholm — Infirmary, Night (NPC Cross-Talk — Conditional: both Mira and Serath present)*

You pass the infirmary and the door is ajar. Inside: Mira is re-dressing Serath's wound. Her hands move with certainty. She does not look at Serath's face while she works.

Serath is watching Mira's hands. Then the assessment becomes something else. They are watching someone who is kind to them without asking for anything.

Mira: 'What you did — leaving the army. That took a different kind of courage.'
Serath: 'You are the first person who called it courage.'

> **A) Watch. Learn. Leave before they notice you. Some kindnesses are not meant to have an audience.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) Enter. 'Is there anything you need?' Mira hands you a roll of bandage without looking up. You are useful here.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53_HUB

## SCENE 55 — THE EMPTY HALL

*Castle Brightholm — Great Hall*

Everyone left. The hall emptied in the efficient way of a military institution responding to something real. You stayed. You are not entirely sure why — something in how he stood after everyone else left made going feel like the wrong thing to do. He is at the table now with the dispatch open again, reading it a third time or using it as somewhere to look. He hears you. Looks up. For one moment, before the composure reassembles, you see what is underneath the officer. He is thirty years old. He is afraid. He is very good at his job and that has not made this less frightening. 'You stayed,' he says. The two words carry at least three others.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> 'I intend to conduct your Trials evaluation before we march — whatever comes after, you should have the thing you came here for.' He says this to his papers. You have never heard Caeron Ashvale ask for anything before.

You stay for a while. Not long — there is work to do and both of you know it. But a while. The dispatch is still open on the table. He does not close it. You do not ask him to. Some things you can only do if you do not make them into an act — if you just stand in the same room with someone who is carrying something heavy until they are ready to carry it into the next room.

> **A) 'I do. Thank you, my lord.' You leave the hall. The candles are still burning behind you.** (+2 CROWN, ROMANCE FLAME Caeron if Spark) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) 'What about you? What do you want?'** (+2 ROSE, Caeron goes very still) --> Scene 59
>
> **C) Stand beside him at the table. Look at the dispatch together. Say nothing.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Caeron) --> Scene 59

---


## SCENE 56 — THESSALY'S INFORMATION

*Castle Brightholm*

Thessaly finds you in the map room an hour after the briefing. She has been busy since — ink on her hands, the look of someone who has been writing fast and stopping to think. She lays it out: the Dragon Army has a specific objective in Vogler. Not only the supply route. Something in the village — or someone. She has narrowed it to two possibilities and cannot narrow it further. 'I wanted you to know before we march,' she says. 'Because you are riding toward it whether you know what it is or not.'

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** History (INT, proficiency if trained) (+3) | INT | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** Vogler is on Lake Akh-Tiel — the only navigable route between the southern Solamnic coast and the northern fortresses that does not require mountain passes. Whoever controls Vogler controls that supply line for the whole northern campaign. The Dragon Army does not need something in the village. They need the village itself.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** The strategic value is military. You cannot narrow it further.
>
> *No dice? Flip a coin: Heads = pass | Tails = fail*

> **A) Take this to Caeron immediately. Thessaly walks with you as far as the corridor. Then she turns back to her desk. More writing to do.** (+1 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **B) Keep it between you for now. She nods. 'Be careful with it.' You will be.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 53_HUB
>
> **C) Stay. There is something else between you tonight.** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE) --> Scene 56B
