*End of Act Three.*

# ACT FOUR: THE ROAD TO VOGLER (LEVEL 3)

## Act Four Overview

You march south toward Vogler. Two more combat encounters await. Romance arcs reach their Oath moments. Paladins: Paladin Scene P4 — the Choosing — is in Act Four.

---


## SCENE 62 — THE MARCH

*South Road — Day 1*

Before the column moves, Caeron distributes march pay from a leather purse. Five steel pieces per squire. He counts them into your palm without ceremony — the Order pays its own, even on the road.

> **WAGES PAID — MARCH PAY**
> Add 5 stl to your gold. *Issued by Lord Caeron before departure.*

Brightholm disappears behind the first hill at the third mile. You watch the towers go until the hill takes them. Aldric rides beside you in the grey morning and says nothing, which is something — Aldric Voss does not ride in silence unless he is thinking something he has not yet decided whether to say.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Perception (+2) | WIS | DC 12
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** Boot prints south of the verge — someone left the road in a hurry recently. Relevant in Scene 70.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** The road looks clear.

After a long while: 'Whatever Order you got — I am not competing with you anymore.' He means: I will now be competing to be worthy of riding beside you, which is a different thing.

> **A) Laugh. 'That is the nicest thing you have said to me.'** (+1 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Aldric) --> Scene 62D
>
> **B) 'Understood. Same.' Comfortable silence.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 62D
>
> **C) 'Race you to the ridge.'** (+1 SWORD, Aldric grins) --> Scene 62D

---


## SCENE 62D — THE FIRST NIGHT ON THE ROAD

*South Road — Day 1, Evening Camp*

The first night out of Brightholm is the hardest. Not because of danger — the road is clear for eight miles — but because of what leaving means. The garrison towers were visible until the fifth mile, then the ridge took them. Brightholm is behind you.

Camp is set with garrison efficiency. The fire is regulation size, which means small and purposeful. You eat garrison rations: hard bread, dried meat, a cheese that has survived the march better than expected. Not good food. Adequate food, eaten in the company of people you have spent the most important weeks of your life with, which makes it the best food you have ever eaten.

> **RATIONS — EVENING MEAL**
> Garrison supplies cover tonight's meal. No personal rations consumed.
> *Caeron distributed three days of column rations at departure. After tomorrow night, you eat from your own pack.*

> **NPC CROSS-TALK — CAERON AND SERA**
> At the edge of camp: Lord Caeron is speaking with Sera Nighthollow. Caeron's careful listening posture; Sera's clipped precision. When they finish, Caeron nods once. Sera glances at you briefly. Whatever she told him, it was about the road ahead.

**IF TARIEL IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She eats apart from the column. She has her notebook open. Once, she looks up and catches your eye. The moment lasts three seconds. She looks down first.

**IF LYSANDER IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He is not in the camp. He rides parallel, not with, the column. Visible occasionally at the treeline, then not visible.

> **A) Walk the perimeter before sleeping.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 62E
>
> **B) Find your companions. Sit with them.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 62E
>
> **C) Watch the stars. Solinari is rising.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 62E
>
> **D) Train together as a group in the morning.** --> Scene BOND_TRAIN
>
> **E) Share a quiet meal together.** --> Scene BOND_MEAL

---


## SCENE 62E — THE FIRST CAMP BOND

*South Road — Day 1, Night*

The fire is low and the stars are out — Solinari full, Lunitari a red sliver on the horizon, and the kind of sky that only exists when you are far enough from any settlement that the darkness is real. The column has settled. Somewhere in the distance an owl is working. The sound is older than anything on this road.

You find yourself at the edge of camp with the particular restlessness that comes from being tired but not sleepy, the body done but the mind still turning over the day like a stone in water. The others are nearby. You can hear them — Aldric's quiet breathing, the scratch of Thessaly's pen, the careful sounds of Mira checking her supplies in the dark.

**IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She materialises beside you without sound. 'You did not hear me. That is fine. Aldric did not hear me either. Caeron almost heard me, which is why I respect him.' She sits. 'The road south has fresh tracks. Two days old. Civilian, heading north fast. Whatever they were running from, it is behind us now.'

**IF VAEL IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She finds you. 'I have been thinking about what Caeron said — about the towers disappearing behind the hill. He watched them too. He did not think anyone noticed.' She looks south. 'I noticed.'

> **A) Sit with Aldric. He is sharpening something that does not need sharpening.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 63
>
> **B) Find Thessaly. Her pen has stopped. She is staring at nothing.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 63
>
> **C) Walk the perimeter with Caeron. He is already walking it.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 63
>
> **D) Sleep. The road will be long tomorrow. Let the fire do the thinking.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 63

---


## SCENE BOND_CAMP — AROUND THE FIRE

*Camp — Evening*

The fire is the right size tonight — not the regulation minimum that Caeron insists on, but the slightly larger version that happens when someone adds a log without being asked and no one corrects them. The column has settled into the particular rhythm of people who have been moving together long enough to develop unspoken protocols: who fills the water, who checks the perimeter, who tells the story.

Aldric is cleaning his blade. He always cleans his blade. It is the thing he does when he wants to be present without having to speak, and it works — the repetitive motion gives his hands somewhere to be while the rest of him listens.

Tonight someone asks a question. It is the kind of question that only gets asked around fires, in the dark, when the day is far enough behind and tomorrow is far enough ahead that the present moment feels briefly safe.

'What will you do when this is over?'

> **PARTY BONDING SCENE**
> This scene deepens your connection with your companions. All companions present will react.

> **A) 'Go home. See my family. Then come back.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) 'Keep going. There is more road.'** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) 'I do not know yet. Ask me at Vogler.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **D) Ask someone else the question instead.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE BOND_TRAIN — TRAINING TOGETHER

*Camp — Morning*

Dawn training has become a group ritual. Not ordered — evolved. Aldric runs sword forms. Vael, if present, matches him pass for pass, the two of them moving through the same combinations with the synchronised precision of people who have been watching each other improve. Sera, if present, watches from the armoury roof or a convenient tree with the professional attention of someone filing observations for later use.

Today someone suggests a change: train together. Not the formal pairs Caeron assigns. Real training — the kind where you learn from each other's differences.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Athletics (+3) | STR | DC 12
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** You learn a technique from the session. +1 to your next combat encounter attack roll.
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** Good exercise. No specific breakthrough.

> **A) Spar with everyone willing. Learn their styles.** (+2 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Focus on teaching. Show them what you know.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Ask Sera or Serath for tactical advice instead.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **D) Run the perimeter with whoever will join you.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE BOND_MEAL — BREAKING BREAD

*Camp — Midday*

Mira, if present, has done something to the garrison rations that borders on alchemy. The bread is the same bread. The cheese is the same cheese. But somehow the combination, with whatever herbs she found at the roadside this morning, has become something worth sitting down for.

If Mira is not present, Aldric has attempted to cook. The result is edible in the way that garrison food is always edible: it sustains life without celebrating it. He is aware of this. He is not apologising.

People sit closer than they used to. That is the change you notice — not the food, not the conversation, but the physical distance. Eight months ago these were strangers. Now they are the people whose breathing you recognise in the dark.

> **PARTY BONDING SCENE**
> Share a meal. Listen. Be present.

> **A) Tell a story from home. Something true.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Ask each companion one question they have never been asked.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Eat in comfortable silence. Let the quiet do the work.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **D) Plan tomorrow's route with the group.** (+1 CROWN, +1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE BOND_STAR — WATCHING THE MOONS

*Camp — Late Night*

Solinari is full tonight, silver-white. Lunitari hangs low on the horizon, red as old copper. Between them, if you know where to look: the absence that is Nuitari, the black moon. Three moons. Three kinds of power. Three ways of seeing the same sky.

You are not alone on the watch. Someone has joined you without asking, which is the specific trust of people who have stopped requiring invitations. You sit together in the silver-red dark and look at the moons and do not speak for a while.

Thessaly, if present, writes in her notebook by moonlight. Tariel, if present, watches the moons the way she watches everything — cataloguing. Lysander, if present, looks south.

> **Paladin Note:** The three moons remind you of the divine presence. Mark 1 tally under whichever god feels right tonight.

> **A) 'Do you believe in the gods?'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) 'What are you fighting for? Not the Order. You, personally.'** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Say nothing. Some moments do not need words.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **D) Point out Nuitari. Not everyone can see the black moon.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE BOND_RETURN — THE ROAD CONTINUES

The moment passes. Tomorrow continues. But something has shifted — the invisible architecture of the group has settled into a new shape, one where you are a little more known and a little more trusted. That is not nothing. In a war, it is almost everything.

> **A) Continue.** --> Scene BOND_HUB

---


## SCENE BOND_HUB — CAMP

The group settles. The road awaits.

> **A) Return to the evening.** --> Scene 11_EVENING
>
> **B) Turn in. Tomorrow the march begins.** --> Scene 11_NIGHT

---


## SCENE 63 — ALDRIC ON THE ROAD

*South Road*

'Do you know what I thought when the draconians hit us on the south road? I thought: good, she is here. Or he. Or they.' He glances over once and then back to the road. 'I was glad it was you. Not someone else. Not anyone else.'

**IF YOU CHOSE TO TIE IN THE SPAR (Scene 12, pulled the strike):** He is quiet for a mile. Then, without looking at you: 'The spar. At Brightholm. The last exchange.' Another mile. 'You had me. You know that. I know that. I have known since the moment you pulled the strike.' He glances at you. The dagger — his dagger, the one he gave you — is on your belt. He can see it. 'I told you that you almost had me. That was a lie. You had me completely. I was beaten and you chose not to beat me and I have been thinking about that choice every day since.' He looks back at the road. 'It was the most honourable thing anyone has ever done to me. And the most infuriating.' The corner of his mouth twitches. 'Do not expect me to pull my strikes for you. I am not that good a person.'

> **A) 'I was glad it was you too.'** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Aldric if Spark active) --> Scene 64B
>
> **B) 'You fight well.'** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 64B

---


## SCENE 64 — RIDING IN SILENCE

*South Road*

A good silence — the kind that only exists between people who do not need to fill it. The smoke on the southern horizon is thicker now.

> **A) Keep the silence all the way to camp.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 64B
>
> **B) After a mile, ask him something you have wanted to ask.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 64B

---


## SCENE 64B — THE WAR SIGNS

*South Road — Day 2, Morning*

The road changes at the tenth mile. The farms are empty — not abandoned, emptied deliberately. At the eleventh mile: a cart on its side, a pair of child's shoes tied together by the laces. At the twelfth mile: a Solamnic mile-marker with fresh chalk. Someone wrote SOUTH NO. Below it, in a different hand: ARMY 2 DAYS.

The column does not comment. The silence deepens.

> **A) Stop. Pick up the child's shoes. Carry them.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 64C
>
> **B) Note the chalk for your report.** (+1 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 64C
>
> **C) Keep moving.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 64C
>
> **D) Watch the moons with whoever will join you.** --> Scene BOND_STAR
>
> **E) Howling. Close. The horses are screaming.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 64B_WOLVES

---


## SCENE 64B_WOLVES — THE PACK

*South Road — Day 2, Pre-Dawn*

You wake to the sound of horses screaming. Not the nervous whinny of animals that have smelled something wrong — the full-throated shriek of prey animals that can see the predator. You are on your feet with your weapon in hand before your brain fully registers what your body already knows: the camp is under attack.

Wolves. Not the cautious grey wolves of the northern forests that avoid campfires and armoured columns. Dire wolves — massive, gaunt, ribs showing through matted fur, eyes catching the firelight like coins. The Dragon Army's advance has pushed them north, out of their hunting grounds and into territory where the only prey large enough to sustain a pack this size is horse. Or human.

The fire is low — banked coals, not flame. The darkness beyond the fire's reach is absolute. The wolves circle at the edge of the light, and you can count them by their eyes: six pairs, twelve points of amber, moving.

**IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He is already up. Sword drawn, shield on his arm, standing between the horses and the wolves with the posture of a man who has decided that nothing is getting past him. 'Six,' he says. 'The alpha is the large one on the left. Kill the alpha and the pack breaks.'

**IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Sera is crouched by the fire, bow strung, an arrow nocked. She has been awake — she was on watch. 'They have been circling for an hour,' she says. 'Waiting for the fire to die. I was going to feed it, but—' She nods toward the treeline. 'I wanted to see how many.'

**IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Mira is with the horses, calming them with hands and voice. One of the pack horses has a gash on its flank — a wolf got close enough to slash before the screaming started. 'The horse will live,' she says. 'If we live.'

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run at your table. Skip to AFTER THE FIGHT.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow rounds below. Roll when prompted.
>
> **ENEMIES:**
> **Dire Wolf Alpha:** AC 14, HP 30, Speed 50 ft. Bite +6 (2d6+4 piercing). Pack Tactics: advantage on attack if another wolf is within 5 ft of target. Knockdown: on hit, target makes DC 13 STR save or is knocked prone. **Retreats if reduced to half HP and 3+ pack wolves are dead.**
> **Dire Wolf (5):** AC 14, HP 16, Speed 50 ft. Bite +5 (2d6+3 piercing). Pack Tactics. Knockdown DC 12.
>
> *The pack attacks in waves: 2 wolves in Round 1, 2 more in Round 2, the alpha + 1 in Round 3. Killing the alpha before Round 3 causes remaining wolves to flee.*
>
> **YOUR STATS:** Fighter: HP per sheet, AC per sheet, weapon per sheet. Paladin: same.
>
> **COMPANION ACTIONS (choose 1 per round):**
> | Companion | Action A | Action B | Action C |
> |-----------|----------|----------|----------|
> | Aldric | Flank (+1 attack) | Shield Wall (+1 AC) | Guard the horses (wolves cannot reach mounts) |
> | Sera | Aimed Shot (1d8+3 at any wolf) | Mark Alpha (+2 to your attacks vs alpha) | Fire Arrow (lights camp perimeter, wolves -1 attack from light) |
> | Mira | Heal (1d6+2, 1/scene) | Calm horses (prevents stampede) | Throw burning brand (1d4 fire + wolf must save DC 11 WIS or flee) |
> | Lysander | Veteran Strike (1d10+3) | Guard flank (wolves cannot flank you) | Hunt the Alpha (Lysander engages alpha directly: 1d10+3 to alpha, takes 1d6) |

> **ROUND 1 — FROM THE DARK**
>
> *Two wolves break from the circle. They do not snarl, do not warn. They come from the dark like arrows — low, fast, silent until the moment of impact. One goes for the horses. One goes for you.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5 or per sheet) | DC 14 (Wolf AC)
>
> **HIT:** Your blade catches the wolf mid-lunge. Deal weapon damage. The wolf yelps — a sound that is worse than a snarl because it is the sound of a predator discovering it is prey.
>
> **MISS:** The wolf is faster than you expected. It slides past your blade.
>
> **WOLF'S BITE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (Wolf bite +5)
>
> **SUCCESS:** You turn the wolf's jaws on your blade or shield.
>
> **FAILURE:** Take 2d6+3 piercing. The bite is not a slash — it is a clamp, and the wolf shakes. STR save DC 12 or be knocked prone. If prone, the second wolf attacks with advantage next round.

> **ROUND 2 — THE PACK COMMITS**
>
> *Two more wolves from the tree line. The circle has broken — the pack is committed now, all of them moving, the fire barely enough to keep the darkness from swallowing everything. You can hear them breathing. You can smell them — wet fur, blood, the musk of animals that have not eaten in days.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5 or per sheet) | DC 14
>
> **(Paladin) OPTIONAL — DIVINE SMITE:** On hit, +2d8 radiant damage. The light pushes the shadows back. Wolves within 10 ft must make WIS save DC 12 or disengage for 1 round.
>
> **(Fighter) OPTIONAL — ACTION SURGE:** Two attacks this round. The wolf pack does not expect this.
>
> **WOLF ATTACKS (x2 if both still standing):**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (first wolf)
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 15 (second wolf, if alive)
> Each hit: 2d6+3 piercing + knockdown save.
>
> **OPTIONAL — ANIMAL HANDLING (replaces attack):**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Animal Handling (+1) | WIS | DC 15
> **SUCCESS:** You lock eyes with a wolf and something passes between you — not dominance, but understanding. The wolf breaks from the pack and does not return. One fewer enemy. +1 ROSE.
> **FAILURE:** Wolves do not negotiate.

> **ROUND 3 — THE ALPHA**
>
> *The alpha comes last. It is the largest wolf you have ever seen — shoulder height with a warhorse foal, scarred across the muzzle, one ear torn. It has survived everything the wild has thrown at it and it is not afraid of fire or steel or you. It steps into the firelight and its eyes find yours and the challenge is absolute.*
>
> *If the alpha has been killed early (Lysander's Hunt or a lucky hit), the remaining wolves scatter into the dark. The fight is over. Skip to AFTER THE FIGHT.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK (vs Alpha):**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (+5 or per sheet) | DC 14 (Alpha AC)
>
> **HIT:** Deal weapon damage. The alpha staggers but does not fall — it takes more than one hit to drop this animal.
>
> **ALPHA'S BITE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 16 (Alpha bite +6)
>
> **SUCCESS:** You turn the alpha's jaws. It circles, recalculates.
>
> **FAILURE:** Take 2d6+4 piercing. STR save DC 13 or knocked prone. The alpha goes for the throat when you are down.
>
> **IF ALPHA REACHES HALF HP (15 or less) AND 3+ WOLVES ARE DEAD:**
> The alpha howls — long, low, the sound of a predator making a cost-benefit analysis. The remaining wolves break and scatter. The alpha backs into the darkness, watching you, and then it is gone.
>
> **IF ALPHA IS KILLED:**
> The pack scatters instantly. The darkness reclaims them. The fire crackles. The horses stop screaming. The silence that follows is the loudest thing you have ever heard.

> **AFTER THE FIGHT**
>
> Dawn comes grey and cold. The wolf bodies are at the edge of the firelight — gaunt, scarred, driven to desperation by an army that does not care what it displaces. There is no glory in this fight. There is survival, and there is the understanding that the Dragon Army's destruction extends beyond the people it targets.
>
> **IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She examines the alpha's tracks. 'They came from the south-east. Driven out of the Lemish border forests.' She pauses. 'The Dragon Army is burning the forests to deny cover. The wolves had nowhere left to go.' She says it without judgment, but her hand is on her bow and her face is the face of a ranger who has just watched the wild die a little more.
>
> **IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** The pack horse's gash needs stitching. Mira works on it as the sun rises, her hands steady, her voice low. 'Everything is fleeing north,' she says. 'The animals. The refugees. The farmers. We are all running from the same thing. The difference is we are running toward it.'
>
> **LOOT — WOLF PELTS (optional):**
> Dire wolf pelts are valuable — thick, warm, large enough to serve as blankets or trade goods.
> **A) Skin the wolves.** (No moral penalty — they attacked you.) Gain: 1d4 dire wolf pelts (worth 2 stl each). Alpha pelt (worth 5 stl, or can be worn as a cloak: advantage on Intimidation vs beasts).
> **B) Leave them.** The road is not a place for skinning.
>
> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots, Lay on Hands pool, bandages, potions consumed.
> **Short rest available** after breaking camp: Recover Second Wind, Action Surge.
> **XP:** 10 XP per wolf, 20 XP for alpha. Max 70 XP if all killed.

> **A) Break camp. The road continues. The wolves were just the prelude.** --> Scene 64C

---


## SCENE 64C — REFUGEES GOING NORTH

*South Road — Day 2, Afternoon*

Eleven people moving north. You are moving south. The man with the child stops when he sees the tabard. He says: 'Vogler. Please.'

**IF YOU SAVED THE REFUGEES IN ACT TWO:** One of the eleven recognises you. 'You. You saved us. My daughter is alive because of you.'

**IF YOU TURNED THE REFUGEES BACK:** You do not know what happened to those thirty people. The not-knowing sits in you like a stone.

> **A) Give them your rations. They take them without pride. You ride on. The afternoon light is thinner now.** (+2 ROSE. Lose 3 days rations from your pack.) --> Scene 64E
>
> **B) Brief them on the road north. The man nods. The child waves. You ride on.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 64E
>
> **C) Keep moving. You carry the image of eleven people walking north with everything they own.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 64E
>
> **D) (Hidden choice) Demand supplies from the refugees.** You are armed. They are not. You are wearing Solamnic steel and the tabard of an Order that swore to protect people like this. The man with the child watches your hand move toward their pack and his face does something you will remember for the rest of your life: it does not change. He has already learned that armoured people take things. He learned it from the Dragon Army. He is learning it again from you.
> **-3 ROSE, -3 CROWN, -2 SWORD. CORRUPTION: SHAKEN on one active corruption track.** You take: 2d4 stl + 3 days rations + a blanket the child was wrapped in. The child cries. The man does not. Caeron will hear about this — the refugees will tell someone, and that someone will eventually wear a tabard.
> **IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He puts himself between you and the refugees. Not violently. Quietly. The way a wall is quiet. 'No,' he says. That is all he says. He does not move until you do. If you push past him: **Aldric leaves the party.** He rejoins the column but he does not ride beside you again until Vogler. When he looks at you, his face is closed. (-1 romance stage with Aldric.)
> --> Scene 64E

---


## SCENE 64E — THE BURNED FARMSTEAD

*South Road — Between the Refugees and Camp, Late Afternoon*

You smell it before you see it. Not the distant, theoretical smoke of the southern horizon — this is close, recent, the thick black smoke of things that should not be burning. Wood. Thatch. Something organic that you do not want to identify.

The farmstead is two hundred yards off the road, set back against a tree line. The barn is fully ablaze. The farmhouse roof is burning from the east end — the fire was set there first and is working its way west. A Dragon Army patrol is in the yard: three soldiers and something else, something taller, with scales that catch the firelight. An officer. The Bozak stands apart from the soldiers, watching the burn with the detached attention of a thing that is checking a task off a list.

From inside the barn: screaming. A woman's voice. A man's voice, lower, shouting something you cannot hear over the fire.

Caeron pulls the column to a halt. He looks at the farmstead. He looks at you. 'Squire,' he says. And the word means: *you decide. This is what the Measure is for.*

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run the encounter at your table, then skip to **AFTER THE FIGHT**.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow the rounds below. Roll when prompted.

> **INJURED NPCs — FARMER HANNA AND DARRIC**
> **Hanna** (inside barn): Severe burns on arms and chest. Needs magic healing or she dies. Paladin Cure Wounds (1 spell slot), Paladin Lay on Hands (10+ HP from pool), Greater Potion of Healing, or Mira + herbs (stabilize + 1d6+2, but burns need magic to fully heal). Bandages alone are not enough — they stabilize but Hanna will lose the use of her hands.
> **Darric** (inside barn): Dislocated shoulder, smoke inhalation. Medicine DC 14 + bandage, or Mira (automatic), or any healing spell/potion. Less critical but in pain.
> *Record any resources spent.*
> **If both healed:** Hanna and Darric appear in Vogler. Hanna's hands work. Darric volunteers for the defence. +2 ROSE.
> **If only Darric healed:** They reach Vogler but Hanna cannot work. Darric is bitter but grateful. +1 ROSE.
> **If neither healed:** They do not make it to Vogler. The road takes them.

> **COMPANION SELECTION**
> Full party is available. Caeron calls the intervention — this is not optional.
> **Aldric** — Takes the Bozak head-on. Brave or foolish. Both.
> **Mira** — Essential for the civilians. She will run for the barn the moment it is safe.
> **Sera** — Ranged fire. Picks off soldiers from the treeline.
> **Serath** — Knows Dragon Army patrol timing. 'We have ten minutes before the next squad.'
> **Lysander** — Veteran assault. He has done this before. His face says he wishes he had not.
> **Thessaly** — Documents. Witnesses. Her pen is shaking but it is moving.
> **Vael** — Warns about the Bozak's spellcasting. 'It has Burning Hands and Lightning Bolt. Do not cluster.'
>
> Choose up to 3 companions for combat. The rest assist with the barn rescue.

> **ENEMY STAT BLOCKS (Pen & Paper)**
> **Human Soldier (3):** AC 14 (chain shirt + shield), HP 16, Speed 30ft. Longsword +5 (1d8+3). Javelin +5 (1d6+3, 30/120). Formation: +1 AC when adjacent to another soldier.
> **Bozak Draconian (1):** AC 15 (natural + studded leather), HP 30, Speed 30ft. Greatsword +5 (2d6+3). Burning Hands (3d6 fire, 15ft cone, DC 12 DEX half, 1/encounter). Lightning Bolt (2d10 lightning, 30ft line, DC 13 DEX half, 1/encounter). Death Throes: bones explode — 1d6 thunder damage in 10ft radius, DC 13 DEX to avoid.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 1

The soldiers see you coming. Two of them form up — shields locked, longswords ready, the mechanical discipline of men who do this for pay. The third is still at the barn door, making sure the fire does its work. The Bozak turns its head slowly, as if the interruption is a minor inconvenience. It draws a greatsword with one hand — a gesture that should require two and does not.

The barn screams are louder now. The fire is winning.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Choose a target:**
> **Soldier (left)** / **Soldier (right)** / **Soldier at barn door** / **Bozak officer**
>
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC (Soldiers: 14, Bozak: 15)
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **IF VAEL IS PRESENT:** 'The Bozak will cast first. Spread out.' You know to expect Burning Hands.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:**
> **Aldric:** A) Flank (+1 next attack) | B) Shield Wall (+1 AC) | C) Charge the Bozak — Aggressive Strike (1d8+2, takes 1d4, draws Bozak attention)
> **Sera:** A) Scout Shot — targets soldier at barn door (1d6 dmg) | B) Mark Bozak (+2 next attack vs Bozak) | C) Cover Fire (+1 AC)
> **Mira:** A) Rush to barn — begins rescue (needs barn door cleared first) | B) Herbal Boost (+1 save vs fire) | C) Bandage (stabilize nearest wounded)
> **Serath:** A) Intel (+2 one attack) | B) Circle behind — Dagger Strike on barn-door soldier (1d4+2) | C) Feint Bozak (Bozak -1 next attack)
> **Lysander:** A) Combat Instruction (+2 attack) | B) Veteran Strike — engages nearest soldier (1d10+3) | C) Guard — positions to take Bozak's first spell
> **Thessaly:** A) Encourage (+1 next roll) | B) Document (+1 ROSE after) | C) Distraction — calls to soldiers in Common: 'Solamnic column! Surrender!' (one soldier hesitates, skips attack)
> **Vael:** A) Flanking Shot (1d6 dmg) | B) Honest Assessment (reveal Bozak HP) | C) Warning Shot — forces Bozak to use Burning Hands defensively (halves cone area)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):**
> • (Paladin) Cast Bless: +1d4 to attacks and saves for up to 3 targets, Concentration, lasts entire combat. 1 spell slot.
> • (Paladin) Divine Smite: Bonus action after hitting with a melee weapon. 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). Once per turn. 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest at level 2+).
> • (Paladin) Lay on Hands: Heal self or ally. Bonus action.
> • (Paladin) Cure Wounds: 2d8+CHA heal. 1 spell slot. Replaces attack.
> • (Fighter) Action Surge: Additional Action this round (except Magic). 1/short or long rest.
> • (Fighter) Second Wind: 1d10+[level] HP. Bonus action. 2 uses/long rest, regain 1/short rest.
> • (Any) Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action.

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 1

The Bozak opens with fire. Its hand comes up, palm forward, and the air between you ignites — not flame exactly, but a cone of superheated air that smells of sulfur and hate.

> **BURNING HANDS — DEX save DC 12:**
> **SUCCESS:** Half damage. You roll clear.
> **FAILURE:** 3d6 fire damage. The heat is extraordinary. Your tabard smoulders.
> **IF VAEL WARNED YOU:** Advantage on the save (roll twice, take higher).
> **IF LYSANDER CHOSE GUARD:** Lysander steps in front. He takes the damage instead. His face does not change. His armour steams.
>
> **Soldier attack:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+3 slashing damage.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 2

The barn-door soldier is the key. As long as he is there, Mira cannot reach the barn. Hanna's screams are getting weaker, which is worse than them being loud.

The Bozak is reloading — the Burning Hands cost it something, you can see it in the way the scales along its arm are darkened. It reaches for the greatsword. The spell was its opening gambit. Now comes the steel.

> **ATHLETICS CHECK (optional, replaces attack):** Roll 1d20 + STR modifier | DC 14
> Break the barn door open. If the barn-door soldier is dead or engaged, this succeeds automatically.
> **SUCCESS:** The door breaks. Smoke pours out. Mira can enter (or you can).
> **FAILURE:** The door holds. The hinges are warped by heat. One more round.

> **YOUR ATTACK:** (if not breaking the door)
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 2

The Bozak engages in melee. The greatsword comes in a wide arc — too wide for indoors, perfect for the open yard. It has reach and strength and the particular arrogance of something that considers you a minor obstacle.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (Bozak greatsword):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15
> **SUCCESS:** You duck the arc. The sword bites dirt.
> **FAILURE:** 2d6+3 slashing damage. The greatsword is not subtle. It does not need to be.
>
> **INVESTIGATION CHECK (free, if barn is open):** Roll 1d20 + INT modifier | DC 13
> **SUCCESS:** Water source — a trough by the fence. Dump it on Hanna's burns. Stabilizes her without magic.
> **FAILURE:** You do not see it. Magic healing or Mira's herbs are the only options.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 3

**IF SERATH IS NOT PRESENT:** A horn sounds from the south road. Another Dragon Army patrol has heard the fighting. They will arrive in 3 rounds. End this fast.
**IF SERATH IS PRESENT:** 'We have time. The next patrol is south of the ridge. We are clear.' No reinforcements.

The Bozak is wounded but fighting. It is the last significant threat — the soldiers are dead, fleeing, or pinned. The farmyard smells of smoke and blood and the chemical stink of draconian. Behind you, the barn fire is being fought by whoever you sent — Mira with wet blankets, or your own hands, or nobody at all.

> **SURVIVAL CHECK (optional):** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 12
> Track the patrol's approach. If Serath is not present, success gives you 1 extra round before reinforcements.
> **IF SERATH IS PRESENT:** Automatic success. No need to roll.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Finish the Bozak.**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC 15
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
> **BOZAK DEATH THROES:** If the Bozak drops to 0 HP, its bones EXPLODE. 1d6 thunder damage, 10ft radius. **DEX save DC 13** or take full damage. *You were warned. Move.*

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 3

The Bozak knows it is losing. It channels the last of its energy — Lightning Bolt, a 30ft line of blue-white electricity that cracks the air and leaves the taste of copper in your mouth.

> **LIGHTNING BOLT — DEX save DC 13:**
> **SUCCESS:** Half damage. You throw yourself sideways.
> **FAILURE:** 2d10 lightning damage. The world goes white. Your muscles lock. The pain is immediate and total.
> **IF VAEL IS PRESENT:** Advantage on the save. You knew it was coming.

---

### AFTER THE FIGHT

The Bozak's bones detonate and the sound is like a thunderclap in a bottle — sharp, contained, final. The soldiers are dead or fled. The farmyard is quiet except for the fire, which is dying now, and the sound of someone crying inside the barn.

Hanna is burned badly. Her arms, her chest. She was shielding Darric and the fire found her. Darric has a dislocated shoulder and the cough of a man who breathed too much smoke. They are alive. Whether they stay that way depends on what you do in the next five minutes.

> **MEDICINE CHECK — DARRIC:** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 14
> Reset the shoulder, treat smoke inhalation.
> **SUCCESS:** Darric stabilizes. He can walk. He is in pain but functional.
> **FAILURE:** The shoulder is worse than it looked. Mira (if present) can still treat him. Without Mira, he needs a sling and time.

> **HEALING HANNA — REQUIRES MAGIC OR MIRA:**
> • Paladin Cure Wounds (1 spell slot): Heals burns. Hanna's hands will work.
> • Paladin Lay on Hands (10+ HP): Same result.
> • Mira (if present) + herbs: Stabilizes. Burns heal slowly — Hanna's hands work but with scars.
> • Greater Potion of Healing: Full recovery.
> • Potion of Healing: Partial — stabilizes but burns remain serious.
> • Bandage only: Stabilizes at 1 HP. Hanna lives but her hands may not fully recover.
> *Record resources spent.*

> **SEARCH THE FALLEN (Optional — moral choice):**
> The soldiers are dead. The Bozak is bone fragments. The officer's satchel survived the explosion.
>
> **Bozak officer's satchel:** No moral penalty — enemy intelligence. Contains: patrol routes, supply line maps, a letter in Draconic that Caeron will want to read. +1d6 stl.
>
> **Soldier bodies:**
> **A) Search them.** (-1 ROSE. Loot Roll below.)
> **B) Leave them. You have done enough.** (+1 ROSE. No loot.)

> **LOOT ROLL (if searched):** Roll 1d20.
> 1–5: Nothing. Dragon Army soldiers carry nothing personal. They were not allowed to.
> 6–10: 1d4 stl. Standard issue pay. 1 day rations (Dragon Army field pack).
> 11–14: 2d4 stl + mundane item (2 days rations, a signal whistle, a bedroll).
> 15–17: 3d4 stl + Potion of Healing (standard issue, one per squad). 2 days rations.
> 18–19: 4d4 stl + quality item (an officer's compass, worth 5 stl to the right buyer). 3 days rations.
> 20: 5d4 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL. 3 days rations.

> **RARE ITEM ROLL:** Roll 1d20.
> 1–19: Quality mundane item (Dragon Army chain mail, AC 16, good condition but unmarked).
> 20: MAGIC ITEM — +1 Longsword. Solamnic make. Taken from a fallen knight. The Bozak was carrying it as a trophy. Returning it to a Solamnic armoury grants +2 CROWN. Keeping it is not dishonourable — it was earned.

> **FARMSTEAD CELLAR:** Investigation DC 13. (No moral penalty — searching for survivors/supplies.)
> **SUCCESS:** Stash Loot Roll:
> 1–5: Empty. The family had nothing worth hiding.
> 6–10: Preserved food, 1d4 stl in a clay jar.
> 11–14: 2d6 stl + Potion of Healing (Hanna's grandmother's recipe, same as Vogler).
> 15–17: 3d6 stl + quality item (a family sword, longsword, well-maintained).
> 18–19: 4d6 stl + a hidden strongbox (the family's life savings — taking this is not theft if you ask, but refusing it is +1 ROSE).
> 20: 5d6 stl + RARE ITEM ROLL.

> **NPC GRATITUDE — HANNA AND DARRIC** (if healed)
> Darric cannot speak for a while. When he does, it is one sentence: 'You came.' Hanna holds her bandaged hands against her chest and looks at you with the expression of a woman who is recalculating everything she thought she knew about Solamnic knights.
>
> **ROLL:** Persuasion (+[bonus]) | CHA | DC 10
>
> **10–12 (Modest):** 1d4 stl. 'Take it. Please. It is the least—' Hanna cannot finish the sentence.
> **13–15 (Grateful):** 2d4 stl and Hanna's dagger — small, plain, sharp as a razor. 'It was my mother's. Use it better than I can now.' (+1 to one attack, single use, as a lucky charm.)
> **16–18 (Deeply Grateful):** 3d4 stl, the dagger, and Darric's promise: he volunteers for Vogler's defence. +1 to Vogler defence checks.
> **19+ (Indebted):** 4d4 stl, the dagger, Darric's service, and Hanna's recipe book (trade goods worth 10 stl in Vogler, or keep for +1 to Medicine checks — Hanna's grandmother knew things).
> **FAILURE (1–9):** They have nothing. They lost everything. Hanna holds your hand with her bandaged fingers and does not let go. +1 ROSE. *If both survived, the reward improves by one tier.*

> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots,
> Lay on Hands pool, bandages, potions consumed.
> Update gold if loot was found. Record any items gained.
> Note if Hanna and/or Darric were saved (affects Vogler).
> **Short rest available:** Recover Action Surge, regain 1 Second Wind use. HP: spend Hit Dice.

> **XP:** 15 XP per soldier (45 total). 30 XP for the Bozak. Bonus 15 XP if Hanna healed. Bonus 10 XP if Darric healed. Bonus 10 XP if barn door broken Round 2.

> **A) The farmstead is ashes. The family is alive. You ride on toward camp. The smoke on the horizon is not theoretical anymore.** --> Scene 64D

## SCENE 64D — MAKING CAMP

*South Road — Day 2, Evening*

The light fails faster this far south — the treeline cuts the horizon higher and the autumn sun drops behind it like a stone into water. Caeron calls the halt at a clearing that has been used before: fire-blackened stones in a ring, a water source thirty yards east, and the particular flatness of ground that has been slept on by enough people to lose its original character.

Making camp is ritual now. You know your role without being told — fire duty, perimeter stones, the particular arrangement of gear that means sleep is available within arm's reach of everything you might need in a hurry. Aldric handles the horses. Mira, if present, claims the flattest ground for the medical kit without discussion. The efficiency of it steadies something.

The smoke on the southern horizon is closer. Not dramatically — a mile, maybe two. But the quality has changed. Yesterday it was distant and theoretical. Tonight it is a fact you can smell on the wind when it shifts.

> **RATIONS — EVENING MEAL (Day 2)**
> Garrison supplies are gone. You eat from your own pack tonight.
> **Consume 1 ration.** Mark it off your character sheet.
>
> **IF YOU HAVE NO RATIONS:**
> You sit by the fire with an empty stomach and try not to look at other people eating.
>
> **IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** He notices before you say anything. He always notices. He breaks his bread in half and puts the larger piece on your knee without looking at you. 'Eat it before I change my mind.' A pause. 'You know, for someone who passed the garrison supply room every day, you are remarkably bad at planning.' He means: *I am worried about you and this is the only way I know how to say it.* **Aldric covers your meal. No ration consumed. Aldric cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY (and Aldric is not, or Aldric already covered):** She produces a wrapped bundle — herbs, dried fruit, a flatbread she baked at Brightholm and has been carrying since. 'I made extra. I always make extra.' She looks at you with the quiet expectation of someone who heals people for a living and considers hunger a wound. 'Next time, pack properly. I am a healer, not a quartermaster.' **Mira covers your meal. No ration consumed. Mira cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF SERA IS IN YOUR PARTY (and no one above can cover):** Sera drops a strip of dried venison in your lap without breaking stride. 'Found it on a scout. Do not ask which scout.' She is already walking away. Then, over her shoulder: 'That is the only time, Squire. Learn to count your supplies or learn to go hungry. I will not save you from arithmetic.' **Sera covers your meal. No ration consumed. Sera cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF NO COMPANION CAN COVER:** You go hungry. Apply hunger penalty (see Combat Reference). The fire smells like other people's food.
>
> *Record your current ration count on your character sheet.*

**IF THESSALY IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She has her map out, marking the refugees' direction and the smoke's position with the methodical precision of someone building a record they expect to need.

**IF SERATH IS IN YOUR PARTY:** They are watching the smoke with the flat attention of someone who has seen what makes it. They do not share what they are thinking. The way they check their blade says enough.

> **A) Help Aldric with the horses. The work is quiet and good.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 65
>
> **B) Sit with the fire. Let the day settle.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 65
>
> **C) Ask Caeron about tomorrow's route. He has been studying the map.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 65

## SCENE 65 — THE ROAD AMBUSH

*South Road — Forest Edge, Day 2*

Arrows from the treeline, then three Dragon Army soldiers and a Sivak Draconian Officer. Not a patrol. Assassins. They have a description of Solamnic squire colours. They have found you.

> **COMBAT ENCOUNTER — DRAGON ARMY ASSASSIN SQUAD**
>
> **ENEMIES:**
> • Human Soldier x3: AC 14, HP 14 each. Longsword +4 1d8+2. Crossbow +4 1d8+2.
> • Sivak Draconian (Officer): AC 16, HP 48. Greatsword +6 2d6+4. Speed 40 ft., Fly 60 ft.
> • Sivak: Shape Steal — on death by melee, takes the killer's appearance. Commander's Aura: soldiers within 30 ft. get +1 to attacks.
>
> **IMPORTANT:** Do not kill the Sivak in melee — it will Shape Steal your appearance. Use ranged attacks or force it to flee.
>
> Rewards: 50 XP. Sivak carries sealed orders naming you as a specific target.
>
> Fallen (0 HP): Aldric holds the Sivak while you are stabilised. 1 HP, one exhaustion.

> **A) The ambush is broken. Continue to Scene 66.** --> Scene 66

The sealed orders have your name in them. Caeron looks at this for a long time. 'They know about the dispatch,' he says. 'And about you.' He folds the paper. 'Good — if they are targeting you specifically, that means what you have been doing has mattered enough.'

### SCENE 66B_Aldric — WHAT HE CARRIES

He tells you about his mother. She died when he was twelve. 'I compete with you because I do not know another way to tell someone they matter to me. I am working on it. It is slow.'

> **A) 'I know. I have always known.' He looks away. The fire crackles. After a while he picks up the whetstone again, but slower now.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 66B
> **B) 'You are better at it than you think.' He almost laughs. The sound is warm. You leave him to his sharpening.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 66B


### SCENE 66B_Thessaly — WHAT SHE FEARS

'I am afraid of writing the history that says they fell.' She opens the locket. Inside: a page from a letter her mother wrote the week before the Cataclysm. 'When the world changes, the people who write it down are the ones who decide what it meant.'

> **A) 'You are. I have seen you work.' She closes the locket. The pen starts again.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 66B
> **B) 'Then write the version where we hold.' She looks at you. Then writes something down.** (+1 SWORD, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 66B


### SCENE 66B_Mira — WHAT SHE KNOWS

'I know what two thousand soldiers means. In medical terms. I know the arithmetic does not work.' She is not afraid. She is past afraid. 'I will be there anyway.'

> **A) 'The arithmetic never accounts for the people who refuse to stop.' She is quiet. Then: 'No. It does not.' She goes back to her supplies.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 66B
> **B) Help her count. The counting helps. When you finish, her hands are steadier.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 66B


### SCENE 66B_Serath — WHAT THEY LOST

'I had a unit. Twelve people. When I left, I left them inside. They are in the army marching on Vogler. I may see people I know across the line. I will not hesitate. But I want you to know it costs something.'

> **A) 'I will stand beside you when it does.' They nod once. The fire settles.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 66B
> **B) 'If you need to step back, I will cover you.' They look at you for a long time. Then back at the fire.** (+2 ROSE) --> Scene 66B


### SCENE 66B_Caeron — WHAT HE HIDES

'I have never led people into a situation where I cannot guarantee their survival.' He turns. His face is the face of a man who is thirty years old and does not know if he is enough. 'I wanted someone to know.'

> **A) 'You are enough. We will hold.' He does not respond for a long time. Then he stands and walks into the dark. But the set of his shoulders has changed.** (+2 CROWN, +1 ROSE) --> Scene 66B
> **B) 'Then we hold for as long as we can.' He nods. The nod of an officer who has received an answer he can use.** (+1 CROWN, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 66B

### SCENE 66B_Tariel — THE QUESTION


'If the Oath is what you say it is — why is Vogler undefended? Why were the refugees turned south? Why is a squire being sent where a regiment should be?'

**CONVICTION CHOICE (FALLEN is possible here):**

> **A) 'Because the institution is failing does not mean the principle is wrong. I am the principle.' She watches you say this. Then looks away. The fire is lower now.** (CONVICTION: STEADFAST. +2 ROSE.) --> Scene 66B

### SCENE 66B_Lysander — THE LAST FIRE


'I took the Oath at nineteen. I meant every word. I stopped meaning them when the system rewarded the decision to let people die and punished the decision to save them, and did both correctly according to its own rules.'

'I am not telling you not to take the Oath. I am telling you: the words are not the thing. You are the thing.'

**CONVICTION CHOICE (FALLEN is possible here):**

I am not sure that is good.'** (CONVICTION: FALLEN. +1 ROSE, -2 CROWN. **BROKEN SWORD — FULL.**) --> Scene 66B

>

## SCENE DATE_ALDRIC — WHAT THE HANDS SAY

*Forest Road — Camp Edge, Night*

He is doing the thing he does when he cannot sleep: walking the perimeter with the whetstone in his hand, running his thumb along the edge without sharpening anything. You fall into step beside him. He does not look at you. He does not need to.

'I have been thinking about Vogler,' he says. The admission costs him something — Aldric does not think about things, he does things, and the gap between those two states is where his fear lives. 'I keep running the numbers. The walls, the bridge, the garrison we do not have. And then I stop running the numbers because the numbers do not help.'

He stops walking. Turns. In the firelight the scar on his jaw is a thin line of silver and his eyes are the particular dark that means he has decided to say the next thing regardless of what it costs.

'The numbers do not help. But you do.' He is looking at you now — really looking, without the deflection or the competition or the whetstone to occupy his hands. 'I am not good at this. At saying things. I am good at standing next to people and hoping they understand what it means that I chose to stand there.' A breath. 'I am standing here.'

His hand finds yours. Not the way it happens in songs — fumbling, a little too tight, the grip of a man who holds everything like a sword because that is the only grip he trusts. Then he adjusts. Softens. Learns the difference.

You stand at the edge of the firelight and the dark and you hold his hand and neither of you says anything else for a while because he was right. Standing there is enough.

Then he turns your hand over and traces the callus on your sword hand with his thumb. Slowly. The roughness of his fingers against your palm. He is memorising the shape of your hand the way he memorises terrain — deliberately, thoroughly, like something he intends to defend.

'After Vogler,' he says. He does not finish the sentence. He does not need to.

> **A) Finish it for him. 'After Vogler, you are still standing here.'** He closes his eyes. When he opens them something has changed and it is not going to change back. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Aldric) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Pull him closer. Not gently. He does not need gentle. He needs to know you are as certain as he is.** His breath catches. Then his arms are around you and he is holding you the way he holds a position — completely, with everything, like letting go has never occurred to him as an option. The kiss, when it happens, is not tentative. It is a decision. (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD, ROMANCE FLAME Aldric) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) 'You do not have to be good at saying things.' Lean your head against his shoulder. Let the fire burn down.** He is very still. Then his cheek rests against the top of your head and you can feel his breathing slow and the tension leave his body one muscle at a time, like a garrison standing down. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE DATE_THESSALY — THE THIRD VERSION

*Forest Road — Camp Edge, Night*

She is sitting on the fallen log at the edge of camp with her notebook open and her pen behind her ear and the locket in her hand. The locket is open. You have never seen the locket open when she knows someone is watching.

She does not close it when she sees you. That is how you know tonight is different.

'Sit,' she says. Not a request. An observation that you were going to sit anyway and she is acknowledging the inevitability.

You sit. The notebook is between you. She has written three columns — you can see the headers even in the firelight: PROFESSIONAL, HONEST, and a third column she has scratched out so thoroughly the paper is torn.

'The third column,' she says, watching you look at it, 'is the one where I write what I actually want instead of what I am willing to admit.' She turns toward you. The firelight catches the locket and the thing inside it — a scrap of paper, handwriting you cannot read at this distance. 'I am tired of scratching things out.'

She reaches up and takes the pen from behind her ear. Holds it out to you. 'Write something in the third column. Not what you think I want to read. What you would write if you knew no one would ever see it.'

You take the pen. Your fingers brush hers. She does not pull away. Her hand is smaller than you expected — ink-stained at the fingertips, a callus on the middle finger from years of writing, and warm in a way that makes you aware of how cold the night air is by contrast.

You write something. She reads it. Her face does the thing it does when she has received information that changes a conclusion she was already committed to — a small reorganisation behind the eyes, a breath held and released.

'Good,' she says. Very quiet. Then she takes the pen back and writes something beneath it. She turns the notebook so you can read it.

It is not professional. It is not even honest, in the way she uses the word — careful, verified, sourceable. It is the other thing. The thing she does not put in dispatches.

She watches you read it. 'I would like,' she says, 'to stop being the person who writes about the world happening and start being the person it happens to. Tonight. With you.'

The locket is still open. In the firelight you can finally read the scrap of paper inside it: a single line in her own handwriting, old enough that the ink has faded. *Remember what wanting feels like.*

She is remembering.

> **A) Kiss her. She has written enough. The pen falls somewhere. Neither of you looks for it.** The notebook slides off the log. Her hand is on the back of your neck and she kisses the way she writes — precisely, thoroughly, with the focused attention of someone who has been composing this sentence for weeks and is finally putting the pen to the page. The locket presses cold between you and then warms. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Thessaly) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) 'Read me the second column. The honest one.' She reads it. Her voice in the dark, reading sentences about you that are true and unflinching and kinder than anything she has said aloud. When she finishes, close the notebook. 'Now tell me the parts you did not write down.'** She tells you. It takes a long time. She is shaking by the end — not from cold. You hold her hand through all of it and the pen stays on the ground and the night is very long and very honest and neither of you sleeps. (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN, ROMANCE FLAME Thessaly) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Write something else in the third column. Something that makes her laugh — really laugh, the sound she never makes when she thinks anyone important is listening. Then something that does not make her laugh. Then close the notebook.** 'Enough writing,' you say. She nods. You sit together until the fire is embers, trading the pen back and forth, filling the margins with things neither of you will say aloud, and at some point her head is on your shoulder and the pen is still and the notebook is full of a conversation that no one will ever read. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

---


## SCENE DATE_MIRA — THE HEALER'S HANDS

*Forest Road — Mira's Station, Night*

She has not stopped moving since the column halted. You have been watching — not deliberately, but with the peripheral awareness that comes from caring about someone who does not care about themselves with sufficient diligence. She checked Aldric's shoulder. She rebound Sera's wrist. She counted the supplies twice and reorganised the surgical kit three times and now she is sitting with her back against the supply cart and her hands in her lap and she is not moving because she has run out of motion.

'Mira.'

'I am fine.' She says it the way she says everything — practically, efficiently, with the specific conviction of someone who has diagnosed herself and refuses to accept the diagnosis. Then: 'I am not fine. I have been fine for eleven hours and the contract has expired.'

You sit beside her. Close enough that your shoulders touch. She does not lean away. She leans in — just barely, a degree of weight that says she has been holding herself upright through professional obligation and the obligation has clocked out for the night.

Her hands are shaking. Not dramatically — a fine tremor in the fingers, the kind that comes from sustained precision work. Healing hands. They have been healing all day and now they have nothing to heal and they do not know how to stop.

You take her hands. She lets you. They are cold and rougher than you expected — callused differently from sword hands, the pads thick from grinding herbs, a thin scar across the left palm where she told you a blade slipped during her first field surgery. You hold them and she watches you hold them with the expression of someone who has spent her life putting other people back together and has forgotten what it feels like from the other side.

'No one—' She stops. Starts again. 'I am always the one who holds the hands. It is what I do. I hold the hands and I count the breathing and I am steady because someone has to be steady. And it works. It always works. Except that after a while you forget that your hands need holding too.'

She is crying. Quietly, efficiently, even her grief organised — tears running but breathing controlled, the discipline of a woman who learned a long time ago to fall apart without making a sound. You do not wipe the tears away. You hold her hands and you let her cry and you are steady because someone has to be steady and tonight it is your turn.

After a while the trembling stops. She breathes out. Looks at your hands holding hers. 'You have a blister forming on your left index finger,' she says. 'The grip on your sword is too tight. I will wrap it in the morning.' She laughs — small, wet, the ghost of humour returning. 'I cannot stop. I am sorry. I look at you and I see things that need tending.'

'Then tend them.' You turn your hand over. Offer her the blister, the calluses, the accumulated small damages of a month on the road. Not because they need healing. Because she needs to heal.

She unwraps a strip of bandage — her hands steady now, the muscle memory taking over. She wraps your finger with the absent-minded care of someone performing a task so familiar it has become a form of love. When she finishes, she does not let go.

'Stay,' she says. 'I do not need healing. I need—' She looks at you. 'I need someone to sit with me and not need anything.'

> **A) Stay. All night. She falls asleep against your shoulder sometime around the third hour and you do not move because the weight of her sleeping is the most important thing you have ever carried.** When she wakes she is embarrassed. You are not. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Mira) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Kiss the top of her head. 'I am here. I do not need anything.' She makes a sound that is either a laugh or a sob or both and her arms go around you and she holds on the way she never allows herself to hold on — not as a healer, not as the steady one, just as a woman who is frightened and tired and has finally found the one person she trusts enough to be both.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Mira) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) 'Tell me about the scar on your left hand. The real story, not the field surgery version.'** She tells you. It is a longer story than you expected and it involves a boy she loved when she was sixteen and a window she climbed out of and a knife she grabbed the wrong way in the dark. She is laughing by the end. Properly laughing. The tremor is gone. (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_SERA — AFTER THE ASSESSMENT

*Forest Road — Ridge Overlook, Night*

She is on the ridge because Sera is always on the ridge. High ground, clear sightlines, two exits — she chooses her positions the way she chooses everything: with the absolute precision of someone who has turned survival into an art form. You climb up. She watched you coming for two minutes before you started climbing and she already has an opinion about your approach angle.

'Your left,' she says. 'You favour your left on uneven ground. An archer would notice.'

'I am not worried about archers. I am worried about you.'

Something shifts in her face. The professional mask — the Scout Nighthollow mask, precise and cool and always slightly ahead of everyone else — holds for a half-second longer and then adjusts. Not gone. Loosened. The way armour shifts when you undo one strap.

She looks at you. The moonlight does something to her face that the daylight does not — softens the angles, finds the version of her that exists underneath the competence. She is beautiful in the way that dangerous things are beautiful, which is to say: you are very aware that this is a person who could kill you from this distance before you registered the shot, and the fact that she is choosing not to is its own form of intimacy.

'I do not do this,' she says. 'I observe. I report. I do not—' She gestures between you. The gesture is the least precise thing she has ever done. 'This. Whatever this is. I do not have a field manual for this.'

'You have assessed me.'

'Constantly.' No hesitation. 'Your sword grip, your footwork, your breathing pattern during stress, the way your eyes move when you enter a room, the scar on your right forearm that you got from a training accident you have never told anyone about.' She is not looking at you. She is looking at the horizon. 'I have assessed you every day since the courtyard. I have filed detailed mental reports. None of them are adequate.'

'What are they missing?'

She turns. Steps closer. The distance between you narrows to an arm's length and then to less and she moves the way she moves through the dark — without sound, without warning, with the absolute commitment of someone who has chosen her angle of approach and is not going to change it.

'They are missing the part where I stop assessing.' Her voice is lower than you have heard it. Her hand finds the front of your shirt — not pulling, just resting there, feeling the heartbeat underneath. 'Your pulse just increased. You are breathing faster. Your pupils are dilated.' She is cataloguing you and the cataloguing has become something else, the clinical attention turning warm and focused and very close. 'I am going to stop assessing now.'

She kisses you. It is — like everything Sera does — precise. Deliberate. And then approximately three seconds in, it is not precise at all. It is the controlled professional losing control and the loss is dizzying and mutual and her hands are in your hair and your hands are on her waist and she makes a sound against your mouth that is the least tactical thing she has ever done.

When she pulls back her breathing is uneven. She looks at you. The mask is gone entirely. Underneath it she is younger and more startled and more wanting than you have ever seen her.

'I am going to need a moment,' she says, 'to recalibrate.'

'Take your time.'

'That is not what I want to do with my time.' She pulls you back.

> **A) The ridge. The moonlight. The woman who sees everything, finally letting herself be seen. Stay until you have both forgotten what precision feels like.** The night is very long and neither of you uses it for sleeping and in the morning she will be Sera Nighthollow again, the mask back in place, the assessment running. But she will look at you once, across the camp, and the mask will slip for a half-second, and that half-second will be worth everything. (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD, ROMANCE FLAME Sera) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) 'I see you too.' Tell her what you have observed — the way she checks the perimeter twice when she is nervous, the way she touches the bowstring when she is thinking, the way she looks south and her jaw tightens. Show her that assessment goes both ways.** She is very quiet when you finish. Then: 'No one has ever watched me back.' The second kiss is slower. The third is not slow at all. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Sera) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Hold her. Not strategically. Not with any angle of approach. Just hold her and let the competence rest for one night.** She is stiff at first — her body does not know how to be held without a tactical purpose — and then something releases, a tension she has been carrying since long before you met her, and she fits against you with a sigh that says she has been waiting for someone to make this feel safe. (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_VAEL — THE LAST PASS

*Forest Road — Clearing, Dusk*

She found the clearing twenty minutes ago and has been running forms since — not the regulation drills Caeron assigns but the real ones, the Ashmore family forms she has never shown anyone. You can tell by the footwork. It is faster than standard. Sharper. The blade traces patterns in the dusk light that look like writing in a language you almost understand.

She sees you. Does not stop. Finishes the form. The last motion is a high cut that ends with the blade perfectly still, the tip at throat height, her breathing even. She holds the position for a three-count. Lowers the blade.

'Staring is rude,' she says. She is smiling. The Vael smile — competitive, warm, the dare already forming.

'I was studying.'

'You were staring. I can tell the difference. When you study, your weight shifts left.' She tosses you a practice sword. You catch it. She notices the catch. 'Good. You are getting faster.'

The spar starts the way their spars always start: measured, technical, two people who have learned each other's patterns through months of daily repetition. She leads with the high guard she favours. You counter with the low redirect that works against it. She adjusts. You adjust. The conversation is in the steel and the footwork and the breathing.

Then it changes.

> **OPTIONAL ROLL:** Athletics (+3) | STR | DC 12
> **SUCCESS (roll 12+):** You land the hit. She was not expecting it. Her eyes widen — not with pain, with surprise, and then with something hotter and more immediate than surprise.
> **FAILURE (roll 1-11):** She lands the hit. Your guard was open and she took it. But the way she follows through — checking the strike at the last instant, the blade resting against your chest instead of striking — is not how you end a spar. It is how you hold someone still.

She drops the practice sword. 'Enough.'

The distance between you is a blade's width. You can feel the heat coming off her — exertion and something else, the flush rising up her neck, her chest rising and falling with each breath. Her hair has come loose from the tie and there is a strand across her face and she is not moving it and you are very aware that she is not moving it on purpose.

'I have been thinking,' she says, 'about what it means that the only person I cannot beat is the only person I want to—' She stops. Swallows. Vael Ashmore does not hesitate. She is hesitating. 'The only person I want.'

The practice sword is on the ground. Her hands are empty for the first time since you have known her and she does not know what to do with them and that uncertainty is the most honest thing she has ever shown you.

> **A) Show her what empty hands are for. Close the distance. Her breath hitches when your hand finds her waist and then her mouth finds yours and the competitive energy that has been building for months converts into something incandescent.** She kisses like she fights — fully committed, no guard, and when you finally break apart she is breathing hard and her eyes are bright and she says, 'Best two out of three,' and she is not talking about the spar. (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD, ROMANCE FLAME Vael) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Take her hands. Hold them still. 'You know exactly what to do with them.' She looks at your hands holding hers and her face does something you have never seen — open, unguarded, the competitor gone and just the woman underneath. She steps closer. Presses her forehead against yours. Breathes.** 'I never lose,' she whispers. 'And I have completely lost this.' She is shaking. You hold her until she stops. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Vael) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Pick up the practice swords. Hand hers back. 'Again. This time without holding back.' The spar that follows is the best either of you has ever fought and when it ends you are both on the ground, breathing hard, laughing, and the distance between you is nothing and the stars are overhead and neither of you moves to stand up.** (+1 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_CAERON — THE WEIGHT OF COMMAND

*Forest Road — Command Tent, Night*

He is alone. This is unusual — Caeron is never alone; he is always *commanding*, always visible, always the version of himself that other people require. But the tent flap is half-closed and the light inside is a single candle and when you enter he does not straighten. He does not compose his face. He is sitting with the dispatch in his hand and the dispatch has been read so many times the paper is soft at the folds.

'Two thousand,' he says. Not to you. To the number. 'I have forty-seven. Forty-eight if I count you, which I do.'

'Caeron.'

He looks up. The candlelight finds the lines around his eyes that you did not notice before — lines that come from sustained squinting against things that should not have to be borne, the particular cartography of a man who has been holding the weight of everyone else's survival since before it was fair to ask him to. He is thirty years old. He looks older. He looks, for the first time since you have known him, like he is not enough.

'I wanted to see you,' you say.

'Why?' He is genuinely asking. Not fishing for reassurance. Genuinely unable to construct a reason why someone would seek out his company tonight, here, where he is not Lord Caeron of Ashvale but just a man with a dispatch and a number that does not work.

You sit across from him. Take the dispatch. Set it face-down on the table.

'Because you are not a dispatch. You are not a number. And tonight I do not want to talk to my commanding officer. I want to talk to you.'

Something breaks in his face. Not dramatically — a crack in the masonry, the kind you only see if you know where the load-bearing walls are. His mouth opens. Closes. He looks away. Looks back. His eyes are bright and he is furious about it.

'I am not—' His voice catches. He clears his throat with the dignity of a man who would rather face the Dragon Army than admit to a feeling. 'I am not accustomed to being seen. In that way. By anyone.'

'I know.'

'I have maintained—' He stops. Starts again. 'The command structure requires a distance that—' He stops again. Puts his hands on the table. They are shaking. Lord Caeron's hands are shaking and the sight of it is more intimate than anything that has happened on this march.

'To hell with the command structure,' you say. 'Just for tonight.'

He looks at you. The mask falls. Underneath it is a man who is lonely and frightened and who has been carrying forty-seven lives and a war and the legacy of his family name and the knowledge that he is probably sending you all to die. Underneath it he is human. Underneath it he wants to be touched.

> **A) Reach across the table. Take his shaking hands. Hold them still.** He stares at your hands on his. Then he stands. Comes around the table. Stands in front of you and he is taller than you remembered and his eyes are the colour of whatever is underneath authority when authority admits it is not enough. He touches your face. His fingers are tentative. He has not touched another person without purpose in years. 'Tell me this is allowed,' he whispers. 'I need to hear it.' (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN, ROMANCE FLAME Caeron) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Stand. Close the distance. 'You are enough. The number does not matter. You matter.' Kiss him before he can construct a counter-argument.** He freezes. Then his hands — the shaking hands, the commander's hands — are on your back and he is pulling you in and the kiss is desperate in a way that Caeron is never desperate and the sound he makes against your mouth is the sound of a man who has been holding his breath for years and is finally, finally exhaling. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Caeron) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Sit with him. Talk about nothing — home, food, the bad poetry Aldric thinks no one knows about. Make him laugh. He resists. Then he does not resist. Then he is laughing and the dispatch is still face-down and the candle burns low and at some point his hand is resting on yours on the table and neither of you moves it.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_TARIEL — THE OBSERVER OBSERVED

*Forest Road — Camp Edge, Night*

Her notebook is closed. You have never seen Tariel's notebook closed when she is awake. She is sitting at the edge of the firelight with her knees drawn up and the closed notebook in her lap and she is looking at the fire with the expression of someone who has run out of observations. Not because there is nothing to observe — because she has observed too much and the weight of it has exceeded the notebook's capacity to contain it.

She hears you coming. She hears everything. But she does not open the notebook.

'I have been trying to write about you,' she says. No preamble. Tariel does not do preamble. 'For seven weeks I have been trying to write about you and I cannot find the right framework. You are not the Order. You are not the system. You defy categorisation and I find it—' She pauses. Chooses the next word with the care of someone who knows words are the most dangerous things she carries. '—distracting.'

You sit beside her. The fire crackles. She watches you sit down with the attentiveness she usually reserves for institutions, the dark eyes cataloguing the angle of your shoulders, the distance you chose, the way you breathe.

'I came here to study the knighthood,' she says. 'To understand why people choose this. The Oath, the structure, the willingness to die for a system. I have catalogued every mechanism of indoctrination. I have identified every leverage point.' She turns to you. The firelight catches the silver at her temples — she is not old, but she has earned those strands. 'And then you happened. And you are the one thing I cannot explain with leverage points.'

'Maybe it is not about leverage.'

'That is what I am afraid of.' Her voice drops. The professional distance — the journalist's distance, the observer's distance — is still there, but thin now, translucent, and you can see through it to the woman underneath who has spent her career at arm's length from everything and has discovered, at the worst possible time, that arm's length is too far.

She puts the notebook on the ground. The gesture is deliberate. She does not put the notebook down. The notebook is her armour. Without it she is just a woman at a fire, looking at you, and the vulnerability of it is breathtaking.

'I am going to say something that I cannot take back,' she says. 'And I need you to understand that I have never said it to anyone and I am not certain I know how.'

'Say it.'

'I am not studying you anymore. I stopped studying you weeks ago. What I have been doing is—' She looks at the fire. Back at you. 'What I have been doing is looking at you and feeling something that I do not have a framework for and I am terrified. Not of the war. Of this. Of you. Of what it means that I would rather be here — without the notebook, without the distance, without any of the things that keep me safe — than anywhere else in Krynn.'

> **A) 'Then be here.' Take the notebook. Set it further away. Move closer. 'No framework. No distance. Just here.'** She is trembling. Not from cold. You brush the hair from her face and she closes her eyes and when you kiss her it is the quietest, most careful kiss — not because you are uncertain, but because this woman has never let anyone this close and the gentleness is a form of respect. She kisses back. Slowly. Then not slowly. Then the notebook is forgotten and the fire is forgotten and she is holding onto you like the last true thing in a world full of analysis. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Tariel) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) 'Write about this. Right now. Not the analysis. The feeling. What it actually feels like.'** She stares at you. Opens the notebook. Writes. Her hand is shaking. When she finishes, she reads it aloud — halting, raw, nothing like her dispatches, everything like the truth. When she looks up there are tears on her face and she is smiling and the smile is the most unguarded thing you have ever seen from Tariel Duskmantle. (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN, ROMANCE FLAME Tariel) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) Say nothing. Take her hand. Sit with her in the quiet space where observation ends and presence begins.** She laces her fingers through yours. Holds on. The fire burns down and the stars come out and she leans against you and for the first time since you have known her, Tariel Duskmantle is not watching. She is just here. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
