## SCENE DATE_LYSANDER — THE SWORD AND THE SCAR

*Forest Road — Treeline, Night*

He is at the treeline because Lysander is always at the treeline — the edge of things, the boundary between the group and the dark, the place where a man who no longer belongs to anything can stand and watch the fire without being warmed by it.

You find him leaning against an oak with his sword unsheathed and laid across his knees. Not cleaning it. Not sharpening it. Just holding it, the way you hold a thing that has been your companion longer than any person. The blade reflects the distant firelight.

'Do not,' he says, before you speak. 'Do not ask if I am alright. I am a forty-year-old man sitting in the dark with a sword. The answer is obvious.'

'I was not going to ask that.'

He looks at you. Lysander's look is the heaviest thing in the world — decades of war and disillusion and the specific gravity of a man who did everything right and watched it mean nothing. But tonight there is something else in it. Something lighter. Not hope — Lysander is past hope — but the memory of what hope used to feel like.

'Then what?'

'I came because I wanted to.'

He is quiet for a long time. The sword stays on his knees. Then he sheathes it — slowly, deliberately, the gesture of a man putting down something he has been carrying for too long.

'You know I left the Order,' he says. 'You know why. What you do not know—' He rolls up his left sleeve. A scar runs from wrist to elbow, old and silver and thick. Not a sword wound. Too deliberate. Too straight. 'Two years after I left. I was in Palanthas. I was drinking. I had stopped being a knight and I had not yet figured out what to be instead. A woman found me in a tavern and stitched it and told me I was a waste and I have been angry about the fact that she was right ever since.'

He rolls the sleeve down. Looks at you. 'I am telling you this because you deserve to know the thing I carry. Before you decide — about me, about whatever this is. You deserve the full report.'

'The full report does not change anything.'

'It should.'

'It does not.'

He stands. He is taller when he is uncertain — as though the vulnerability adds an inch, the way a man straightens when he is bracing for impact. He is looking at you with the expression of someone who has forgotten what it means to be chosen and is trying to remember the protocol.

'I am too old for this,' he says.

'You are not.'

'I am difficult. I am angry. I have not been kind to another person in—' He stops counting. The number is too large. 'I do not know how to do this gently.'

> **A) 'Then do not do it gently.' Step into him. He is stiff — a soldier's posture, every muscle armoured — and then your hand is on his chest and you can feel his heart hammering beneath the leather and the scars and the years.** 'I am not asking for gentle,' you say. 'I am asking for honest.' He makes a sound. Not words. Something older than words. His hand covers yours on his chest and then his mouth is on yours and the kiss is not gentle — it is raw and desperate and years of loneliness converting into a single point of contact and he is shaking and you are holding him upright and the treeline could be burning and neither of you would notice. (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD, ROMANCE FLAME Lysander) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Take his hand. The scarred one. Turn it over. Press your lips to the scar on his wrist — gently, deliberately, with the specific tenderness of someone who is saying: this is not a waste. You are not a waste. This is worth something.** He is absolutely still. You can feel his pulse under your lips, fast and uneven. When you look up, his face has come apart — the cynicism, the anger, the armour, all of it gone, and underneath is a man who is fifty per cent grief and fifty per cent the sudden, devastating realisation that someone has just touched the worst thing about him and not flinched. 'You—' His voice breaks. He pulls you in. Holds on. Does not let go for a very long time. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME Lysander) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) 'Sit down. Tell me about the woman in Palanthas. Tell me all of it. Every year since.' Sit beside him against the oak and listen as the fire burns down and the story comes out, not in order, not cleanly, but in the fragments a broken man offers when he has decided to let someone see the pieces.** It takes hours. He cries once — silently, briefly, furious about it. You do not comment. When he finishes, the sky is grey with predawn and he looks lighter. Not healed. But lighter. 'No one has ever listened to the whole thing,' he says. 'Thank you.' The word sounds unfamiliar in his mouth. He is learning it. (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_POLY — THE THREE OF YOU

*Camp — Evening*

It takes time to learn the geometry of three. Not the logistics — those are simpler than expected — but the emotional architecture: who needs attention when, whose silence means contentment and whose means distance, how to hold two people in your awareness at once without making either feel secondary.

Tonight the geometry works. They talked to each other first, before either of them talked to you. That matters. This is not two separate relationships with you at the centre. It is a triangle, and tonight all three sides are holding.

One of them is leaning against you. The other is leaning against them. The chain of contact runs through all three of you like a current. Someone's hand is in your hair. Someone else's ankle is hooked around yours. You have stopped tracking whose body is where because the boundaries have become optional and the intimacy of that — the sheer trust of three people who have decided that the space between them is no longer necessary — is overwhelming in the quiet, powerful way that real things are overwhelming.

'I have a question,' one of them says. 'And it is not tactical.'

'Ask it.'

'Are you happy?'

The word is strange in a war camp. Happiness is not a military objective. But the answer is yes, and you say it, and the person who asked looks at the person you are all tangled up with and they both smile and the two smiles are different and both of them are for you.

> **A) 'Are *you* happy? Both of you. With each other. Not just with me.'** The question lands. They look at each other — really look, not through you, not about you — and the look that passes between them is its own answer. 'Yes,' one says. 'Surprisingly,' says the other. The laughter that follows is the laughter of three people who did not expect this and are grateful. (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE FLAME) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Pull them both closer. Words are inadequate. Show them instead.** The night is slow and warm and careful and generous. Three people learning the language of attention, of asking without words, of giving without keeping score. In the morning you will all be soldiers again. Tonight you are something older and more necessary than soldiers. (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN, ROMANCE FLAME) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **C) 'I never expected this. I do not have a framework for it.' Tariel laughs, or Thessaly smirks, or whoever it is looks at you with the expression of someone who finds your honesty devastating. 'Neither do we. We are building it as we go.'** The fire is low. The conversation continues until it becomes silence and the silence becomes sleep and you wake with two heartbeats you can feel through your chest and it is the most complete you have ever been. (+1 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE DATE_POLY_MORN — MORNING AFTER

*Camp — Dawn*

You wake to warmth. One of them is still asleep — curled against you with the specific weight of a person who has decided in their sleep that you are a safe place, their breathing slow and even and trusting in a way that waking consciousness would never allow. The other is awake, watching you with morning eyes, the softness of someone who has been conscious for a while and decided that the view was worth staying still for.

'Good morning,' they whisper. Careful not to wake the sleeping one.

The light is grey-pink. Birds. The distant sound of the camp waking up — Aldric's voice giving someone an order, the clink of a cook pot, the ordinary machinery of a march preparing to resume. But here, in this small space between three people, the war has not started yet.

The sleeping one stirs. Tightens their arm around you. Mumbles something that might be your name and might be nonsense and is, either way, the most tender sound you have heard on this entire march.

'We should get up,' says the waking one.

No one gets up.

> **A) 'Five more minutes.' The waking one laughs — quietly, for the sleeping one — and settles back against you and the five minutes become ten, become twenty, become the length of time it takes for the camp noise to reach the volume that means Caeron is about to send someone looking.** You get up. Together. The sleeping one blinks awake and looks at both of you and smiles. The smile says: this was real. The morning confirms it. (+2 ROSE) --> Scene BOND_RETURN
>
> **B) Kiss the waking one. Gently. They taste like morning and woodsmoke and the particular warmth of a person who chose to stay. Then the sleeping one wakes, sees this, and says — with absolute sleepy indignation — 'I was about to be kissed and you started without me.'** The laughter wakes half the camp. Caeron gives you a look at breakfast that says he knows exactly what happened and has decided not to have an opinion. (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene BOND_RETURN

## SCENE REST_ROMANCE — A QUIET MOMENT

*Camp — Evening*

The fire is low. Tomorrow the road continues. Tonight, for a few hours, the war is somewhere else and you are here with the people who matter to you.

> **REST SCENE — RELATIONSHIP CHECK**
> This scene occurs at the end of each act. If you are pursuing more than one romance, the situation may need to be addressed.

*If you are pursuing one romance, continue the story. If you are pursuing two or more, proceed to the appropriate scene below.*

> **A) (Single romance active) Continue. The night is yours.** *Return to the scene that sent you here.*
>
> **B) (Two romances, companions are compatible) Something unexpected happens.** --> Scene REST_COMPATIBLE
>
> **C) (Two romances, companions are not compatible) A conversation you cannot avoid.** --> Scene REST_CONFRONT
>
> **D) (Your feelings have changed) Something has shifted.** --> Scene REST_SWITCH

## SCENE REST_COMPATIBLE — AN UNEXPECTED UNDERSTANDING

*Camp — Late Evening*

You expected awkwardness. What you got was something else entirely. They already knew — of course they did. They are both too perceptive to have missed it. What surprises you is that they are not angry. What surprises you more is the look they exchange — not jealousy, not competition, but a kind of mutual recognition.

'We have talked,' one of them says. 'About you. About this.' A pause. 'We are not in competition. We do not need to be.'

> **POLYAMORY PATH AVAILABLE**
> Both companions are willing to share this with you — and with each other. This requires honesty, attention, and the understanding that love is not a finite resource.

*The polyamory path is now open. DATE_POLY scenes become available at future rest points.*

> **A) Accept. 'I did not know this was possible.' It is.** (+2 ROSE) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*
>
> **B) 'I need time to think about this.' They nod. The offer stands.** (+1 ROSE) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*

## SCENE REST_CONFRONT — THE CONVERSATION YOU CANNOT AVOID

*Camp — Late Evening*

You knew this was coming. You hoped it would not. You were wrong.

They find you at the same time — or near enough. One arrives from the left, one from the right, and the geometry of it is almost funny except that no one is laughing. They have already talked to each other. You can see it in the way they stand — not as rivals, but as two people who have reached the same conclusion and are waiting for you to reach it too.

'We need to talk,' one of them says. 'About this. About you. About what you want.'

The other is quieter. They are watching you — not with anger, not with jealousy, but with the patient, devastating attention of a person who has already accepted the answer and is waiting for you to say it.

'I care about both of you,' you say, and they both flinch because they knew this and it does not help.

'That is not the question,' the quiet one says. 'The question is: when Vogler comes, and everything becomes real, and there is one person you reach for in the dark — who is it?'

The fire crackles. The silence stretches. You have never wanted to be somewhere else as much as you want to be somewhere else right now. But you are here. And they are waiting. And the answer — the real answer, the one you have known for longer than you are willing to admit — is forming in your chest like a physical thing.

> **You must choose.** Both companions will remain in your party regardless. The romance continues with only one. The other will carry this differently depending on how you handle it.

> **A) Turn to the first companion. Say their name. The second sees it in your face before the name is fully spoken — they were already leaving, already constructing the version of this that they can survive, and the nod they give you on the way out is the bravest thing you have seen on this march.** The first companion looks at you. 'Are you certain?' You are. The cost of certainty is the sound of the other's footsteps receding, and you will carry that sound for a long time. But you are certain. (-1 ROSE for the unchosen. +1 ROSE for the chosen.) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*
>
> **B) Turn to the second companion. The first knows before you speak — they have been watching you watch the second for weeks and the data was always there, they simply chose not to read it.** 'I understand,' the first says. Their voice is level. Their hands are not. They leave. In the morning they will be professional and kind and the kindness will be worse than anger. The second companion looks at you. 'I did not want it to happen like this.' Neither did you. But it happened. (-1 ROSE for the unchosen. +1 ROSE for the chosen.) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*
>
> **C) 'I cannot choose. Not tonight. Not like this.' Both of them look at you. One with understanding. One with something harder. 'That is a choice,' the harder one says. 'You just do not want to call it one.' They both leave. Separately.** The romance with both companions cools to SPARK. You may pursue one again at the next rest point — but the window is narrower now. (-1 ROSE from both.) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*

---


## SCENE REST_SWITCH — SOMETHING HAS CHANGED

*Camp — A Private Moment*

You have been carrying this for a while now — the slow shift in how you feel, the awareness that what you want has changed. It is not a betrayal. It is honesty, arriving late but arriving.

> **ROMANCE CHANGE**
> You may end a current romance and redirect your heart. The previous partner will transition to friendship or distance, depending on how you handle it.

*Choose how to address the change. Your current romance ends. A new romance may begin at the next opportunity.*

> **A) Tell them honestly. It costs something. It is the right thing.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*
>
> **B) Let it fade. Say less. They will understand eventually.** (+1 ROSE) *Return to the scene that sent you here.*

---


## SCENE 67 — ALDRIC AT THE RIVER

*Forest River Crossing — Dawn, Day 3*

> **RATIONS — MORNING MEAL (Day 3)**
> Cold breakfast before the column moves. **Consume 1 ration.** Mark it off your character sheet.
>
> **IF YOU HAVE NO RATIONS:**
>
> **IF VAEL IS IN YOUR PARTY (and has not already covered):** He appears beside you at the river with a handful of fish — three small ones, still flopping, speared with a sharpened stick. 'I was up before dawn. The river has trout.' He watches you eat with the quiet satisfaction of someone who solved a problem you did not ask him to solve. Then, less gently: 'Squire, I have watched you fight draconians and hold a breach and carry a child through the dark. You are telling me the thing that defeats you is *packing food*?' He shakes his head. 'I can do this once. I cannot fish for you and fight beside you. Sort it out.' **Vael covers your meal. No ration consumed. Vael cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF ALDRIC CAN STILL COVER (and no one above):** He does not say anything. He puts half his breakfast in front of you. He does say, eventually: 'You realise this is becoming a pattern. I am not a supply wagon. I am barely a functional human being before sunrise. The fact that I am sharing food with you at this hour should be interpreted as a profound personal sacrifice.' He is smiling, slightly, the way Aldric smiles when he is being serious about something he is pretending is not serious. **Aldric covers your meal. No ration consumed. Aldric cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF MIRA CAN STILL COVER (and no one above):** She hands you a bundle of herbs and dried fruit without comment. Then the comment: 'I packed these for medical emergencies. Hunger caused by poor planning is not a medical emergency. I am choosing to reclassify it because I like you. Do not make me regret the reclassification.' **Mira covers your meal. No ration consumed. Mira cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF NO COMPANION CAN COVER:** You march on an empty stomach. The column eats around you. The river water helps but it is not food. Apply hunger penalty (see Combat Reference).
>
> *Record your current ration count on your character sheet.*

He tells you about three months before you arrived: he disobeyed an order to turn away refugees at the western gate. He has been waiting to be punished. 'I need to know if you would have done the same.'

> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Persuasion (+0) | CHA | DC 13
>
> **SUCCESS (roll 13+):** +1 Aldric Oath track. ROMANCE OATH activates if Flame was present.
>
> **FAILURE (roll 1-12):** He nods anyway.

> **A) 'Yes. I would have done the same.'** (+3 ROSE, ROMANCE OATH Aldric) --> Scene 68D
>
> **B) 'I do not know for certain. But you made the right call.'** (+2 ROSE, +1 SWORD) --> Scene 68D

---


## SCENE 68D — THE STARS OVER THE ROAD

*Forest Road — Night, Day 3*

You cannot sleep. The river is behind you and the road ahead narrows through old-growth forest — the trees here are centuries old, their canopy so thick that the starlight comes through in points, like holes in a dark ceiling. You walk away from camp because the sounds of people trying to sleep have become worse than being alone.

The clearing is small — a break in the canopy where a tree fell years ago and the sky opened up. Both moons are visible: Solinari full and white, Lunitari a red sickle at its edge. The astronomical term is conjunction. The common term is omen, which is not the same thing but feels closer tonight.

You lie on the fallen trunk and look up. The constellations are the same ones you memorised at Brightholm in the chapel library — Paladine's constellation bright in the northern sky, the Queen's dark space where no stars burn. Aldous taught you the navigation ones. You remember the lesson better than you expected: 'Learn the sky,' he said. 'It is the one map no one can take from you.'

**IF MIRA IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She finds the clearing too. She does not speak. She lies on the grass beside the fallen trunk and looks up. After a while: 'My mother knew all the star names. The old ones, from before the Cataclysm. She said they were the same stars but the names had changed because the people naming them had.' A long pause. 'I think that is true of most things.'

**IF ALDRIC IS NEARBY:** He is at the edge of the clearing. He saw you leave camp and followed — not to talk, but to make sure you were not alone in the dark. He leans against a tree and watches the sky and says nothing, which is the best thing he could do.

> **A) Count the stars in Paladine's constellation. Seven. You have counted them before. The number has not changed. Something about that steadies you.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 68
>
> **B) Close your eyes. The sky will be there tomorrow. Sleep will not wait.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 68
>
> **C) Stay until Solinari sets. The dark after moonset is total. You walk back to camp by memory.** (+1 ROSE, +1 CROWN) --> Scene 68

---


## SCENE 68 — THE LAST CAMP

*Forest Road — Night, Day 3*

The last camp before Vogler. Someone has a flute somewhere down the line — playing every night for twenty years. The melody is old. Tomorrow, Vogler.

> **RATIONS — EVENING MEAL (Day 3)**
> **Consume 1 ration.** Mark it off your character sheet.
>
> **IF YOU HAVE NO RATIONS:**
>
> **IF SERATH IS IN YOUR PARTY (and has not already covered):** They appear beside you without sound, which is how Serath does everything. A small bundle — dried meat, a hard biscuit, something wrapped in a leaf that turns out to be surprisingly edible. 'Dragon Army field rations,' they say. 'Terrible. But they will keep you standing.' They watch you eat with the expression of someone who has eaten worse things in worse places. 'I will not do this again. Not because I do not want to — because I will not have any left. Plan ahead, Squire. The road does not forgive people who forget to eat.' **Serath covers your meal. No ration consumed. Serath cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF THESSALY IS IN YOUR PARTY (and no one above can cover):** She looks up from her notebook. She has been watching you not eat for several minutes with the journalistic precision of someone cataloguing details. Then she reaches into her satchel and produces a wrapped parcel — cheese, bread, dried apples. 'I packed for the contingency of companions who confuse bravery with meal planning,' she says. 'Eat. And if you tell anyone I shared my rations, I will write something deeply unflattering about you in the official record.' A beat. 'That was not a joke. I keep very thorough records.' **Thessaly covers your meal. No ration consumed. Thessaly cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF LYSANDER IS IN YOUR PARTY (and no one above can cover):** He materializes from the treeline — he always comes from the treeline — and drops a rabbit and a handful of wild roots beside your fire. 'Cook that.' He is already leaving. Then he stops. 'Squire. A soldier who does not feed themselves is a soldier who becomes a liability. I am telling you this once. There will not be a second lecture or a second rabbit.' **Lysander covers your meal. No ration consumed. Lysander cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF CAERON IS NEARBY (and no one above can cover):** Caeron does not give you food. He gives you something worse: a look. The look of a commanding officer who has noticed a failure of basic field discipline and has decided to address it with silence rather than words, because the silence is worse. Then he produces a ration pack from the command supplies — the emergency reserve — and sets it in front of you. 'This is not generosity,' he says. 'This is an operational decision. A hungry squire is a dead squire and I have insufficient squires to lose one to poor logistics.' He walks away. You have never felt more fed and more ashamed simultaneously. **Caeron covers your meal. No ration consumed. Caeron cannot cover for you again.**
>
> **IF NO COMPANION CAN COVER:** You go hungry. The fire smells like other people's food and the flute sounds like a song about someone who remembered to bring rations. Apply hunger penalty (see Combat Reference).
>
> *Record your current ration count on your character sheet.*

> **PALADIN — THE CHOOSING**
> All Paladins: after your choice below, turn to Scene P4 now.

> **PALADIN — FALLEN TRACK**
> If FALLEN on DG track: turn to Scene DG4 now.

> **FIGHTER — MEASURE TRACK**
> If you have not yet completed M3 and M4: turn to Scene M3 now.

> **RELATIONSHIP CHECK — ACT 4**
> If you are pursuing **two or more romances**, turn to Scene REST_ROMANCE now before choosing below. Resolve that scene, then return here.

> **ROMANCE CONDITIONAL SCENES**
> If Sera at FLAME: turn to Scene 68B. If Vael at FLAME: turn to Scene 68C.

> **A) Tell her the true thing.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE OATH Thessaly if Flame active) --> Scene 69
>
> **B) 'Same thing as before. Not being enough.'** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 69
>
> **C) 'Right now? Nothing.'** (+2 SWORD) --> Scene 69

---


---


## SCENE 68B — THE LAST CAMP — SERA

*Forest Road — Night, Day 3 (if Sera Oath-track active)*

> **CONDITIONAL SCENE**
> This scene occurs if Sera is at Flame level or above.

The camp is quiet. The watch has changed. Sera is not on rotation tonight — she has not slept in forty hours and you told her you would take the first watch if she told you where she was going. She told you.

You find her at the far edge of the firelight where it thins into darkness, sitting with her back against a tree and her knife across her knees not because she thinks she needs it but because having it there is how she slows down. She looks up at you. The half-dark makes her face different — softer, less defended, the way people look when they think no one is watching.

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> She says: 'You came.' Like she did not expect it. Like she expected it. Like both are true. You sit down against the same tree and the distance between you is not much. She tilts her head and studies your face with the focused attention she normally gives to terrain. Then she says: 'I have been thinking about this since the south road.' She does not elaborate. She does not need to.

> **A) 'So have I.' Two words. She holds your gaze for a long moment. Then she puts the knife down and turns toward you and the rest of the watch is not spent watching.** (+ROMANCE OATH Sera, vivid fade to black) --> Scene 69
>
> **B) 'Tell me what you found in that village. The real version.' She tells you. It is terrible. You hold it together. Sometime before dawn the holding becomes something else.** (+ROMANCE OATH Sera, emotional and physical, fade to black) --> Scene 69
>
> **C) 'I did not want to get to Vogler without saying something.' She considers this. Then: 'What are you saying?' You tell her.** (+ROMANCE OATH Sera) --> Scene 69

---


## SCENE 68C — THE LAST CAMP — VAEL

*Forest Road — Night, Day 3 (if Vael Oath-track active)*

> **CONDITIONAL SCENE**
> This scene occurs if Vael is at Flame level or above.

She is cleaning her equipment for the third time, which is how you know she is not actually thinking about her equipment. She looks up when you approach with the expression of someone who has made a decision and is not sure they have the nerve to act on it.

She says: 'I want to say something before tomorrow and I need you to let me finish it because I am going to say it badly.' She looks at her sword. 'I have been here six months and the only person whose opinion of me I actually care about is yours. I did not plan for that. I do not know what to do with it. But we are one day from Vogler and I am not going to be someone who did not say it.'

> **ROMANCE MOMENT**
> She is looking at you now. The firelight is behind you and her expression is completely unguarded — all the competitive competence and dry deflection set aside, just: a person who told you a true thing and is waiting to see what you do with it. She is slightly breathless. She would hate knowing that you can see that.

> **A) 'I know. I have known for a while. I did not know what to do with it either.' She exhales. Somewhere in that exhale is a laugh. Then she closes the distance and so do you.** (+ROMANCE OATH Vael, passionate fade to black) --> Scene 69
>
> **B) 'You said it exactly right.' You mean this. She blinks. Then she sets down the sword and reaches for you.** (+ROMANCE OATH Vael, vivid tender fade to black) --> Scene 69
>
> **C) Say nothing. Close the distance instead. She makes a small surprised sound and then she is kissing you back like she has been waiting to for weeks, which she has.** (+ROMANCE OATH Vael) --> Scene 69

---


## PALADIN SCENE P4 — THE CHOOSING

*Forest Road — Dusk, Night Before Vogler*

> **PALADIN ONLY — THE MOST IMPORTANT SCENE**
> Count your God Sign tallies now. The god with the most tallies has been reaching for you throughout this journey. Fighters: skip ahead to Scene 70.

You are on watch. The camp is quiet behind you. The road south is dark. Tomorrow you reach Vogler. The presence is here tonight. Not behind you — not anywhere you can point at. It is simply present, the way a colour is present when you open your eyes. You have felt it before. It has been patient. It is still patient. But tonight you understand, in the way you understand things below language, that it has brought you this far and will not push you further. Whatever comes next is your decision.

> **DIVINE SIGN**
> The forest is still. The stars are out — Solinari rising, Lunitari somewhere behind the clouds, and in the space between them, if you look in the right way, a darkness that is not empty: Nuitari, the Black Moon. All three moons moving through their courses. And below them, somewhere very far down, the presence. Patient. Waiting. Still not asking.

Count your tallies:

| PALADINE | KIRI-JOLITH | MISHAKAL | HABBAKUK | BRANCHALA |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ | Signs: ___ |

Now choose:

> **A) Speak to Paladine. 'I am yours, if you will have me. I will guard what is good. I will not look away.'** --> Scene P4_Paladine
>
> **B) Speak to Kiri-Jolith. 'I will fight. I will not waste what you give me. The line will hold while I stand.'** --> Scene P4_KiriJolith
>
> **C) Speak to Mishakal. 'I will heal. I will not choose who deserves it. I will be where the hurt is.'** --> Scene P4_Mishakal
>
> **D) Speak to Habbakuk. 'I will protect what cannot protect itself. I will not ask permission first.'** --> Scene P4_Habbakuk
>
> **E) Speak to Branchala. 'I will hold onto the possibility of beauty in the middle of this. I will not let the war take everything.'** --> Scene P4_Branchala
>
> **F) Remain silent. 'I am not ready to name you. But I will not pretend you are not here either.'** --> Scene P4_Unnamed
>
> **G) The tallies do not match how you feel. Choose the god who calls to you most regardless of the count.** --> (Choose from A-F based on feeling)

---


## P4_Paladine — PALADINE RESPONDS

*Platinum Dragon, The Valiant Warrior, Father of Good*

Something vast and silver acknowledges you. Not with words — with the feeling of a great weight settling, not on you but around you, as if the space you occupy has been noted and found to matter. The silence after is profound.

> **DRAGONLANCE CAMEO — AN OLD MAN WITH A POINTY HAT**
> There is an old man sitting on a tree root nearby. He was not there before. He has a long beard, a battered pointy hat, and the general air of someone who wandered in by mistake and is enjoying the view. He looks at you with kind, gold-flecked eyes. 'Ah,' he says. 'Good. Very good.' He sounds pleased in the way someone sounds pleased when a thing they have been hoping for finally happens. When you look back he is gone. Fizban is, depending on who you ask, a befuddled old wizard, a Hero of the Lance, or Paladine himself walking the world in mortal guise. These three things are not mutually exclusive.

**Mechanics:** Devotion Oath (recommended). Sacred Weapon grants your longsword +CHA to attacks. Channel Divinity: Turn the Unholy. +1 ROSE. Advantage on CHA saves for the remainder of this adventure.

**In the Main Campaign:** Paladine was worshipped as the highest of the gods of good. His chosen were judges and guardians. His divine spark in you is a candle against a coming darkness — and candles matter.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## P4_KiriJolith — KIRI-JOLITH RESPONDS

*The Bison of Heaven, God of Just War*

Something strikes. That is the only word for it — not painful but percussive, like a hammer on an anvil very close to you. A sound and a sensation at once. Then silence. Then the smell of steel and something that might be blood but might be rain.

**Mechanics:** Vengeance Oath (recommended) or Devotion. Vow of Enmity: choose one enemy per fight to gain Advantage against for 1 minute. Abjure Enemy: one creature within 60 ft. must make WIS DC 13 save or be frightened and halved in speed for 1 minute. +2 SWORD.

**In the Main Campaign:** Kiri-Jolith has always chosen those who fight not for glory but for the person beside them. His paladins will find that fighting to give someone else a chance to live is its own kind of prayer.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## P4_Mishakal — MISHAKAL RESPONDS

*The Blue Lady, Goddess of Healing and Compassion*

Warmth. Simple and enormous. Your hands feel it first — both palms, spreading up your arms and settling in your chest. It is the warmth of something that is pleased with you. Not proud. Pleased. Like coming home.

**Mechanics:** Devotion Oath. Sacred Weapon. Channel Divinity: Turn the Unholy. Bonus: Lay on Hands pool increases to 15 HP per long rest. Cure Wounds spell added to your spells known (no slot required, 1/day). +2 ROSE.

**In the Main Campaign:** Mishakal's return is the most significant spiritual event in Krynn's history since the Cataclysm. Her chosen carry actual divine healing in a world that has forgotten what that feels like. The healing you provide will be understood by NPCs as a miracle. Because it is.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## P4_Habbakuk — HABBAKUK RESPONDS

*The Fisher King, God of Nature, Sea, and Animal Life*

The forest moves. Not like wind — like attention. The trees around you shift their weight fractionally. Somewhere close, an owl lands and watches you with complete stillness. A fox crosses the road twenty feet ahead and sits down and looks at you and then moves on.

**Mechanics:** Ancients Oath (recommended). Nature's Wrath: restrain one creature with spectral vines (STR/DEX DC 13, concentration 1 min). Turn the Faithless: fey and fiends within 30 ft. must make WIS DC 13 save or be turned for 1 min. +1 ROSE, +1 SWORD. Animals in the main campaign will not flee from you.

**In the Main Campaign:** Habbakuk is the god of living things that do not have a vote in what happens to their world. His paladins will find that Krynn's natural world responds to them — animals bring warnings, weather shifts, and occasionally something very old in a forest recognises you.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## P4_Branchala — BRANCHALA RESPONDS

*The Song of Life, God of Beauty, Art, and Inspiration*

You hear music. Not in your ears — in the space behind your eyes. Something that is not quite a song and not quite a feeling and is exactly what you would call the reason not to give up. It lasts three seconds. It is enough.

**Mechanics:** Devotion or Ancients Oath. Channel Divinity: Sacred Weapon. Bonus: once per long rest, you may use your Channel Divinity to grant an ally advantage on their next ability check or attack roll. +2 ROSE.

**In the Main Campaign:** Branchala is the god of the unreasonable belief that beauty and hope survive. His paladins carry something the Dragon Army cannot easily destroy: the ability to make people feel, briefly, that it will be all right. This turns out to matter enormously.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## P4_Unnamed — THE UNNAMED PRESENCE

*The God Who Did Not Name Themselves*

The presence acknowledges your silence the way a patient teacher acknowledges a student who says: I do not understand yet. Not disappointment. Something that is almost approval. The between-spaces are where most thinking actually happens.

**Mechanics:** Choose any Sacred Oath at Level 3. Bonus: once per long rest, you may roll twice on any Religion or History check and take the better result. +1 ROSE, +1 CROWN.

**In the Main Campaign:** The unnamed presence has been patient for three hundred years. Your god's identity will become clearer through your actions rather than through declaration. What you do in Vogler will matter more than what you said tonight.

Proceed to Scene 70.

---


## SCENE DG4 — THE RECKONING

*Vogler Road — The Day Before Vogler (Paladin Who Has Fallen)*

> **FALLEN PALADINS ONLY**
> If you are HELD, HELD FIRM, PURIFIED, or PULLED BACK: skip to Scene 70.

You are on the last road before Vogler. The column has stopped for water. You are sitting on a stone wall looking at the lake in the distance when you hear footsteps approaching — not Aldric's, not Mira's. The figure is old. Very old. Robes that are neither white nor grey but the specific colour of very old wood. A face like a map of decisions made and paid for. He sits down without being invited and looks at the lake with you for a while.

> **DRAGONLANCE: ELISTAN OF PALANTHAS (or a messenger in his name)**
> Elistan was the first Chosen of Paladine after the Cataclysm — the first person in three hundred years to carry true divine power. He did not come to judge you. He came because someone asked him to find you.

'You've been carrying something that isn't yours,' he says. Not unkindly. Factually. 'It is not permanent. But it does not come off easily. The question is whether you want it off badly enough.' He looks at you. 'Not whether you are sorry. Whether you want to be different.' He waits.

This is the hardest question the prelude asks. Not 'did you fall' — you know the answer to that. But whether the falling was truly the end of something or whether it was a lesson you are willing to carry forward. The answer has to be real. He will know if it isn't.

> **A) Yes. I want to be different. I want to understand what I chose and unmake it.** (Full recovery) --> Scene DG4_recover
>
> **B) I want to be different but I don't know if I can. That's the honest answer.** (Partial recovery) --> Scene DG4_partial
>
> **C) I want redemption more than anything. But I don't have the path.** (Ember path) --> Scene DG4_ember
>
> **D) I made a rational choice. I stand by it.** (No recovery — remain fallen) --> Scene DG4_fallen

---


## SCENE DG4_recover — THE RETURN

*Vogler Road — Recovery*

He nods once. He puts his hand on your head for a moment — briefly, the way a blessing works when it is genuinely meant — and then he stands and walks away. The road is the same road. The lake is the same lake. Your hands feel clean. Not new-clean. Clean the way things are clean when they have been used and washed and used again. Your god's warmth is back in full, unfiltered, entirely present.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE VOW RESTORED**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement by a Paladin), Uncommon*
> A small medallion of white-silver, shaped like a closed fist holding a flame.
> **Mechanics:** Once per long rest: when you use Lay on Hands, you may also remove one condition: frightened, charmed, or poisoned. Advantage on saving throws against being charmed or possessed by fiends or undead.
> **Lore:** Carried by one who fell and chose to return.

> **A) Proceed to Scene 70.** --> Scene 70

---


## SCENE DG4_partial — THE SCAR

*Vogler Road — Partial Recovery*

He does not argue with the honesty. 'That is a better answer than certainty,' he says. Your Lay on Hands is restored. The muffled quality in your prayers is mostly gone. But there is still a small thing — a faint violet note to the golden warmth.

> **MARK ON YOUR CHARACTER SHEET — FAULTY DIVINE POWERS**
> Lay on Hands: restored to full pool. Spell slots: each time you expend a spell slot, roll 1d6 first. On a 1 or 2, the slot is spent but the spell fails. This instability ends if you complete the Quest of the Returning Flame.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE SHARD OF RETURNING LIGHT**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement by a Paladin), Uncommon — GROWING*
> A sliver of white crystal that throws no reflection and casts no shadow. It is slightly warm.
> **Mechanics:** Advantage on saves against being frightened. Once per long rest, as a bonus action: creatures of your choice within 10 ft. that are frightened or charmed may reroll their saving throw with advantage. QUEST STATE: grows stronger when quest is completed.
> **Lore:** Given to a paladin whose faith is cracked but not broken. The crystal holds light it hasn't earned yet, on credit.

> **QUEST: THE RETURNING FLAME**
> Complete in Shadow of the Dragon Queen: Find the Shrine of Mishakal (or any good-aligned god shrine). Spend a full night in honest prayer. In the same session, perform one act of genuine self-sacrifice for a stranger. When both conditions are met: faulty spell mechanic ends permanently. The Shard upgrades: bonus action also grants 2d6 temp HP. Once per long rest: cast Protection from Evil and Good without a slot.

> **A) Proceed to Scene 70.** --> Scene 70

---


## SCENE DG4_ember — THE EMBER

*Vogler Road — The Wanting Without the Way*

Elistan is quiet for a long time. 'That is the hardest state,' he says at last. 'Wanting and not having the path. It is not failure. It is the condition that precedes everything real.' He gives you something small and closes your fingers around it.

Your Lay on Hands pool is restored to half normal (rounded up). Your divine abilities still function — unevenly, with effort. But the wanting is a kind of fire, and fire is not nothing.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE EMBER THAT REMAINED**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement by a Paladin), Uncommon — SEEKING*
> A small piece of charcoal that is faintly warm at the centre when you hold it in a closed fist.
> **Mechanics:** Lay on Hands pool is half normal maximum (rounded up). Once per long rest: spend 10 minutes in honest prayer to cast Guidance on yourself without a slot. Each time you act in direct service of an innocent without personal benefit, mark one tally. At 5 tallies, the ember becomes The Vow Restored. Tallies reset if you knowingly act against innocents.
> **Lore:** Given to a paladin who wanted the way back and didn't have it yet. The gods of good do not require certainty — they require the wanting.

> **A) Proceed to Scene 70.** --> Scene 70

---


## SCENE DG4_fallen — THE GIFT OF THE DARK QUEEN

*Vogler Road — No Recovery*

He looks at you for a long moment. 'You believe it,' he says. 'That is real.' He stands. He does not touch you. 'When you understand what you chose,' he says, 'the door is still open. It is always open. The gods of good do not lock doors.' He walks away. That night, something else leaves gifts at the edge of your bedroll. They are beautiful. They are cold.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE QUEEN'S BRAND**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement), Uncommon — TAINTED*
> A black iron ring inlaid with five colours of enamel — red, blue, black, green, white — in the pattern of five dragon heads.
> **Mechanics:** Lay on Hands heals normally. Once per long rest: add 1d6 necrotic damage to a melee attack. However: at dawn each day, DC 12 WIS save or take 1 point of Exhaustion. Removing the ring requires Remove Curse or Greater Restoration.
> **Lore:** A gift from Takhisis to a paladin she considers an investment. The Queen of Darkness plays a long game.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE UNASKED QUESTION**
> *Weapon (Longsword), Requires Attunement, Rare — TAINTED*
> A longsword with a blade of black steel that reflects nothing. The crossguard is five interlocking crescents.
> **Mechanics:** +1 to attack and damage rolls. Once per long rest: on a hit, target makes DC 13 WIS save or is frightened until end of their next turn. Whenever you use this ability, make a DC 12 WIS save yourself or take 1 Exhaustion. The sword cannot be lost — if separated, it reappears in your pack within 24 hours.
> **Lore:** A gift from Takhisis to a paladin she considers a long-term investment. It can be unmade only at the Shrine of Paladine by someone who genuinely no longer wants what it offers.

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE SHADOW MANTLE**
> *Wondrous Item (Cloak), Requires Attunement, Rare — TAINTED*
> A cloak of deep violet-black that absorbs the light around you slightly.
> **Mechanics:** +1 to AC. Advantage on Stealth checks in dim light or darkness. Once per long rest: become heavily obscured to creatures more than 5 ft. away until start of your next turn. Disadvantage on Persuasion checks with clerics and paladins of good-aligned gods. Removing the cloak requires a DC 14 WIS save at dawn. On failure, you feel no desire to remove it.
> **Lore:** Takhisis gives good gifts. That is the point.

> **YOUR PALADIN ABILITIES — THE SECRET PATRON**
> Until you formally pledge to Takhisis in Shadow of the Dragon Queen, your paladin abilities continue to function — but their source has changed. Lay on Hands heals normally. Divine Smite is very slightly violet. Spell slots function. You are, right now, a paladin of Takhisis who does not know it yet.

> **QUEST: THE PLEDGE OF THE FIVE HEADS**
> In Shadow of the Dragon Queen: Takhisis will reach for you at moments of violence, desperation, or victory. When ready, seek a Dragon Army officer of Black Wing Command who carries her symbol. The pledge is private, brief, and irreversible. Upon pledging: Oathbreaker subclass. Channel Divinity becomes Animate Dead and Aura of Hate. Lay on Hands can harm enemies. The redemption arc remains available. Elistan said the door is always open.

> **A) Proceed to Scene 70.** --> Scene 70

## SCENE M4 — THE VOGLER QUESTION

*Vogler Road — Day Before the City (Fighter Only)*

> **FIGHTER ONLY — MEASURE SUBPLOT CONCLUSION**
> Count your Measure Track score: 3-4 = Scholar, 5-7 = Practitioner, 8+ = Keeper. This determines your gift.

Ser Aldous finds you at the edge of the last camp. He has the old book again — the cracked binding one, not the official Measure. He sets it down beside you. 'One more question,' he says. 'Tomorrow you ride into Vogler. You will be a newly-oathed squire of the Knights of Solamnia carrying the Measure you have been learning for three weeks. Someone in that village will need you to know what it means. What do you know?'

> **A) 'I know the Measure is a tool for protecting people. Not a shield for the person holding it. If I have to choose between the law and the person, the law is there to serve the person.'** (The Keeper's answer — highest track) --> Scene M4_keeper
>
> **B) 'I know the Measure requires me to make judgment calls I cannot undo. And that the right call is not always the comfortable one.'** (The Practitioner's answer — middle track) --> Scene M4_practitioner
>
> **C) 'I know I do not know everything yet. But I know enough to hold the line until I do.'** (The Scholar's answer — early track, honest) --> Scene M4_scholar

---


## SCENE M4_keeper — THE KEEPER'S GIFT

*The Last Camp*

He nods slowly. Not just at the answer — at the person saying it. 'That is what the Measure says,' he tells you. 'Not in those words. But that is what it says.' He hands you the old book. 'Not a copy. The original. My copy, the one I have carried for forty years. I do not need it anymore. I have it memorised.' He looks at you. 'You have what matters. Go use it.'

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: ALDOUS'S MEASURE**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement by a Solamnic Knight), Uncommon*
> A small, ancient book with a cracked leather binding and forty years of margin notes in Ser Aldous's precise hand. The pages are worn thin where he returned to them most. It smells of tallow and old stone — the chapel library at Brightholm.
> **Mechanics:** While attuned: advantage on History checks related to law, justice, or the Knights of Solamnia. Once per long rest: you may consult the book to automatically know the Measure's position on any legal or ethical question (the DM will provide the answer). Additionally, Insight checks against NPCs who are acting under false pretence of law are made with advantage.
> **Lore:** Ser Aldous of Brightholm carried this book through forty years of knighthood and gave it to the squire who understood it fastest. In the main campaign, senior Solamnic Knights will recognise it and understand what it means that you are carrying it.

> **A) Return to Scene 69.** --> Scene 69

---


## SCENE M4_practitioner — THE PRACTITIONER'S GIFT

*The Last Camp*

He is quiet for a moment. Then: 'That is honest. That is the honest answer and it is the right answer.' He reaches into his robe and takes out something he has been carrying. 'I was not sure I would give you this,' he says. 'But you have earned it. Not because you were perfect. Because you understood what you were not perfect at and kept going anyway.'

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE CHAPLAIN'S SEAL**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement), Uncommon*
> A brass stamp in the shape of the Solamnic sun, worn smooth with use. Aldous has used it to seal documents for thirty years. When you press it to paper, the impression is clean and permanent.
> **Mechanics:** While attuned: once per long rest you may invoke the Measure's authority — any Intimidation or Persuasion check made to enforce law or protect innocents is made with advantage. Additionally, documents bearing this seal are treated as legally binding by any Solamnic NPC of Knight rank or below.
> **Lore:** A working seal, not ceremonial. Aldous of Brightholm's seal carries forty years of genuine decisions. In the main campaign, NPCs who recognise it will understand that its bearer earned it.

> **A) Return to Scene 69.** --> Scene 69

---


## SCENE M4_scholar — THE SCHOLAR'S GIFT

*The Last Camp*

'That,' says Aldous, 'is the truest thing a new squire can know.' He looks at you for a moment. 'You will make mistakes in Vogler. Every new knight does. What matters is that you have the foundation to understand them.' He sets the old cracked book down in front of you. 'Read the third chapter tonight. Then read it again after Vogler. See how different it looks.'

> **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: THE COMMENTARIES (INCOMPLETE)**
> *Wondrous Item (Requires Attunement), Common — Grows in Power*
> A copy of the secondary Measure commentaries, heavily annotated by Ser Aldous but with wide margins left blank. He intended you to fill them.
> **Mechanics:** While attuned: advantage on History checks about Solamnic law. After each completed adventure in which you faced a Measure dilemma, add a note to one blank page. When all blank pages are filled (DM discretion, usually 3-5 adventures), the book becomes Aldous's Measure (Uncommon, see Keeper's gift). The item grows with you.
> **Lore:** A book given to someone at the beginning of understanding, not the end. The best version of this gift is earned later. In the main campaign, any Solamnic Knight who examines it will read Aldous's marginal note on the front page: 'For the squire who had the sense to know what they did not know yet.'

> **A) Return to Scene 69.** --> Scene 69

## SCENE 69 — MIRA AT THE CROSSROADS

*Forest Road Junction — Afternoon, Day 3*

> **FIGHTER ON MEASURE TRACK:** Before continuing, turn to Scene M4 (The Vogler Question) now. Aldous finds you at the edge of the last camp. After M4, return here.

The road splits. North to safety. South toward Vogler. Mira stands at the junction. 'I told myself I was going to take the safe road. I am not going to do that.'

> **A) South. She falls in beside you.** (+2 ROSE, ROMANCE OATH Mira if Flame active) --> Scene 69_ROAD
>
> **B) 'North. Take the others to safety.'** (Romance pauses until main campaign.) --> Scene 69_ROAD

---


## SCENE 69_ROAD — THE LAST MILES

*South Road — Day 3, Late Afternoon*

The road narrows for the last time. The forest thins and through the gaps you can see the sky changing — the grey-blue of inland Solamnia giving way to the silver-white that means water. Lake Akh-Tiel. You have read about it. You have studied maps of it. You have heard Aldous describe the water in the specific nostalgic voice of someone who saw it once and never forgot. None of that prepared you for the scale.

The column has gone quiet in the way that columns go quiet when the destination is close enough to taste and the tasting changes everything. Hooves on packed earth. Leather creaking. The particular sound of people not speaking because the silence says it better.

Aldric pulls his horse alongside yours. He does not say anything. He looks ahead and so do you and for a moment the two of you are just people on a road looking at what they are riding toward, which is either the defence of a village or the definition of who they are or both, because those are the same thing when you are twenty years old and sworn to something larger than yourself.

**IF THESSALY IS IN YOUR PARTY:** She is writing. Not in her notebook — on a loose leaf tucked into her coat. A letter. To whom, she does not say.

**IF CAERON IS WITH THE COLUMN:** He rides at the front. His posture has not changed since Brightholm — the same compressed focus, the same economy. But his hand rests on his sword hilt now, and it did not before.

> **RANDOM ENCOUNTER CHECK**
> Roll 1d10. On a **10**: A rider appears on the road ahead, alone, armoured, mounted on a warhorse that has seen better decades. Turn to **Scene 69_KNIGHT** before continuing. On 1-9: nothing. The road is empty. Continue below.

> **A) Ride in silence. Let the road be the road.** (+1 SWORD) --> Scene 70A
>
> **B) Look at Aldric. Nod. He nods back.** (+1 ROSE) --> Scene 70A
>
> **C) Touch the tabard. The Solamnic sun is still on your chest.** (+1 CROWN) --> Scene 70A

---


## SCENE 69_KNIGHT — THE LAST KNIGHT OF THE WHITE SPAN

*South Road — Day 3, Afternoon*

The rider is old. That is the first thing — the particular old of a man who has been old for a long time and has been fighting against it and is now, finally, not fighting against it anymore. He sits his warhorse with the posture of a man whose body remembers perfection even though perfection left it a decade ago. The horse is old too — a grey destrier, scarred across the flanks, its mane cropped short in the Solamnic military style that nobody has used in twenty years.

His armour is Solamnic half-plate. Old. The rose insignia on the breastplate is worn to a ghost, the steel patched and repatched, the plates dented in places that speak of fights survived rather than fights won. And across his back: a greatsword in a harness that does not match the rest of his equipment. The harness is new. The sword is not — it is very, very old, and even from this distance you can feel something about it. A hum. A weight. The particular quality of a weapon that is more than steel.

He blocks the road. Not aggressively — he simply stops his horse and waits.

Caeron signals the column to halt. His hand goes to his hilt. The rider raises one gauntleted hand — not a threat. A greeting. The salute of the Order of the Rose, executed perfectly, from a man who learned it in an era when the salute still meant something universal.

'I am Ser Hadrian of the White Span,' he says. His voice is a ruin. A beautiful ruin — deep, resonant, cracked in places where time and weather have done their work. 'Knight of the Rose. Forty-three years of service. I was at Thelgaard when the garrison fell. I was at the Vingaard bridge when they tried to take the crossing. I have been riding south alone for six months because there was no one left to ride with.'

He looks at your column. He counts. His expression does not change.

'I have a request,' he says. 'Not for your commander. For the youngest among you.' His eyes find yours. 'For the squire.'

**IF CAERON IS WITH THE COLUMN:** Caeron's hand tightens on his hilt. He knows what this is. His expression says: *This is not your fight. You do not have to do this.* But he does not say it. Because Ser Hadrian has forty-three years of Rose authority and the request, by the Measure, is his to make.

Ser Hadrian dismounts. It costs him — you can see the pain in his knees, the careful way he transfers his weight, the veteran's trick of making the dismount look deliberate when it is actually the body's last negotiation with gravity. He draws the sword.

The hum intensifies. The blade catches the afternoon light and the light *bends* — not refraction, something else, something that lives in the steel and has been living there for longer than anyone in your column has been alive. The sword is ancient. The sword is beautiful. The sword is *awake*.

'*Dawnstrike*,' he says, holding it before him. 'Given to the first Knight of the White Span by a cleric of Paladine in the year 118 AC. It has been carried by my family for nine generations. It is the only thing I have left that matters.'

He plants the blade point-down in the road.

'I am sixty-seven years old,' he says. 'My hands shake in the morning. My left knee has not bent properly since Vingaard. I have ridden six months alone and I have watched everything I served fall to dust and I am tired in the way that no rest will fix. The Dragon Army took my garrison, my soldiers, my friends, and every institution I believed in. They did not take my sword and they did not take my honour and I would like to spend both before they take me.'

He meets your eyes.

'I am asking for a duel,' he says. 'Not to the death. To the yield. One knight against one squire, by the old forms. If you win—' he touches the sword, the armour — 'everything I carry is yours. If I win, I ride south, and I keep riding until I find the Dragon Army, and I make them earn what they have already taken.'

He pauses.

'You may refuse,' he says. 'There is no dishonour in it. But I would ask you not to. I have been riding alone for a very long time, and I would like my last fight to be against someone who wears the sun.'

> **A) Accept the duel. Draw your blade. 'Est Sularus oth Mithas, Ser Hadrian.'** --> Proceed to THE DUEL below.
>
> **B) Refuse. 'I will not fight you, ser. Ride with us instead. Vogler needs every sword.'** (+2 ROSE, +1 CROWN)
> Ser Hadrian is quiet for a long time. Then he sheathes Dawnstrike. 'You are kind,' he says. 'That is not what I asked for. But I recognise it.' He does not ride with you. He salutes — the Rose salute, perfect, the last time he will give it — and turns his horse south. You watch him ride toward the smoke. He does not look back.
> **IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Aldric watches him go. His jaw works. 'He wanted to choose how it ended,' he says quietly. 'You took that from him.' It is not a criticism. It is a fact. Facts, with Aldric, are the hardest things.
> --> Return to Scene 69_ROAD choices.

---

> **THE DUEL — SER HADRIAN OF THE WHITE SPAN**
>
> The column forms a circle. This is the old form — Solamnic tradition, older than the current Order, older than the Cataclysm. A ring of witnesses. Two swords. The sun overhead. Caeron dismounts and stands at the edge, arms folded, expression unreadable.
>
> Ser Hadrian takes Dawnstrike from the road. The sword hums in his hands and for a moment — just a moment — the old man is not old. The posture straightens. The eyes sharpen. The forty-three years of service flow into his grip and his stance and the particular way he holds the blade, and you understand: he was magnificent once. He intends to be magnificent one more time.
>
> **Your companions step back. This is a duel. They do not intervene. They watch.**
>
> **COMBAT — DUEL (3 rounds, no companion actions)**
>
> **YOUR STATS:** Per character sheet. Your weapon. Your armour.
>
> **SER HADRIAN:**
> HP 20 (old, fragile — the body has nothing left to give)
> AC 15 (Solamnic half-plate)
> *Dawnstrike* +7, 2d6+5 slashing + 1d6 radiant (Hadrian burns both Radiant Strikes in this duel — the sword's magic compensates for his failing strength)
> **Veteran's Instinct:** Once per duel, Hadrian can force you to reroll a successful attack. 'Not yet. Again.'
> **Failing Body:** Each round after Round 1, Hadrian makes a CON save (DC 12, then 14, then 16). On failure, his AC drops by 1 as his stance weakens. His attacks do not weaken — the sword carries what the body cannot.
> **Yield:** Hadrian yields at 0 HP. He does not die. This is a duel to the yield, not to the death.

> **ROUND 1 — THE OLD FORM**
>
> *He comes at you with the first combination of the old Solamnic forms — the ones from the textbooks, the ones that haven't been taught in two decades because the masters who taught them are dead. The blade leads with a diagonal cut that turns into a thrust that turns into a bind that you have never seen executed at speed before. Dawnstrike leaves a trail of pale gold light in the air.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (per sheet) | DC 15 (Hadrian's AC)
>
> **HIT:** Your blade finds the gap between plates. Hadrian grunts — pain, real pain, and something else. Satisfaction. 'Good steel,' he says. 'Good arm.' Deal weapon damage.
>
> **MISS:** He turns your blade with a parry that looks effortless. It is not. You can see the strain in his wrist. But the parry is perfect.
>
> **HADRIAN'S STRIKE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 17 (Dawnstrike +7)
>
> **SUCCESS:** You catch Dawnstrike on your blade. The impact travels through your arms and into your shoulders and you understand what a magical weapon feels like when it is trying to get through your guard: it feels like being hit by something that wants to hit you.
>
> **FAILURE:** Dawnstrike connects. Take 2d6+5 slashing + 1d6 radiant damage. The radiant burns cold — not fire, light, the pure white light of a Paladine-blessed blade that does not distinguish between evil and merely in-the-way.
>
> **HADRIAN'S CON SAVE:** DC 12. (DM rolls or player rolls for Hadrian.)
> **FAILURE:** His stance wavers. AC drops to 14. He grits his teeth. He does not comment.
> **SUCCESS:** He holds. The old body has one more round of perfection.

> **ROUND 2 — THE KNIGHT HE WAS**
>
> *He is faster than he should be. The sword is carrying him — you can see it, the way Dawnstrike pulls his arm into positions his muscles can no longer hold on their own. The blade is fighting through him and he is letting it. Forty-three years of service distilled into a weapon that remembers every one of them.*
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (per sheet) | DC 15 (or lower if AC has dropped)
>
> **HIT:** Deal weapon damage. Hadrian staggers. His knee — the left one, the one that does not bend — buckles. He catches himself. He raises the blade. He is not done.
>
> **IF HADRIAN USES VETERAN'S INSTINCT (once per duel):**
> 'Not yet,' he says. 'Again.' You must reroll a successful attack. Take the new result. The old knight is not ready to fall.
>
> **MISS:** His guard holds.
>
> **HADRIAN'S STRIKE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 17
>
> **HIT:** Take 2d6+5 + 1d6 radiant. The radiant light flares. Your companions flinch.
>
> **MISS:** His swing goes wide. His arm shakes. The sword tries to correct. The body cannot.
>
> **HADRIAN'S CON SAVE:** DC 14.
> **FAILURE:** AC drops by 1 again. His breathing is audible now. Ragged. The kind of breathing that says the body is writing checks the lungs cannot cash.
> **SUCCESS:** He holds. It costs him everything to hold.

> **ROUND 3 — THE END**
>
> *He is failing. You can see it — the left leg dragging, the breath coming in gasps, the arm that held Dawnstrike for forty-three years beginning to tremble. But the eyes are clear. The eyes are younger than the rest of him. The eyes say: finish this. Please.*
>
> **CHECK HP TOTALS.**
>
> **IF YOU ARE WINNING (Hadrian at lower HP):**
>
> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll (per sheet) | DC per Hadrian's current AC
>
> **HIT:** Your blade stops at his throat. Or his chest. Or the gap in his shoulder plate. Wherever it stops, it stops, and Ser Hadrian of the White Span looks at the blade and at you and his face does something it has not done in six months of riding alone: it relaxes.
>
> 'Yield,' he says. And means it. And is grateful.
>
> **MISS:** The round ends. Go to TIE.
>
> **IF HADRIAN IS WINNING (you at lower HP):**
>
> **HADRIAN'S STRIKE:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Defense roll | DC 17
>
> **FAILURE:** Dawnstrike connects. The impact is final — not lethal, not cruel, but absolute. You go down. The packed earth hits your back. The sky is very blue above you. Ser Hadrian stands over you, Dawnstrike's point at your chest, and the sword's pale light illuminates his face. He is weeping. Not with sadness. With relief.
>
> 'You fought well,' he says. 'Better than well. You fought like a knight.' He sheathes Dawnstrike. He does not offer his hand — instead, he salutes. The Rose salute. Full, perfect, given to a squire lying in the dirt, which means he does not see a squire lying in the dirt. He sees a knight.
>
> Then he mounts. The old destrier turns south. Ser Hadrian of the White Span rides toward the smoke without looking back, and the last thing you see before your companions reach you is the Solamnic sun on his battered breastplate, catching the light.
>
> **YOU LOSE:**
> Your weapon is **BROKEN** — the impact of Dawnstrike against your blade has shattered it. Your weapon now counts as an **improvised weapon** (1d4, no proficiency bonus) until replaced. Mark this on your character sheet.
> Your armour is **SHATTERED** — Dawnstrike's radiant edge has cracked the plates beyond repair. Your AC is reduced to 10 + DEX modifier (unarmoured) until you acquire new armour. Mark this on your character sheet.
> Your companions drag you back to the column. You are **unconscious** and wake at **1 HP**. If Mira is present, she is already working on you when you open your eyes. If Aldric is present, his face is the first thing you see, and his expression is the expression of a man who just watched someone he cares about fight a legend and lose, and the losing is not what bothers him — the getting-back-up is what he is waiting for.
> **+1 SWORD, +1 ROSE** (the honour of the attempt). Ser Hadrian's respect was genuine.
>
> **SUCCESS (you defend):** The round ends. Go to TIE.
>
> **IF HP IS TIED — THE DRAW:**
> You are both still standing. Barely. Hadrian's sword arm is trembling. Your arms burn. Neither of you can find the finishing blow and neither of you is willing to take a bad one.
> 'Draw,' you say.
> Hadrian looks at you for a long time. Then he laughs. A real laugh — broken, exhausted, alive. 'I have not drawn in thirty years. I forgot what it felt like.' He sheathes Dawnstrike. 'Keep your weapons, squire. You will need them. I will keep mine. I will need it where I am going.' He salutes. He rides south.
> **+2 SWORD, +1 ROSE, +1 CROWN.** No loot. The honour of the draw.

> **IF YOU WIN — THE YIELD**
>
> Ser Hadrian kneels. The kneeling costs him — the left knee makes a sound that is not a sound a knee should make — and he places Dawnstrike flat on the ground before you. Then he begins, with slow and painful dignity, to unbuckle his half-plate.
>
> 'It is yours,' he says. 'All of it. By right of arms, by the old forms, by the Measure.'
>
> He stands in his gambeson — suddenly smaller, suddenly his age, suddenly just an old man on a road. He looks at Dawnstrike on the ground and his expression is not loss. It is completion.
>
> 'I was afraid,' he says. 'Not of losing. Of no one being good enough to take them from me. Of riding south and dying alone and the sword being found by someone who did not know what it was. You know what it is.' He meets your eyes. 'Carry it for the people I could not save. That is all I ask.'
>
> **ITEMS GAINED:**
>
> > **✦ MAGIC ITEM GAINED: DAWNSTRIKE**
> > *Weapon (Greatsword), Rare (Requires Attunement)*
> > An ancient Solamnic greatsword, the blade inscribed with prayers to Paladine in a script that predates the Cataclysm. The crossguard is shaped like outstretched wings. The steel hums faintly when held — not vibration, resonance. It knows when it is being carried by someone worthy.
> > **Mechanics:** +1 Greatsword. 2d6+1+STR slashing, two-handed. Weapon Mastery: Graze (on miss, deal STR mod damage). Radiant Strike: 2/day, on hit add +1d6 radiant damage (free action, declare before damage roll). The blade hums faintly when pointed toward fiends or undead within 60 feet. Once per long rest: *Dawn's Light* — as a bonus action, Dawnstrike emits bright light in a 20-foot radius for 1 minute. Undead and fiends within the light have disadvantage on attack rolls. Once per long rest: *Last Stand* — when reduced to 0 HP, you may instead drop to 1 HP. Dawnstrike's light flares and goes dark until the next dawn.
> > **Lore:** Nine generations of the White Span lineage carried this blade. Ser Hadrian was the last. Now you are the first of whatever comes next.
>
> > **ARMOUR GAINED: SER HADRIAN'S HALF-PLATE**
> > *Armour (Half-Plate), Mundane*
> > AC 15 + DEX (max 2). Solamnic make, old but functional. The rose insignia on the breastplate is worn nearly invisible. The dents tell stories. Stealth disadvantage.
> > **Lore:** Forty-three years of service. Every dent has a name.
>
>
> Ser Hadrian stands in his gambeson, unarmed and lighter than he has been in forty-three years. He salutes one final time. He walks — not rides, walks — to his horse, mounts with difficulty, and turns south.
>
> 'I will find the Dragon Army,' he says. 'Without the sword, they will kill me quickly. That is a kindness I have been riding toward for six months.' He looks back. 'If the sword sings for you — and it will, I think — listen to it. It knows things the Measure forgot.'
>
> He rides south. You watch him until the road takes him. He does not look back. He does not need to. He has finished.
>
> **IF ALDRIC IS IN YOUR PARTY:** Aldric is silent for a very long time. Then: 'That was a knight.' Not a compliment. An epitaph.
>
> **+3 SWORD, +2 ROSE.** The honour is immense. The weight is heavier.
>
> **AFTER THE FIGHT — UPDATE YOUR SHEET**
> Record current HP. Record items gained or lost (BROKEN weapon, SHATTERED armour if defeated). Mark any used: Second Wind, Action Surge, spell slots, Lay on Hands pool.
> Equip new items if gained. Update AC accordingly.
> **Short rest available:** Recover Second Wind, Action Surge.
> **XP:** 50 XP (the duel itself). Bonus 25 XP if you won.

> **A) The road continues. Whatever just happened, Vogler is still ahead.** --> Scene 70A

---


## SCENE 70A — THE LAKESIDE SKIRMISH

*Lake Akh-Tiel — Eastern Shore, Pre-Dawn*

Sera finds it. She was scouting ahead — she always scouts ahead now, without being asked, because the road taught her that asking takes time nobody has — and she comes back to the column at a run that is trying very hard to look like it is not a run.

'Observation post,' she says. She is not out of breath because Sera Nighthollow does not get out of breath, but her eyes are wider than usual. 'Eastern lake shore. Four combatants: two soldiers, a scout with a longbow, and a war dog. They have line of sight to the bridge approach. If they signal, the bridge garrison gets reinforcements before we arrive.'

Caeron processes this in two seconds. 'Can we go around?'

'Not without them seeing the column.' Sera's jaw is set. 'We go through.'

This is not a rescue. There are no civilians. No moral complexity. This is a tactical problem with a tactical solution: neutralize the observation post before they can signal, or fight two extra soldiers at the bridge. The mathematics are simple. The execution is not.

> **COMBAT MODE**
> **Pen & Paper:** Use stat blocks below. Run the encounter at your table, then skip to **AFTER THE FIGHT**.
> **Narrative Mode:** Follow the rounds below. Roll when prompted.

> **COMPANION SELECTION**
> **Sera** — Essential. She knows the terrain. +2 to all Stealth rolls during approach.
> **Serath** — Knows Dragon Army signal protocols. Can identify and disable the signal system.
> **Aldric** — Assault. If stealth fails, Aldric is the one you want beside you.
> **Lysander** — Veteran precision. +2 to first attack. 'One chance. Make it count.'
> **Vael** — Tactical assessment. Reveals enemy positions before engagement.
>
> Choose up to 2 companions.

> **ENEMY STAT BLOCKS (Pen & Paper)**
> **Human Soldier (2):** AC 14 (chain shirt + shield), HP 16, Speed 30ft. Longsword +5 (1d8+3). Javelin +5 (1d6+3, 30/120). Formation: +1 AC when adjacent.
> **Dragon Army Scout:** AC 15 (studded leather + DEX), HP 22, Speed 30ft. Longbow +5 (1d8+3, 150/600). Shortsword +5 (1d6+3). Observant: advantage on Perception. **Signal Horn:** Action to blow — adds 2 soldiers to the bridge fight (Scene 70). If the scout is killed or the horn destroyed before it sounds, no reinforcements.
> **War Dog:** AC 12 (natural), HP 11, Speed 40ft. Bite +4 (1d6+2, DC 11 STR or knocked prone). Pack Tactics: advantage on attacks if ally is adjacent to target. **Can be calmed:** Animal Handling DC 13 — the dog stops fighting and sits. It is a dog. It was trained, not born, to this.

> **STEALTH APPROACH:** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15 (DC 13 if Sera present)
> **SUCCESS:** Surprise round. All enemies are unaware. You get one free round of attacks with advantage. The scout does not reach the horn.
> **FAILURE:** The war dog smells you. It barks. The scout reaches for the horn. You have 1 round to stop the signal.

> **SURVIVAL CHECK (optional, before approach):** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 14
> Approach downwind. The dog cannot smell you.
> **SUCCESS:** +2 to Stealth check. Dog does not detect you regardless of Stealth result (eliminates the dog-smells-you failure condition).
> **FAILURE:** The wind is wrong. Standard approach.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 1

The observation post is simple: a lean-to of branches against a rock outcropping, the kind of fieldcraft that is invisible from the road and obvious from ten feet away. The fire is cold — they are professionals, they know fires are visible — but the bedrolls are warm and the ration wrappers are fresh. They have been here at least two days. Watching. Counting. Reporting.

The scout is the problem. He is on the high ground — a shelf of rock above the lean-to — with the longbow and the signal horn at his belt. He has the eyes of a man who is paid to notice things, and his dog is curled at his feet, one ear up. Always one ear up.

**IF STEALTH SUCCEEDED:** They do not see you. The scout is looking south. The soldiers are dozing. The dog is asleep. This is the moment. Take it clean.

**IF STEALTH FAILED:** The dog is on its feet, teeth bared, and the bark has woken every one of them. The scout's hand is on the horn. One round. If he blows it, the bridge gets reinforcements.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Choose a target:**
> **Scout (priority — the horn)** / **Soldier (left)** / **Soldier (right)** / **War Dog**
>
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC (Scout: 15, Soldiers: 14, Dog: 12)
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus. (Advantage if stealth succeeded.)
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **IF STEALTH FAILED — RANGED ATTACK ON SCOUT (emergency):** If you have a ranged weapon or javelin, you can target the scout before he blows the horn. Ranged attack, DC 15. On hit, the horn falls. On miss, he blows it Round 2.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:**
> **Sera:** A) Scout Shot — targets the horn at the scout's belt (ranged attack, DC 15, destroys horn on hit) | B) Mark Scout (+2 next attack vs scout) | C) Aimed Shot (1d6+3 dmg, targets scout)
> **Serath:** A) Intel (+2 one attack) | B) Signal Sabotage — if she can reach the scout (Stealth DC 13), she disables the horn silently | C) Dagger Strike (1d4+2)
> **Aldric:** A) Flank (+1 next attack) | B) Shield Wall (+1 AC) | C) Charge — engages both soldiers (1d8+2, draws aggro, takes 1d4)
> **Lysander:** A) Combat Instruction (+2 attack) | B) Veteran Strike — single devastating blow (1d10+3) | C) Guard (takes next hit for you)
> **Vael:** A) Flanking Shot (1d6 dmg) | B) Honest Assessment (reveal all enemy HP) | C) Cover Fire (+1 AC)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):**
> • (Paladin) Cast Bless: +1d4 to attacks and saves for up to 3 targets, Concentration, lasts entire combat. 1 spell slot.
> • (Paladin) Divine Smite: Bonus action after hitting with a melee weapon. 2d8 radiant (+1d8 vs Fiends/Undead). Once per turn. 1 spell slot (or free 1/long rest at level 2+).
> • (Paladin) Lay on Hands: Bonus action.
> • (Fighter) Action Surge: Additional Action this round (except Magic). 1/short or long rest.
> • (Fighter) Second Wind: 1d10+[level] HP. Bonus action. 2 uses/long rest, regain 1/short rest.
> • (Any) Drink Potion of Healing: 2d4+2 HP. Bonus action.

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 1

**IF SCOUT HAS THE HORN AND STEALTH FAILED:**
The scout blows the horn. The sound carries across the lake — a flat, brassy note that bounces off the water and the far shore and the bridge you cannot yet see. Two additional soldiers will be waiting at Scene 70. The tactical cost is real.
**IF SCOUT DOES NOT HAVE THE HORN:** No signal. The bridge garrison remains unaware.

The soldiers engage. They are disciplined — shields up, formation tight, advancing together. The dog lunges low, going for your legs.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (soldier):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **SUCCESS:** Blocked.
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+3 slashing damage.
>
> **DEFENSE ROLL (war dog):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14 (Pack Tactics — advantage if soldier adjacent)
> **SUCCESS:** You kick the dog away. It snarls but retreats.
> **FAILURE:** 1d6+2 piercing damage. **STR save DC 11** or knocked prone (disadvantage on next attack).

> **ANIMAL HANDLING (optional, replaces attack next round):** Roll 1d20 + WIS modifier | DC 13
> Calm the dog. It is a dog. It was trained to fight but it was also trained to obey, and the voice you use matters.
> **SUCCESS:** The dog sits. Whines. It is done fighting. (+1 ROSE. The dog follows you. No combat benefit, but it is a dog and dogs are good.)
> **FAILURE:** The dog is too agitated. It attacks again next round.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 2

The observation post is chaos now — the lean-to is knocked over, the cold fire is scattered, and the scout is retreating up the rock shelf with the longbow. He is trying to create distance because the longbow is a 150-foot weapon and you are at 15 feet. From up there, he can pin you while the soldiers close.

The lake is behind everything. Silver in the pre-dawn. You are fighting on the shore of the most beautiful place you have ever seen and the beauty does not stop or slow anything.

> **YOUR ATTACK:**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage.
>
> **SCOUT LONGBOW SUPPRESSION:** If the scout is alive and on the high ground, all targets in the open take -1 to attack rolls (suppressing fire). Eliminate the scout to remove this penalty.

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 2

The scout fires from the high ground. The arrow comes fast and flat — a longbow shot at close range, which means it hits like a thrown spear.

> **DEFENSE ROLL (longbow):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 15
> **SUCCESS:** The arrow buries in the dirt beside you.
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+3 piercing damage.
>
> **Soldier attack (if alive):** Roll 1d20 + DEX modifier | DC 14
> **FAILURE:** 1d8+3 slashing damage.

---

### NARRATIVE COMBAT — ROUND 3

What remains is mathematics and will. The scout, if alive, is running out of arrows and running out of rock shelf. The soldiers, if alive, are considering the same calculation every soldier makes when the fight turns: is this worth dying for? The answer, for Dragon Army regulars this far from support, is usually no.

> **YOUR ATTACK — Clean up.**
> **ROLL REQUIRED:** Attack roll | DC = target's AC
> Roll 1d20 + your attack bonus.
> **ON HIT:** Roll damage. *End this before the sun comes up.*

> **COMPANION ACTION — Choose one for each companion:** (same options)

> **ABILITY / ITEM USE (choose one, optional):** (same options)

---

### ENEMY STRIKE — ROUND 3
