The intelligence is still there — it is always there, it is structural, it is the thing she was built from — but it is not being deployed. It is simply present, the way a fire is present: warm, lit, existing.

'I have decided to stay,' she says. 'Not as an observer.' She reaches into her jacket and pulls out her press credential — the folded paper that has been her identity, her access, her shield, and her excuse for as long as you have known her. She unfolds it. Looks at it. Folds it again with the precision of someone who is about to let go of something load-bearing.

She puts it in your hand.

'I do not need this anymore,' she says. 'I know what I am observing. I have known for — longer than I admitted, which is unusual for me, because I admit things quickly as a rule. I am observant. I observe. I observe you, specifically, with an attention that crossed the line from professional to personal approximately—' She stops. Recalculates. 'No. I am not going to put a date on it. I am going to do the unprecedented thing and allow a feeling to exist without timestamping it.'

The credential is in your hand. It is lighter than you expected. It is the weight of a career and an identity and a way of being in the world, and she has given it to you the way she gives everything: as information, as evidence, as the data point that completes a thesis she has been building since the first time she looked at you and saw not a story but a person.

'I love you,' she says. She says it like she is testing a hypothesis — carefully, with the awareness that the data may not support the conclusion. 'I love you the way I love an argument: completely, with my full attention, and with the knowledge that the conclusion may change. But I do not think it will change. The data is — comprehensive.'

Below you, Vogler. The closed notebook between you. The credential in your hand. Tariel Duskmantle, for the first time in your experience, is not observing. She is being observed. And she is allowing it.

'Ask me something,' she says. 'Something you want to know. Not about the Dragon Army or the political situation or the Knights of Solamnia. Something about me. I have never given anyone this kind of access before. I may not give it again. But tonight—' She gestures at the dark, the village, the smoke in the south. 'Tonight I would like to be the person someone asks about. Not the person who asks.'

*In the main campaign, Tariel Duskmantle is a political advisor with no rank, no oath, and the most accurate assessment of power in any room she enters. Her credential stays in your possession — a private symbol of the thing she surrendered to be here. She loves you with intelligence, with attention, with the focused intensity of a mind that has finally found something more interesting than observing: participating.*


## SCENE 80 — LYSANDER GRAVES: THE SWORD AND THE SCAR

*Vogler — The Gate, Night*

He is not at the ceremony. He is at the gate, facing south, sitting on the low wall with his sword across his knees. The sword is clean. He has cleaned it the way he does everything — thoroughly, without ceremony, with the competence of a man who has been taking care of weapons for longer than some of the squires have been alive.

You sit on the wall beside him. He does not startle. He knew you were coming. Lysander Graves always knows when someone is approaching — it is the survival instinct of a man who has slept in bad places and learned that awareness is the difference between waking up and not.

'You took the Oath,' he says. Not a question.

'I took the Oath.'

'Good.' He runs a cloth along the blade. The sword catches moonlight. 'I did not. In case that was unclear.'

'It was clear.'

A silence. The gate frames the southern road — the road you came up, the road the Dragon Army will come down. In the moonlight it is a pale line between dark trees, and at the end of it, very far away, the smear of smoke that means tomorrow.

'I want to show you something,' he says. He sets the sword down. Rolls up his left sleeve. In the moonlight, the scar is visible — the one that runs from wrist to elbow, a clean line, too straight and too deliberate to be combat. You have seen it before, in pieces, in moments when his sleeve rode up. You have never seen him show it.

'Twelve years ago,' he says. 'I was twenty. A knight of the Sword — did you know that? I was Solamnic. Ranked. Oathed. The whole thing.' He traces the scar with one finger. 'I was stationed at a border fort with forty soldiers and an order to hold against a bandit army that outnumbered us eight to one. The order came from a commander who knew the arithmetic and sent us anyway because holding the fort for three days would buy time for a retreat he did not have the courage to order without cover.'

He rolls the sleeve down. 'We held for two days. Twenty-eight soldiers died. I requested withdrawal. The request was denied. I withdrew anyway. Saved twelve people. The commander court-martialled me for disobeying a direct order. The Order stripped my rank. The scar is—' He pauses. 'The scar is what happened the night I understood that the institution I gave everything to did not value my judgment. Or my people. Or me.'

He picks up the sword. Holds it. The grip is the grip of a man who has been holding swords for two decades and has decided, after everything, that the sword is still worth holding even if the institution that gave it to him was not.

'I do not trust the Order,' he says. 'I do not trust oaths. I do not trust institutions. I trust—' He stops. Looks at you. In the moonlight, Lysander Graves's face is the face of a man who has spent twelve years being alone and is standing at the edge of a decision that terrifies him more than any battle ever has. 'I trust you. Specifically. Not the tabard. Not the rank. You. The person who sat with me on a wall when they could have been sleeping and did not ask about the scar until I showed it.'

He stands. Slides the sword into its sheath. Offers you his hand — the scarred one, the left one, the one that carries twelve years of survival and bitterness and the slow, painful learning that loneliness is not the same as safety.

'I will be at the wall tomorrow,' he says. 'Whatever they need me to be. Sword for hire. No title, no Oath, no complications.' He looks at you, and the loneliness in his face is not gone — it has been there too long to disappear in a single night — but it is thinner. It has a crack in it, and the crack is shaped like you. 'Except one complication.'

His hand is warm. His grip is steady. The scar is under your fingers and it is the topography of a man who broke and kept going and is standing here, at a gate, at the edge of a war, choosing to be something other than alone for the first time in twelve years.

'Do not die tomorrow,' he says. 'That is not a request. That is the only order I am ever going to give.'

*In the main campaign, Lysander Graves is an unaffiliated fighter with no rank, no oath, and the best sword arm in Vogler. He is the most dangerous kind of complication: a good man without a system, in love with someone inside one. His quest line involves the commander who sent forty soldiers to die and the twelve years of consequences that followed. He loves you with the desperate precision of a man who has finally found something worth losing, and is terrified, and stays anyway.*

# THE BRIDGE TO THE CAMPAIGN

| What You Carry Forward | Details |
|---|---|
| Your Class | Fighter or Paladin. Both Level 3. Bring your full character sheet. |
| Your Order | Determines social standing with Solamnic NPCs and Caeron's attitude. |
| Sacred Oath / Archetype | Paladin: god and Oath active. Fighter: Archetype features active. |
| Active Companions | Any companion at Flame or Oath level joins the main campaign party. |
| Romance Status | Oath-level romances have dedicated scenes in Chapters 1-3. |
| Serath (if kept) | Dragon Army intelligence at key points — but creates political tension. |
| Refugees saved | May reappear in Vogler or Kalaman with information or aid. |
| The Dispatch Pouch | If kept: Caeron can use it to delay the Dragon Army by six hours. |
| Paladin: God Relationship | Your deity is active. Divine signs continue. |
| Corruption Track 1 | STEADFAST through FALLEN. Affects institution-related checks. |
| Corruption Track 2 | STEADFAST through FALLEN. Affects institution-related checks. |
| The Hollow Crown (if active) | Disadvantage on Order authority Persuasion. FALLEN: also Advantage on individual appeals. |
| The Broken Sword (if active) | Disadvantage on institutional defence Persuasion. FALLEN: also Advantage on civilian defence attacks. |
| Diplomatic Observer (if staying) | Political advisor, intelligence asset, no rank. |
| Disgraced Knight (if riding to Vogler) | Unaffiliated fighter. Best sword arm available. |
| Combat XP | Total your XP. 5 fights available. 120 XP max. |

# CORRUPTION MODIFIER REFERENCE

## THE HOLLOW CROWN

**CONVINCED (reduced):** Disadvantage on Persuasion when invoking Order authority. Fixable through main campaign story.

**FALLEN (full):** Disadvantage on Order authority Persuasion. Advantage on individual appeals. Permanent unless resolved through main campaign quest.

## THE BROKEN SWORD

**CONVINCED (reduced):** Disadvantage on Persuasion when defending institutional decisions. Fixable through story.

**FALLEN (full):** Disadvantage on institutional defence Persuasion. Advantage on civilian defence attack rolls. Permanent unless resolved through quest.

## INTERACTIONS

**Both FALLEN:** Both modifiers full strength. Hardest character — sees both sides of every argument.

**SHAKEN+ corruption + LISTENING+ DG:** All DG saves at Disadvantage.

**FALLEN corruption + FALLEN DG:** Darkest Paladin outcome. Recovery requires two separate quests.

**STEADFAST corruption + HELD FIRM DG:** Strongest character. Advantage on charm/compulsion/fear saves for remainder of prelude and first chapter of main campaign.

**FALLEN corruption + Keeper Measure (Fighter):** Most sophisticated fall. You understand the Measure deeply AND believe it is insufficient. Aldous will recognise this.

The Dragon Queen's armies are marching.

The gods are waking.

Ride on, Squire.
